The Analogy of Extra Limbs and Multiple Proofs
The author compares sending prophets to creating two eyes and multiple proofs, showing it is perfection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses analogies from creation to argue that sending prophets is an act of divine perfection and favor, not foolishness, even if reason alone could suffice.

Core Idea
Extra proofs are not redundancy; they are divine perfection.

The author deepens the defense against the objection that sending prophets is unnecessary. He draws on two analogies: the human body has two eyes and ears when one would suffice, and Allah has placed multiple rational proofs for His existence. These are seen as perfection, not foolishness. This passage shows how the same logic applies to prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the repetition of 'لم يعد ذلك سفهًا'.
2
Identify the two analogies
Find the two examples the author gives: the body parts (two eyes/two ears) and the multiple rational proofs. Notice how each is introduced with 'وكذا'.
3
Understand the conclusion
The author applies the same reasoning to the sending of prophets. Ask yourself: why does he say it is not foolishness but a favor?
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولئن كان بدون ذلك كفاية. لم يعد ذلك سفهًا بل عد إنعامًا وإفضالا وكذا الله تعالى خلق للخلق عينين وأذنين، وكذا كل ذي عدد في الجسم، وإن كانت الحاجة تندفع والمقصود يحصل بواحد ولم يعد ذلك سفهًا بل عد تماما، وكذا الله تعالى لم يكتف بإقامة دليل واحد عقلي على ثبوته وتوحيده، بل جعل في كل مما خلق وذرأ آية لذلك ولم يعد سفها فكذا فيما نحن فيه لم يكن إرسال الرسل سفهًا وإن كان في العقل عنه غنية وكفاية، بل يعد إنعامًا وإفضالاً.
And if without that there is sufficiency, that is not considered foolishness, rather it is counted as favor and beneficence. Similarly, Allah created for creation two eyes and two ears, and likewise everything that is paired in the body, even if need is met and the purpose is attained with one, and that is not considered foolishness, rather it is counted as perfection. Similarly, Allah did not suffice with establishing a single rational proof for His existence and oneness, but He made in everything He created and scattered a sign for that, and it is not considered foolishness. So likewise in our matter, sending messengers was not foolishness even if reason had about it sufficiency and adequacy, rather it is counted as favor and beneficence.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage uses analogies to reinforce that extra provision is not foolish. Even if one eye sufficed, the creation of two is perfection. Similarly, multiple rational proofs for God's existence show that adding more is not absurd. Thus, sending prophets, even if reason alone could guide, is an extra favor and perfection.

Key Terms
عينان
أذنان
دليل
تمام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Adding extra proofs or messengers is redundant and therefore foolish.
Correction: The author argues that such additions are not foolish but are signs of divine perfection and generosity.

Checkpoint
What does the author compare sending prophets to?
A) Creating unnecessary things.
B) Creating two eyes instead of one.
C) Creating many stars.
D) Creating water.

Key Takeaway
The sending of prophets, like multiple limbs and proofs, is an act of divine generosity and perfection, not foolishness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have been given many repeated reminders of the truth—through nature, prophets, and scripture. Have you ever complained about hearing the same message again, instead of realizing it is a gift from a God who desires your guidance? Will you today treat that repetition as a loving sign rather than an annoyance?
?
Consider your own two eyes: you could see with one, yet you have two. Does that extra capacity stir gratitude in you? How often do you use your faculties to recognize the signs of Allah around you? What might your lack of reflection say about your response to His boundless favors?
?
If sending prophets were an act of favor even when reason could suffice, then what is your response to the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and his message? Will you receive it as a burden or a gift? What change in your daily life would show that you truly see it as divine beneficence and not just information?

Refutation of Denying God's Power to Change Natures
Nasafi refutes denying God's power to change natures using natural philosophers' own premises.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that natural philosophers' own admission that substances can change (e.g., fire to water) undermines their denial of God's power to change natures.

Core Idea
If natural philosophers admit fire can become water, why deny God can change natures?

Nasafi presents a sharp refutation of those who deny that God can change the inherent natures of things. He argues that this denial leads to ta'til (negation of attributes) and is inconsistent with the premises of natural philosophers themselves. In this passage, he uses their own example of fire turning into water to expose their contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Pay attention to the structure: first a claim, then supporting evidence from natural philosophers, then a rhetorical conclusion.
2
Identify the key claim
Note that Nasafi states that denying the change of natures results from ta'til. This is the main thesis he is defending.
3
Examine the supporting evidence
He cites the consensus of natural philosophers that all substances are one genus and differ by accidents, and that fire can turn into water by change of qualities. Understand why this example is powerful: it shows that even naturalists admit substantial transformation.
4
Analyze the rhetorical conclusion
Nasafi then asks rhetorically: if this is so, how can one deny God's power to change natures? He attributes such denial to impudence and foolishness. Reflect on the logical force of this argument.
5
Consider the broader implication
Think about how this argument protects God's complete power and refutes atheistic positions. This passage is a model of using opponents' premises against them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا كان إنكار قلب الطبائع نتيجة القول بالتعطيل، وفيما سبق قيل: هذا من الدلائل على إثبات القدرة الكاملة لله تعالى ما يوجب بطلان قول هؤلاء الملحدين. والذي يؤيد بطلان هذه الشبهة: أن من قول جميع الطبيعيين أو الجمهور الأعظم منهم أن جواهر العالم كلها جنس واحد واختلافها بما يوجد فيها من الأعراض، وأن جوهر النار (قد ينقلب ماء) لتبدل كيفيتي الحرارة واليبوسة بالبرودة والرطوبة. وإذا كان الأمر كذلك كيف ينكر جواز قلب الطبائع ويخرج من مقدور الله تعالى لولا الوقاحة والحماقة.
Since the denial of changing the natures results from the saying of ta'til (negation of attributes), and in what preceded it was said: this is among the evidences for the establishment of the complete power of God Almighty which necessitates the invalidity of the saying of these atheists. And what supports the invalidity of this doubt is: that it is from the saying of all the natural philosophers or the vast majority of them that the substances of the world are all one genus and their difference is by what occurs in them of accidents, and that the substance of fire may turn into water due to the change of the qualities of heat and dryness into cold and moisture. And if the matter is thus, how can one deny the possibility of changing the natures and exclude it from the power of God Almighty, were it not for impudence and foolishness.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a proof against those who deny God's power to change the inherent natures of things, a position that leads to ta'til (negation of God's attributes). Nasafi first states that such denial results from ta'til. He then presents an argument from the common position of natural philosophers: they hold that all material substances are essentially one genus, and differences arise from accidents. For example, fire's substance can turn into water if its qualities of heat and dryness are replaced by cold and moisture. If natural philosophers themselves admit that substances can change their qualities and even transform, then it is contradictory for them to deny that God can change natures. Nasafi concludes that such denial is only due to impudence and foolishness. The argument uses the opponents' own premises to refute them.

Key Terms
قلب الطبائع
التعطيل
القدرة الكاملة
الطبيعيين
جواهر العالم
الأعراض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Denying that God can change natures is a rational position based on the stability of natural laws.
Correction: Nasafi shows that even natural philosophers admit that substances can change (e.g., fire to water), so it is irrational to deny God's power to do so; such denial stems from impudence, not reason.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what do natural philosophers admit that undermines their denial of God's power to change natures?
A) They admit that substances are composed of atoms.
B) They admit that all substances are one genus and differ by accidents, and that fire can turn into water.
C) They admit that miracles are impossible.
D) They admit that God does not intervene in nature.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi refutes the denial of God's power to change natures by showing it contradicts natural philosophers' own admission that substances can transform.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself thinking that some situation is 'beyond God's ability' to change or resolve? What does this passage reveal about the hidden impudence of such a thought, and how can you actively train yourself to believe in His absolute power over all things, including the 'fixed' laws of nature?
?
When you see natural processes like fire burning or water boiling, do you truly attribute the change directly to God's ongoing power, or do you fall into the habit of seeing these as automatic, self-sufficient laws? How would your daily awareness of God change if you constantly reminded yourself that every transformation is an act of His creation?
?
This passage accuses those who deny God's power to change natures of 'foolishness.' In what areas of your life—spiritually, morally, or in your reliance on material means—might you be acting foolishly by limiting God's intervention? What concrete step can you take this week to rely more on His power than on secondary causes?

Poets' inability to match the Quran proves its inimitability
Nasafi argues that poets' inability to imitate the Quran proves its inimitability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses the empirical fact of poets' inability to match the Quran to establish its inimitability.

Core Idea
The best poets' failure to imitate the Quran proves it is beyond human capacity.

This lesson explores a key argument for the Quran's miraculous nature: if the most eloquent poets of the age could not produce anything like it, then no one can. Nasafi presents a rhetorical challenge that compels the reader to accept the Quran's uniqueness. Let's examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the rhetorical question posed by Nasafi to the poets of his time.
The passage addresses a hypothetical poet who claims the Quran could be matched.
2
Identify the two alternatives
Nasafi presents two possibilities: either the poets had the ability but chose inferior speech, or they were incapable. Determine which alternative is plausible.
The obvious answer is that they were incapable, given their high skill.
3
Connect to the conclusion
Understand how this argument leads to the conclusion that the Quran is inimitable (i'jaz) and that this is known by clear reason (badihah al-‘aql).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أهل عصرك كصريع الغواني ومروان بن أبي حفصة وأبي نواس وسلم الخاسر وأشجع السلمى وغيرهم في نهاية الجودة والبلاغة ورشاقة النظم وجزالة الألفاظ وإحكام الصنعة؟ ألأنك مع القدرة على مثل تلك القصائد البليغة الفصيحة المحكمة اخترت لنفسك الأدون والأرذل والأبشع؟ أم لأنك عجزت عن ذلك، ولم ينقد لطبعك البارد الثقيل مثل تلك القصائد؟ ولا يخفى على أحد أن ذلك كان لعجزه عن اختياره، وكذا ما ذكر يؤدي إلى ارتفاع التفاضل بين الشعراء والخطباء والبلغاء والفصحاء وانعدام الإفحام، وحيث كان التفاضل بين هؤلاء معلومًا وانقسام الناس إلى الشعراء المعلقين والمتبلدين المفحمين أمرًا ظاهرا دل أن ذلك كلام باطل يعرف بطلانه ببديهة العقل.
Your contemporaries such as Sari' al-Ghawani, Marwan ibn Abi Hafsah, Abu Nuwas, Salm al-Khasir, Ashja' al-Sulami and others are at the peak of quality, eloquence, graceful versification, dignity of words, and perfection of craftsmanship? Is it that while being able to produce such eloquent, fluent, and perfect poems, you chose for yourself the lower, inferior, and ugliest? Or is it that you were incapable of that, and your cold, heavy nature did not yield such poems? It is not hidden from anyone that this was due to his inability to choose it. Likewise, what was mentioned leads to the elimination of distinction between poets, orators, eloquent speakers, and fluent speakers, and the absence of incapacity. And since the distinction between these people is known, and the division of people into accomplished poets and dullard incapacitated is an evident matter, it indicates that this is false speech whose falsehood is known by the primary intuition of reason.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that the Quran could be matched but people chose not to. Nasafi argues by pointing to the most eloquent poets of the time: if anyone could produce similar speech, it would be them. Yet they did not produce the like of the Quran. He presents a rhetorical question: is it because they had the ability but chose something inferior, or because they were incapable? The obvious answer is that they were incapable, as their best works are far inferior. This leads to the conclusion that the Quran is unique and inimitable, a fact known by clear reason (badihah al-‘aql).

Key Terms
بديهة العقل
الإفحام
التفاضل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran's inimitability is merely a claim, not a fact.
Correction: This passage demonstrates that it is empirically evident: the best poets of the time were unable to produce the like, proving its inimitability.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the argument about the poets?
A) Poets were unable to produce the like of the Quran due to lack of effort.
B) The best poets were incapable of matching the Quran, proving it is inimitable.
C) The Quran is similar to the poets' works in eloquence.
D) The poets chose not to imitate the Quran out of respect.

Key Takeaway
The inability of the best poets to match the Quran proves its divine origin and inimitability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Looking at the finest poets of your time, they were silenced by the Quran. When you read the Quran, does it silence your pride? Or do you still feel you could match its words with your own? Spend a moment in prayer, asking Allah to grant you true humility before His speech.
?
The poets' failure proves their inability. What about you? Have you ever tried to improve your own speech or writing to match the Quran's beauty? If not, why? And if you have, did you not realize its transcendence? Let this question linger in your heart until you weep or submit.
?
Nasafi says the falsehood of the claim is known by 'badihah al-'aql' — primary intuition. Do you have that conviction? When the Quran is recited, does your intellect immediately recognize it as divine, or do you rationalize? Ask yourself: am I truly convinced, or only paying lip service?

Quranic Proofs for Creation and Creator
Al-Nasafi enumerates Quranic proofs for the world's createdness and the Creator's existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran uses logical arguments to demonstrate the createdness of the world and the existence of the Creator, particularly through verses that reason from change and from the impossibility of self-creation.

Core Idea
The Quran argues for God's existence by pointing to what cannot be divine.

The Quran is not only a book of guidance but also a book of rational arguments. Imam al-Nasafi highlights a profound layer of the Quran: it contains proofs that the world is created and that a Creator must exist. In this passage, he cites several verses that appeal to reason, such as Abraham's statement 'I do not like those that set' and questions like 'Were they created from nothing?' These verses form a logical case for tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Read the opening sentence: what does al-Nasafi say the Quran contains? Focus on the phrase 'dilalat hadath al-alam' and 'istihalat al-qawl bil-uluhiyya'. This sets the stage.
The claim is that the Quran contains proofs both for the world being created and for the impossibility of divinity for changing things.
2
Examine the first proof: argument from change
Look at the verse 'I do not like those that set' (6:76). How does this verse argue against worship of celestial bodies? Why does setting indicate change and therefore temporality?
This is the Abrahamic argument against astral worship.
3
Examine the second proof: argument from creation
Now consider the verses from Surah al-Dhariyat (51:20-21) and Surah al-Tur (52:35-36). What signs in the earth and yourselves point to a Creator? How do the rhetorical questions in 52:35-36 refute self-creation or creation from nothing?
These verses appeal to observable creation and logical necessity.
4
Reflect on the argument's structure
Notice that al-Nasafi combines two types of proofs: one from the impermanence of objects (change) and one from the dependence of existence (creation). How do these complement each other?
Together they form a cumulative case for tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووجه آخر من دلالات الكتاب ما تضمن من دلائل حدوث العالم استحالة القول بالألوهية من تعتري عليه الحوادث ويتعاقب عليه الأضداد المتباينة من نحو قوله: لا أُحِبُّ الأَفِلِينَ وقوله: وَفِي الْأَرْضِ آيَاتٌ لِلْمُوقِنِينَ وَفِي أَنْفُسِكُمْ أَفَلَا تُبْصِرُونَ ودلالة ثبوت الصانع من نحو قوله تعالى: أَمْ خُلِقُوا مِنْ غَيْرِ شَيْءٍ أَمْ هُمُ الْخَالِقُونَ أَمْ خَلَقُوا السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ وقوله: وَمِنْ آيَاتِهِ أَنْ خَلَقَكُمْ مِنْ
And another aspect of the indications of the Book is what it contains of proofs of the temporality of the world and the impossibility of attributing divinity to that which is subject to accidents and upon which contradictory opposites succeed each other, such as His saying: 'I do not like those that set' (6:76) and His saying: 'And in the earth are signs for the certain, and in yourselves, do you not see?' (51:20-21) and the proof of the existence of the Maker from His saying: 'Were they created from nothing, or are they the creators? Or did they create the heavens and the earth?' (52:35-36) and His saying: 'And among His signs is that He created you from...'
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage introduces another miraculous face of the Quran: it contains proofs of the createdness (hadath) of the world and the existence of the Creator. The author cites several verses: (1) 'I do not like those that set' (Quran 6:76) from the story of Abraham, which argues against worshipping things that undergo change; (2) verses from Surah al-Dhariyat (51:20-21) pointing to signs in the earth and in themselves; (3) verses from Surah al-Tur (52:35-36) arguing that they were not created from nothing nor are they creators themselves, and they did not create the heavens and earth. These verses provide rational arguments for the world's dependence on a Creator. The text cuts off at the beginning of another verse, so the argument is incomplete in this window.

Key Terms
حدوث العالم
دلائل
الصانع
الأَفِلِينَ
آيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Quran only contains commands and stories, not logical arguments.
Correction: The Quran contains rational proofs for foundational truths, as exemplified by these verses.

Checkpoint
Which verse is cited to argue against worshipping things that undergo change?
A) 'And in the earth are signs...'
B) 'I do not like those that set'
C) 'Were they created from nothing...'
D) 'And among His signs is that He created you...'

Key Takeaway
The Quran presents rational proofs for God's existence, such as the argument from change (things that change cannot be divine) and the argument from creation (the world could not have created itself).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see the sun set tonight, will you remember that it is a creature, not a creator? How can that moment become a worshipful reminder for you?
?
Your own body is a sign. What specific flaw or limitation in your body have you ignored that actually points to your need for a perfect Creator? How will you use that awareness today?
?
If someone asked you tomorrow, 'Why do you believe in God?', would you be able to give a clear reason from this passage? Write down one verse and commit to sharing it with one person this week.

The Argument from Change: Why Changing Things Cannot Be Gods
The author presents the Quranic argument from change against ascribing divinity to mutable things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Qur'an argues that anything subject to change cannot be divine, as demonstrated by the verse 'I do not love those that set.'

Core Idea
Change implies dependence; a true God must be beyond all change.

The Maturidi author presents a distinct Qur'anic argument: the very fact that things change—like celestial bodies setting—shows they cannot be gods. This lesson explores the first part of his evidence, focusing on the verse from Ibrahim (AS) and the call to reflect on signs within ourselves and the earth.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the source Arabic without analyzing it yet. Let the words and rhythm of the original sink in. It is a short but packed statement.
Notice the phrase 'لَا أُحِبُّ الْأَفِلِينَ' — it is a direct quote from the Quran (6:76).
2
Identify the core argument
The author states that the Book contains proofs of the temporality (hadath) of the world, which makes it impossible to claim divinity for anything that is subject to events and changing opposites.
The technical term 'الأضداد المتباينة' refers to contrasting states like light and darkness, life and death.
3
Examine the cited verse
The first verse is the statement of Prophet Ibrahim: 'I do not love those that set.' This applies to the celestial bodies that set and thus change—they cannot be gods because a god must be eternal and unchanging.
The second verse, 'وَفِي الْأَرْضِ آيَاتٌ لِلْمُوقِنِينَ وَفِي أَنفُسِكُمْ أَفَلَا تُبْصِرُونَ' (51:20-21), directs attention to signs in creation and within ourselves.
4
Reflect on the broader significance
This argument refutes not only ancient polytheism but any claim that a changeable being (like a prophet or angel) could be divine. It establishes a key criterion for divinity: immutability.
This point connects to the later discussion on divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووجه آخر من دلالات الكتاب ما تضمن من دلائل حدوث العالم استحالة القول بالألوهية من تعتري عليه الحوادث ويتعاقب عليه الأضداد المتباينة من نحو قوله: لَا أُحِبُّ الْأَفِلِينَ وقوله: وَفِي الْأَرْضِ آيَاتٌ لِلْمُوقِنِينَ وَفِي أَنفُسِكُمْ أَفَلَا تُبْصِرُونَ ودلالة ثبوت الصانع من نحو قوله تعالى: أَمْ خُلِقُوا مِنْ غَيْرِ شَيْءٍ أَمْ هُمُ الْخَالِقُونَ أَمْ خَلَقُوا السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ وقوله: وَمِنْ آيَاتِهِ أَنْ خَلَقَكُم مِّن تُرَابٍ ثُمَّ إِذَا أَنتُم بَشَرٌ تَنتَشِرُونَ وقوله: وَمِنْ آيَاتِهِ أَن يُرْسِلَ الرِّيَاحَ مُبَشِّرَاتٍ وقوله: إِنَّ فِي خَلْقِ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَاخْتِلَافِ الَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ وَالْفُلْكِ الَّتِي تَجْرِي فِي الْبَحْرِ بِمَا يَنفَعُ النَّاسَ وَمَا أَنزَلَ اللَّهُ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مِن مَّاءٍ فَأَحْيَا بِهِ الْأَرْضَ بَعْدَ مَوْتِهَا وَبَثَّ فِيهَا مِن كُلِّ دَابَّةٍ وَتَصْرِيفِ الرِّيَاحِ وَالسَّحَابِ الْمُسَخَّرِ بَيْنَ السَّمَاءِ وَالْأَرْضِ لَآيَاتٍ لِقَوْمٍ يَعْقِلُونَ في آيات كثيرة يطول حصرها وإحصاؤها حرض فيها على التأمل والتفكر، ونبه عن المعنى الموجب أن يكون لهذه المحدثات صانع
And another aspect of the evidences of the Book is what it includes of proofs of the temporality of the world, [showing] the impossibility of the claim of divinity for that which is subject to events and upon which contrasting opposites follow, such as His saying: 'I do not love those that set' and His saying: 'And in the earth are signs for the certain, and in yourselves, do you not see?' And evidence for the existence of the Maker from His saying: 'Were they created from nothing or are they the creators? Or did they create the heavens and the earth?' and His saying: 'And of His signs is that He created you from dust, then behold you are humans spreading out' and His saying: 'And of His signs is that He sends the winds as bringers of glad tidings' and His saying: 'Indeed in the creation of the heavens and the earth, and the alternation of night and day, and the ships that sail in the sea with what benefits people, and what Allah sends down from the sky of water, then He revives the earth after its death, and He spreads in it every kind of creature, and the directing of the winds and the clouds subservient between the sky and the earth, are signs for a people who reason' in many verses whose enumeration and counting would be lengthy, in which He incited to reflection and contemplation, and He alerted to the meaning that necessitates that these contingent things have a Maker.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage presents another category of Qur'anic evidences: arguments for the temporality (hadath) of the world and the impossibility of attributing divinity to anything that changes. The author begins by citing verses that demonstrate that things subject to events and opposites (like the celestial bodies that set) cannot be gods—hence the Prophet's statement 'I do not love those that set.' Then he gives verses that prove the existence of a Creator (thubut al-sani'), such as the verse asking whether humans were created from nothing or they created themselves, and the verses describing various signs in creation. The author notes that many such verses exist, all calling for contemplation and affirming that contingent things must have a Maker. This is a proof from the order and design in the universe.

Key Terms
حدوث العالم (temporality of the world)
استحالة الألوهية (impossibility of divinity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that powerful natural objects like the sun or moon could be gods because they are great and beneficial.
Correction: The Quran refutes this by pointing out their change: they set, they follow cycles, so they are not eternal or self-sufficient. A true God must be beyond all change.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse does the author cite to show that changeable things cannot be gods?
A) 'Were they created from nothing or are they the creators?'
B) 'I do not love those that set'
C) 'And of His signs is that He created you from dust'
D) 'Indeed in the creation of the heavens and the earth...'

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an uses the fact of change—like celestial bodies setting—to prove that such things cannot be gods, establishing immutability as a necessary quality of divinity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What 'setting stars' – things that fade or change – have you mistakenly placed your trust in as if they were permanent? How does this lesson challenge you to redirect your ultimate reliance to the Eternal alone?
?
Prophet Ibrahim (AS) rejected the stars because they set. When you look at your own life – your health, wealth, relationships – do you see them as temporary signs pointing to the Creator, or do you treat them as ultimate securities? What will you do today to remind yourself of their contingency?
?
If change is proof of dependence, what does your own rapidly changing state (moods, circumstances, age) teach you about your need for a Creator who does not change? How does this truth humble you and drive you to worship?

The Argument from Creation and Design: Contingent Existence Requires a Maker
The author presents Quranic verses as evidence for the existence of a Creator, citing multiple verses about creation and design.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'an uses verses about creation, design, and order to demonstrate the existence of a Creator.

Core Idea
The intricate order of the universe points to a wise Creator.

After refuting the divinity of changeable things, the author turns to positive evidence for the existence of a Maker. The Qur'an abounds with verses that call us to reflect on creation—from the origin of humans to the cycles of nature. This lesson examines these evidences and how they lead to the conclusion that contingent things must have a Maker.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage for this lesson
Read the Arabic text that begins with 'ودلالة ثبوت الصانع' and continues to the end. Try to catch the flow from one verse to the next.
The passage lists several verses that are all arguments for the existence of a Creator.
2
Identify the key question posed
The first verse 'أَمْ خُلِقُوا مِنْ غَيْرِ شَيْءٍ أَمْ هُمُ الْخَالِقُونَ' (52:35) presents a logical dilemma: either humans were created from nothing (no creator) or they created themselves. Both are impossible, so there must be a Creator.
This is a classic argument from contingency.
3
Examine the verses about creation
The author then cites verses about creation from dust, sending winds, and the vast systems of the universe. Each points to design and purpose, demanding a wise Maker.
The last verse cited (2:164) is a comprehensive list of signs in nature.
4
Understand the conclusion
The author notes that these verses 'incite to reflection and contemplation' and 'alert to the meaning that necessitates that these contingent things have a Maker.' The conclusion is that the universe's order is inexplicable without an intelligent Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
You did not create yourself, and you certainly were not created from nothing. If you know that a Maker brought you into existence, why do you sometimes live as if your life is your own, ignoring the One who gave it to you?
?
The Qur'an challenges you to reflect on these signs. What is stopping you from that reflection? Are you willing to set aside distractions today and spend five minutes truly contemplating one of these signs, allowing it to deepen your conviction in Allah?

The Qur'anic Argument from Initial Creation to Resurrection
Proving resurrection via the argument from initial creation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'an argues for the possibility of resurrection by pointing to the greater miracle of initial creation.

Core Idea
The one who created from nothing can certainly recreate.

This passage presents a powerful Qur'anic argument for resurrection (al-baʿth). The author explains that God's initial creation of humans from nothing is a far greater feat than resurrecting them, so denying resurrection is logically inconsistent. He cites the verse from Surah Ya-Sin where a man denies resurrection while forgetting his own creation, and marvels at the subtlety of this argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the author's emphasis on the subtlety of the argument.
The verse referred to is Surah Ya-Sin 36:78.
2
Identify the core argument
The author states that affirming power over the more difficult (initial creation) proves power over the easier (resurrection). Understand this analogy.
This is a classic kalam argument: al-bad' (beginning) as proof for al-i'ada (return).
3
Reflect on the Qur'anic verse
The verse 'And he struck for Us a parable and forgot his own creation' reminds the denier that he himself was created ex nihilo. Consider how this silences doubt.
The denier's own existence is the counter-evidence to his denial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودلالة إثبات البعث وإثبات الاستدلال بالبدء على الإعادة، وبيان إثبات القدرة على ما هو الأصعب في تقدير عقولنا على ما هو الأهون فيه، ولو لم يكن في ذلك إلا قوله: وَضَرَبَ لَنَا مَثَلًا وَنَسِيَ خَلْقَهُ إلى آخره.. لكان حقيقاً أن يتعجب العاقل منه بل يتحير ويبهت من لطف تلك المحاجة واستمالها على إبطال جميع ما يتخالج فيه عن الشبه ووجوهها.
And evidence for the affirmation of resurrection and the affirmation of using the beginning as evidence for the return, and a clarification of affirming power over what is more difficult in the estimation of our intellects over what is easier in it. And if there were nothing in that except His saying: 'And he struck for Us a parable and forgot his own creation' to the end of it, it would be fitting for the intelligent person to marvel at it, nay, to be bewildered and stunned at the subtlety of that argument and its swaying in refuting all that enters into it of doubts and their aspects.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage presents evidence for resurrection (ba'th) and the method of arguing from the initial creation (al-bad') to the return (al-i'ada). The author explains that the Qur'an demonstrates God's power to do what seems more difficult (initial creation) to prove He can do what seems easier (resurrection). He then cites the verse from Surah Ya-Sin (36:78) where a person denies resurrection and forgets his own creation. The author praises the subtlety of this argument, saying it would amaze any intelligent person and refutes all doubts. This is a favorite kalam argument: the one who created ex nihilo can certainly recreate.

Key Terms
إثبات البعث (affirmation of resurrection)
الاستدلال بالبدء على الإعادة (arguing from beginning to return)
المحاجة (argumentation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Resurrection is impossible because dead bodies cannot be reconstituted.
Correction: The Qur'an argues that initial creation from nothing is a far greater miracle, so resurrection is easier by comparison and thus rationally possible.

Checkpoint
How does the Qur'an refute the one who denies resurrection, according to this passage?
A) By citing a verse about the creation of the heavens
B) By reminding him of his own creation
C) By mentioning the resurrection of past nations
D) By proving that God is all-powerful

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an uses the argument from initial creation (al-bad') to prove the return (al-i'ada), reminding the denier that he himself was created.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that the One who created you from nothing can recreate you after death, how would your priorities change today? What are you holding onto that you think God cannot revive?
?
You have forgotten your own creation — your own beginning from a drop. In what specific area of your life have you forgotten that God's power is greater than your difficulty?
?
The denier in the parable forgot his own creation while arguing against resurrection. Where in your own heart do you resist the reality of your own mortality and accountability?

The Quranic Argument from Initial Creation for Resurrection
Nasafi presents the Quranic refutation using the harder/easier comparison.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran refutes the denial of resurrection by using the principle that initial creation from nothing is harder than re-creation, making resurrection rationally possible.

Core Idea
Initial creation is harder; resurrection is easier and thus possible.

Imam Nasafi begins explaining the Quranic response to those who deny resurrection. The first argument draws attention to the fact that God created everything from nothing initially, which is a greater feat than bringing back what already existed. This establishes that resurrection is not impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
2
Identify the Quranic verse
Notice the verse quoted: 'Who will give life to bones when they are decayed?' and how the author explains the forgetting of first creation.
3
Understand the logical comparison
The key is that initial creation is harder, so re-creation is easier. Grasp why this makes resurrection not impossible.
This is the core reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن الله تعالى كما أخبر عن مقالة المنكر للبعث على الإجمال عقبه قبل إعادة التفسير ما يوجب كونه في حيز الممكنات، ثم أعاد ذكر المقالة وبيان إمكان البعث على طريق التفسير والإيضاح فقال تعالى: (وَضَرَبَ لَنَا مَثَلًا وَنَسِيَ خَلْقَهُ) تقديره: خلقه أولاً، والله أعلم، وضرب لنا مثلاً بقوله: (مَنْ يُحْيِ الْعِظَامَ وَهِيَ رَمِيمٌ) ونسي خلقه أن الله تعالى أنشأ أول مرة لا عن أصل والبداية في تقدير عقولنا أصعب من الإعادة، فعين بذلك أن ذلك ليس من جملة المستحيلات الممتنعات لأن ما هو أصعب في تقدير عقولكم كان ممكنا وتثبت قدرة الله بما عليه قدر ابتداء لأولى في تقدير عقولكم ثم بقوله تعالى: (وَهُوَ بِكُلِّ خَلْقٍ عَلِيمٌ) بين أن الإعادة وإن كان فعلاً محكماً لا تتأتى إلا من عالم فالله تعالى عالم بعلم يحيط بالمعلومات أجمع، ثم بقوله: (الَّذِي جَعَلَ لَكُم مِّنَ الشَّجَرِ الْأَخْضَرِ نَارًا) بين كمال قدرته وعجيب تدبيره أنه جعل من الشجر الأخضر الذي رويت أصوله وفروعه وغصونه من الماء إذ جعل من الأخضر بدون الماء نارا مع تضاد في كيفيتهما، إذ الماء بارد رطب والنار حارة يابسة، ولم يصعب عليه ذلك لكمال قدرته ونفاذ مشيئته وصائب تدبيره ولطف تقديره، وأعلم أن من له هذه القدرة والمشيئة وهذا التدبير والتقدير لا يبعد عنه إيجاد الحياة في العظام الرميمة والأجساد البالية، إذ ليس فيها ما يضاد الحياة، ولو كان فيها ذلك لكان قادرا على إعدام المضاد وإيجاد الحياة وذلك أقرب في تقدير عقولنا من جعل النار من الشجر الأخضر مع بقاء خضرته ووجود ما فيه من الماء، ثم أشار بقوله: (أَوَلَيْسَ الَّذِي خَلَقَ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ)
Then God Almighty, as He informed of the statement of the denier of resurrection in summary, followed it before repeating the explanation with what necessitated its being within the realm of possibilities, then He repeated the statement and the explanation of the possibility of resurrection by way of interpretation and clarification, and said: "And he strikes for Us an example and forgets his creation" meaning his first creation, and Allah knows best. And he strikes for us an example by his saying: "Who will give life to bones when they are decayed?" And he forgot his creation that God Almighty originated first time without an origin, and the beginning in the estimation of our minds is harder than the return, so He specified by that that it is not among the impossible things, because what is harder in the estimation of your minds was possible, and the power of God is established by the fact that He had power over the beginning, which is more fitting in the estimation of your minds. Then by His saying: "And He is of all creation Knowing," He made clear that the return, even if it is a precise act, cannot be accomplished except by a knower, so God is Knowing with a knowledge that encompasses all known things. Then by His saying: "He who made for you from the green tree fire," He made clear the perfection of His power and wonderful management, that He made from the green tree whose roots, branches, and twigs were watered from water, fire without water, despite the opposition in their qualities, since water is cold and wet and fire is hot and dry, and that was not difficult for Him due to the perfection of His power, the penetration of His will, the correctness of His management, and the subtlety of His determination. And He taught that whoever has this power, will, management, and determination, it is not unlikely that He brings life into decayed bones and worn-out bodies, because there is nothing in them that opposes life, and if there were such, He would be able to remove the opposition and bring life, and that is closer in the estimation of our minds than making fire from green tree while preserving its greenness and the presence of water in it. Then He pointed by His saying: "Is not He who created the heavens and the earth..."
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the possibility of resurrection, expounding how the Quran refutes the denier. The author follows the Quranic argument step by step. First, God mentions the denier's objection and then shows that resurrection is possible because initial creation (from nothing) is harder than re-creation, so if the harder is possible, the easier is even more so. Second, God's knowledge is perfect, so the precise act of re-creation is no problem. Third, the example of fire from green tree demonstrates God's power over opposites, making life after death easy by comparison. Finally, the argument from the creation of the heavens and earth (implied completion: 'Is not He who created the heavens and the earth able to give life to the dead?') drives the conclusion home. The author explains each Quranic verse in sequence, showing how it supports the logical possibility of resurrection.

Key Terms
بعث
إعادة
ممكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think resurrection is inherently impossible.
Correction: The Quran proves its possibility by pointing out that initial creation, which is more difficult, has already occurred, so re-creation is even more possible.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is resurrection not impossible?
A) Because God is powerful
B) Because initial creation is harder
C) Because the denier was wrong
D) Because bones can regenerate

Key Takeaway
The Quran refutes denial of resurrection by comparing it to the harder initial creation, thus establishing its possibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe in resurrection, but do you live with its certainty? What would change in your daily choices if you truly knew that the same God who made you from nothing will raise you from decay? Commit to one specific action today that reflects this certainty.
?
The denier forgot his own creation. When do you forget that God created you from nothing—perhaps in moments of pride or despair? How can you remind yourself daily of your origin and dependence on Him? Write a short prayer for this.
?
If resurrection is easier than initial creation, what does that say about God's ability to revive your dead heart, your broken faith, or your stagnant worship? What area of your spiritual life needs resurrection, and will you ask Him for it today?

The Quranic Arguments from God's Knowledge and the Fire Example
Nasafi expounds God's knowledge and the miraculous fire example as further proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran uses God's all-encompassing knowledge and the example of creating fire from green tree to demonstrate the possibility of resurrection.

Core Idea
God's knowledge and power over opposites make resurrection easy.

Imam Nasafi continues the Quranic refutation by presenting two more arguments: first, God's perfect knowledge ensures He can precisely re-create; second, the example of bringing fire from a green tree shows His power over opposites, making life after death even more plausible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to see the structure of two arguments and a concluding pointer.
2
Analyze the knowledge argument
Note that re-creation requires precise knowledge, and God has knowledge of all things.
3
Analyze the fire example
See how fire from a green tree demonstrates overcoming opposites, making resurrection easier by comparison.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن الله تعالى كما أخبر عن مقالة المنكر للبعث على الإجمال عقبه قبل إعادة التفسير ما يوجب كونه في حيز الممكنات، ثم أعاد ذكر المقالة وبيان إمكان البعث على طريق التفسير والإيضاح فقال تعالى: (وَضَرَبَ لَنَا مَثَلًا وَنَسِيَ خَلْقَهُ) تقديره: خلقه أولاً، والله أعلم، وضرب لنا مثلاً بقوله: (مَنْ يُحْيِ الْعِظَامَ وَهِيَ رَمِيمٌ) ونسي خلقه أن الله تعالى أنشأ أول مرة لا عن أصل والبداية في تقدير عقولنا أصعب من الإعادة، فعين بذلك أن ذلك ليس من جملة المستحيلات الممتنعات لأن ما هو أصعب في تقدير عقولكم كان ممكنا وتثبت قدرة الله بما عليه قدر ابتداء لأولى في تقدير عقولكم ثم بقوله تعالى: (وَهُوَ بِكُلِّ خَلْقٍ عَلِيمٌ) بين أن الإعادة وإن كان فعلاً محكماً لا تتأتى إلا من عالم فالله تعالى عالم بعلم يحيط بالمعلومات أجمع، ثم بقوله: (الَّذِي جَعَلَ لَكُم مِّنَ الشَّجَرِ الْأَخْضَرِ نَارًا) بين كمال قدرته وعجيب تدبيره أنه جعل من الشجر الأخضر الذي رويت أصوله وفروعه وغصونه من الماء إذ جعل من الأخضر بدون الماء نارا مع تضاد في كيفيتهما، إذ الماء بارد رطب والنار حارة يابسة، ولم يصعب عليه ذلك لكمال قدرته ونفاذ مشيئته وصائب تدبيره ولطف تقديره، وأعلم أن من له هذه القدرة والمشيئة وهذا التدبير والتقدير لا يبعد عنه إيجاد الحياة في العظام الرميمة والأجساد البالية، إذ ليس فيها ما يضاد الحياة، ولو كان فيها ذلك لكان قادرا على إعدام المضاد وإيجاد الحياة وذلك أقرب في تقدير عقولنا من جعل النار من الشجر الأخضر مع بقاء خضرته ووجود ما فيه من الماء، ثم أشار بقوله: (أَوَلَيْسَ الَّذِي خَلَقَ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ)
Then God Almighty, as He informed of the statement of the denier of resurrection in summary, followed it before repeating the explanation with what necessitated its being within the realm of possibilities, then He repeated the statement and the explanation of the possibility of resurrection by way of interpretation and clarification, and said: "And he strikes for Us an example and forgets his creation" meaning his first creation, and Allah knows best. And he strikes for us an example by his saying: "Who will give life to bones when they are decayed?" And he forgot his creation that God Almighty originated first time without an origin, and the beginning in the estimation of our minds is harder than the return, so He specified by that that it is not among the impossible things, because what is harder in the estimation of your minds was possible, and the power of God is established by the fact that He had power over the beginning, which is more fitting in the estimation of your minds. Then by His saying: "And He is of all creation Knowing," He made clear that the return, even if it is a precise act, cannot be accomplished except by a knower, so God is Knowing with a knowledge that encompasses all known things. Then by His saying: "He who made for you from the green tree fire," He made clear the perfection of His power and wonderful management, that He made from the green tree whose roots, branches, and twigs were watered from water, fire without water, despite the opposition in their qualities, since water is cold and wet and fire is hot and dry, and that was not difficult for Him due to the perfection of His power, the penetration of His will, the correctness of His management, and the subtlety of His determination. And He taught that whoever has this power, will, management, and determination, it is not unlikely that He brings life into decayed bones and worn-out bodies, because there is nothing in them that opposes life, and if there were such, He would be able to remove the opposition and bring life, and that is closer in the estimation of our minds than making fire from green tree while preserving its greenness and the presence of water in it. Then He pointed by His saying: "Is not He who created the heavens and the earth..."
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the possibility of resurrection, expounding how the Quran refutes the denier. The author follows the Quranic argument step by step. First, God mentions the denier's objection and then shows that resurrection is possible because initial creation (from nothing) is harder than re-creation, so if the harder is possible, the easier is even more so. Second, God's knowledge is perfect, so the precise act of re-creation is no problem. Third, the example of fire from green tree demonstrates God's power over opposites, making life after death easy by comparison. Finally, the argument from the creation of the heavens and earth (implied completion: 'Is not He who created the heavens and the earth able to give life to the dead?') drives the conclusion home. The author explains each Quranic verse in sequence, showing how it supports the logical possibility of resurrection.

قدرة
تضاد

Correction: The fire example shows God can create fire from its opposite, water, so He can bring life to dead bones.

Checkpoint

A) God's power over opposites
B) That trees contain fire
C) That resurrection is unnecessary
D) That water and fire are the same

Key Takeaway

The Qur'anic Argument from Original Creation for the Possibility of Resurrection
Imam Nasafi explains how the Qur'an refutes deniers by pointing to the first creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi uses the Qur'anic reference to the first creation to prove that resurrection is possible and not impossible.

Core Idea
If God created once from nothing, resurrection is even easier.

Imam Nasafi unpacks a powerful Qur'anic rebuttal to those who deny resurrection. The denier asks, 'Who can give life to decayed bones?' The Qur'an responds by reminding of the original creation, which was harder. This lesson traces the logical argument that places resurrection firmly within the realm of possibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation carefully. Notice the Qur'anic verse quoted within.
2
Identify the denier's claim
The denier questions the revival of decayed bones. The verse uses this as an example. Find the phrase 'Who will give life to bones when they are decayed?' in the translation.
The denier forgets his own creation.
3
Understand the argument from difficulty
The passage argues that the first creation from nothing was more difficult than resurrection. Since God accomplished the harder task, resurrection is not impossible. Grasp this logical move.
First creation ex nihilo is harder than reconstitution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن الله تعالى كما أخبر عن مقالة المنكر للبعث على الإجمال عقبه قبل إعادة التفسير ما يوجب كونه في حيز الممكنات، ثم أعاد ذكر المقالة وبيان إمكان البعث على طريق التفسير والإيضاح فقال تعالى: وَضَرَبَ لَنَا مَثَلًا وَنَسِيَ خَلْقَهُ تقديره : خلقه أولاً، والله أعلم ، وضرب لنا مثلاً بقوله: (مَن يُحْيِ الْعِظَامَ وَهِيَ رَمِيمٌ) ونسي خلقه أن الله تعالى أنشأ أول مرة لا عن أصل والبداية في تقدير عقولنا أصعب من الإعادة، فعين بذلك أن ذلك ليس من جملة المستحيلات الممتنعات لأن ما هو أصعب في تقدير عقولكم كان ممكنا وتثبت قدرة الله بما عليه قدر ابتداء لأولى في تقدير عقولكم
Then indeed Allah the Exalted, just as He informed about the statement of the denier of resurrection in summary, He followed it before the detailed explanation with what necessitates its being within the realm of possibilities. Then He repeated the statement and the explanation of the possibility of resurrection in a detailed and clarifying manner. So He said, the Exalted: "And he strikes for Us an example and forgets his own creation." Its interpretation: He created him first, and Allah knows best. And he strikes an example with His saying: "Who will give life to bones when they are decayed?" And he forgets his creation that Allah the Exalted originated (creation) the first time not from an origin, and the beginning in the estimation of our intellects is more difficult than the return. So He indicated by that that it is not from the category of impossible things, because what is more difficult in your intellects' estimation was possible, and the power of Allah is established by what He established (the creation) originally, which is more fitting in your intellects' estimation.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the Qur'anic argument from original creation for the possibility of resurrection. The author follows the sequence of the verse: Allah first summarizes the denier's objection that bones cannot be revived, then responds by reminding that He created them the first time from nothing. The author explains that the first creation is more difficult in human estimation than the return (resurrection), so if God accomplished the harder task, the easier one is not impossible. He emphasizes that resurrection is excluded from the category of impossibilities. The argument is based on the premise that what is possible in the past is possible in the future, and God's power is established through the actual occurrence of the first creation.

?

How does this truth confront your doubts about His power to forgive your worst sins or to transform your hardened heart? Write one specific area where you struggle to trust Allah's power, and commit to reflecting on His creation of you as evidence.

The Argument from Creation: Greater to Lesser
Nasafi explains the greater-to-lesser argument from creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the creation of the heavens and earth serves as a proof for resurrection through the principle that if God can do the greater, He can do the lesser.

Core Idea
If God creates the vast cosmos, reviving the dead is easier.

Imam Nasafi uses a Qur'anic verse that asks whether the Creator of the heavens and earth can also create the like of humans. He explains that the creation of the heavens is, in our estimation, a greater act than reviving the dead. Therefore, if God's power is established over the greater act, it is even more fitting that He can accomplish the lesser act of resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author quotes the verse and then explains its logical implication.
The verse is from Surah al-Ahqaf (46:33) but is referenced indirectly.
2
Identify the logical principle
The passage uses the principle of 'a fortiori' (awlā): if God can create the greater (heavens and earth), He can certainly create the lesser (resurrection). Identify where this reasoning appears.
3
Compare with your own estimation
The author says 'in the estimation of our intellects' creation is greater. Reflect on why humans might consider cosmic creation more impressive than resurrection, and why this makes the proof effective.
4
Understand the conclusion
The passage concludes that since God's power over the greater act is established, His power over revival is also established—indeed it is more fitting. This refutes those who deny resurrection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أشار بقوله : أَوَلَيْسَ الَّذِي خَلَقَ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ بِقَدِرٍ عَلَى أَن يَخلُقَ مِثْلَهُمْ بَلَى ) إن أمرًا ما لا يفوت قدرته لعظمه فإن خلق السماوات والأرض في تقدير عقولنا أعظم من إحياء الموتى، فلما كانت قدرته ثابتة على ذلك كانت على الإحياء ثابتة بل أدل في تقدير عقولكم، ثم نبه بقوله: ﴿ إِنَّمَا أَمْرُهُ إِذَا أَرَادَ شَيْئًا أَن يَقُولَ لَهُ كُن فَيَكُونُ ) أنه ليس ممن يتعذر عليه شيء أو يصعب عليه أمر بل سرعة وجود ما يوجده كسرعة قول واحد منكم "كن"، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك لم يبق وجه يمتنع وجود الإعادة والإحياء بعد الموت، فلا معنى للإنكار هذا والله أعلم - مضمون الآية
Then He indicated by His saying: "Is not He who created the heavens and the earth able to create the like of them? Yes..." That an affair, any affair, does not escape His power due to its greatness. For the creation of the heavens and the earth in the estimation of our intellects is greater than reviving the dead. So when His power is established over that, it is established over reviving—rather more fitting in your intellects' estimation. Then He alerted by His saying: "His command, when He wills a thing, is only to say to it 'Be', and it is," that He is not one for whom anything is impossible or an affair difficult. Rather, the speed of existence of what He brings into existence is like the speed of a single word from you: "Be." And when the matter is so, no face remains that prevents the existence of the return and revival after death. So there is no meaning to denial. This—and Allah knows best—is the purport of the verse.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a proof from two more Qur'anic verses. First, the creation of the heavens and earth is a greater act than reviving the dead, so if God can do the greater, He can do the lesser. Second, God's command 'Be' makes anything happen instantly without delay or effort. The author concludes that resurrection is not impossible and denial is baseless.

Key Terms
خلق السماوات والأرض
قدرة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that resurrecting the dead is more difficult than creating the heavens and earth because it involves bringing life back to decayed bodies.
Correction: The passage corrects this by pointing out that creating the entire universe is a far greater act in our estimation, so if God can do that, resurrection is even easier for Him.

Checkpoint

A) Because creating the heavens is a greater act, so resurrection is easier for God.
B) Because the heavens are made of the same elements as humans.
C) Because the heavens were created before humans.
D) Because resurrection involves the same kind of power.

Key Takeaway
God's creation of the vast heavens and earth proves that resurrection, being a lesser act, is well within His power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Command 'Be' and Instantaneous Creation
Nasafi explains the command 'Be' argument for instant resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'anic description of God's command 'Be' demonstrates that resurrection is instant and effortless for Him.

Core Idea
God's command 'Be' makes anything exist instantly—no delay or effort.

The passage continues by citing another Qur'anic verse that describes how God creates: He simply says 'Be' and it is. Imam Nasafi explains that this shows that nothing is difficult or impossible for God. The speed of creation is like the speed of a word from us. Therefore, resurrection after death is not only possible but happens without any hindrance. This refutes those who deny the possibility of life after death.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and explanation
Read the Arabic text and translation. Notice that the verse emphasizes the immediacy of creation through the command 'Be'.
The verse is from Surah Ya-Sin (36:82) but is paraphrased here.
2
Understand what 'Be' implies
The passage explains that God is not someone for whom anything is impossible or difficult. The instantaneous existence of what He wills is compared to the speed of saying one word. Reflect on what this reveals about divine power.
3
Apply to resurrection
The author then directly applies this: if God can will anything into existence instantly, then there is nothing preventing the return of life after death. Therefore, denial is baseless.
4
Consider the rhetorical force
The passage ends by saying 'there is no meaning to denial.' Think about why the combination of the two verses (creation and command) completely undermines any rational objection to resurrection.

Proof of Resurrection from God's Power
Sanusi gives two Qur'anic proofs for resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof from the Qur'an that resurrection is not impossible for God.

Core Idea
Resurrection is easier for God than creating the heavens and earth.

Sanusi argues that God's power knows no limit of size or difficulty. He presents two Qur'anic proofs: the greater creation of heavens and earth, and the instantaneous command 'Be!' to show that resurrection is well within divine power.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Pay attention to the mention of the heavens and earth verse.
2
Analyze the two evidences
Identify the two main proofs: (1) creation of heavens and earth is greater, so resurrection is easier; (2) God's command is instantaneous, so no difficulty.
The second proof is the 'Be' verse.
3
Understand the conclusion
Why does the author say there is no meaning to denial? The conclusion follows from the proofs.

بِقَادِرٍ عَلَى أَن يَخْلُقَ مِثْلَهُمْ بَلَى) (۱) إن أمرًا ما لا يفوت قدرته لعظمه فإن خلق السماوات والأرض في تقدير عقولنا أعظم من إحياء الموتى، فلما كانت قدرته ثابتة على ذلك كانت على الإحياء ثابتة بل أدل في تقدير عقولكم، ثم نبه بقوله: ﴿ إِنَّمَا أَمْرُهُ إِذَا أَرَادَ شَيْئًا أَن يَقُولَ لَهُ كُن فَيَكُونُ ﴾ (٢) أنه ليس ممن يتعذر عليه شيء(۳) أو يصعب عليه أمر بل سرعة وجود ما يوجده كسرعة قول واحد منكم "كن"، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك لم يبق وجه يمتنع وجود الإعادة والإحياء بعد الموت، فلا معنى للإنكار هذا والله أعلم - مضمون الآية، غير أن الله تعالى لا يخرج كلامه مخرج كلام الواحد منا (٤) إذا ناظر خصمه بل يخرج مخرج مخاطبة السادة العبيد، والأرباب المماليك، فأخرج هذه المعاني على هذا النظم العجيب والوصف البليغ الذي تكاد العقول الوافرة، والألباب الكاملة تتحير (٥) في رونقه وفخامته وبلاغته وفصاحته، بل تذهل من هيبته وجلالته، ثم إن المتكلمين من سلف الأمة منذ تكلموا في هذه الخصوم وأثبتوا دلائلها في التصاريف لم يزيدوا على ما في الكتاب من مع الإشارة إلى ذلك، بل لم يستخرجوا من قعور تلك البحور وإن غاصت فيها أفكارهم عشر ما فيها من درر الحجج وغرر المعاني والنكت
He is powerful to create the like of them, yes. (1) Indeed, a matter does not escape His power due to its greatness; for the creation of the heavens and the earth is in the estimation of our minds greater than reviving the dead. Since His power is established over that, it is established over revival, rather more indicative in your estimation. Then He alerted by His saying: 'His command, when He wills a thing, is only to say to it "Be," and it is' (2), that He is not one for whom anything is impossible (3) or a matter difficult, but rather the speed of existence of what He brings into existence is like the speed of the saying of one of you, 'Be.' And if the matter is such, there remains no way by which the occurrence of return and revival after death is impossible, so there is no meaning to denial. This — and God knows best — is the purport of the verse. However, God does not produce His speech in the manner of the speech of one of us (4) when he argues with his opponent, but rather He produces it in the manner of addressing masters to slaves and lords to servants. So He produced these meanings in this wondrous composition and eloquent description, at which abundant intellects and complete minds almost become bewildered (5) in its beauty and grandeur and eloquence and fluency, rather they become stunned by its awe and majesty. Then indeed the theologians from the predecessors of the community, since they spoke about these claims and established their proofs in the writings, did not add to what is in the Book beyond indicating that; rather, they did not extract from the depths of those seas, even if their thoughts dived into them, a tenth of what is in them of pearls of arguments and gems of meanings and fine points.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage provides a proof of resurrection from God's power and then highlights the miraculous eloquence of the Qur'anic expression. The author first argues that God's power is not limited by size; creating the heavens and earth is greater in our estimation than resurrecting the dead, so if He can do the greater, He can do the lesser. Then he cites the verse that God's command is instantaneous ('Be and it is'), further showing no difficulty. He then notes that this is the meaning of the verse, but the Qur'an expresses it in a style far beyond human speech, addressing with majesty. He concludes that the theologians before did not add to what the Qur'an contains; they only extracted a fraction of its arguments. So the Qur'an itself is a miracle in its content and style.

Key Terms
الإعادة
الإحياء
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Resurrection is less probable than initial creation because it happens later.
Correction: The author shows that resurrection is actually easier in our estimation because it is smaller than creating the heavens and earth.

Checkpoint
How does the author argue that resurrection is possible for God?
A) By comparing to the creation of the heavens and earth.
B) By citing the verse about God's instantaneous command.
C) Both A and B.
D) By quoting consensus of theologians.

Key Takeaway
God's power over resurrection is proven by His greater creation and instant command.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that your resurrection is as easy for Allah as saying 'Be', how would your attitude towards death and accountability change today? Will you prepare for that moment starting now?
?
Since Allah's command is instantaneous and nothing is difficult for Him, why do you still hesitate to submit fully to His commands, fearing they are too hard for you to follow? What one command will you commit to obeying this week?
?
The creation of the heavens and earth is greater than your own resurrection. If you trust Allah for the vast universe, why do you doubt He can forgive your deepest sins or transform your hardened heart? What sin have you been despairing of? Turn to Him in repentance today.

The Miraculous Eloquence of the Qur'an
Sanusi explains the miraculous eloquence of the Qur'an.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Qur'an's style is a miracle and how it surpasses human speech.

Core Idea
The Qur'an's beauty and depth of meaning are beyond human capacity.

Sanusi shifts from the argument of power to the argument of style. He explains that the Qur'an expresses profound truths in a manner befitting divine majesty, not human argumentation, and that all theologians have only extracted a fraction of its treasures.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on style

Notice the descriptions: wondrous composition, eloquent description.
2
Observe the effect on intellects
Identify what the passage says about the reaction of intellects—they become bewildered and stunned.
This shows the Qur'an's impact is a proof of its divine origin.
3
Consider the theologians' limitation
Understand the claim that past theologians only extracted a fraction of the Qur'an's arguments.

The Impossibility of Knowing Tawhid Without Divine Teaching
Proof that no one could know tawhid independently, concluding it is from Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the kalam proof that comprehensive knowledge of tawhid cannot be attained independently and must come from divine teaching.

Core Idea
No one can know tawhid comprehensively without Allah teaching them.

This passage presents a classic proof by impossibility. The author argues that if someone knew all the details of tawhid without any human teacher or book, that would be impossible; therefore such knowledge must come directly from Allah. This demonstrates the necessity of divine revelation for the deepest theological truths.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the hypothetical scenario and the strong conclusion.
The author uses 'محال ممتنع' to mark the impossibility.
2
Identify the hypothetical scenario
The passage describes someone who never studied with a teacher or book, yet claims to know all aspects of tawhid with their proofs, surpassing scholars.
This is the premise of the impossibility argument.
3
Understand why it is impossible
The author deems such independent comprehensive knowledge impossible (محال ممتنع). Reflect on why deep theological insights require learning or direct divine teaching.
The impossibility leads to the conclusion of divine origin.
4
Grasp the conclusion and praise
The knowledge must be from Allah, who teaches whom He wills. The passage ends with praise of Allah's absolute sovereignty and power.
This is a klassical kalam argument for prophethood and revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ببال أحد منهم من ذلك، شيء، لم يقرعوا للتوحيد بابا، ويجعلون الأنداد والأصنام شيئا عجابا، لم يختلف إلى أحد للتعلم ولا درس كتابا فيه شيء من ذلك ثم عرف من تلقاء نفسه جميع هذه الوجوه التي مر ذكرها بدلائلها، ثم بين على وجه قصر عن بلوغ كنهه ونهايته ممن لا يحصون كثرة من العلماء المبرزين المخصوصين برجاحة العقول والألباب وحدة الخواطر وجودة القرائح الذين زجوا أعمارهم في تعلم العلوم الملية والارتياض بالمعالم الحكمية، والبحث عن حقائق الأشياء، واكتساب العلم بقوانين الجدل وشرائط البرهان. هذا محال ممتنع. وبالوقوف على هذه الجملة يعلم أنه علم ما علم من عند العزيز الحميد الذي يكرم من يشاء من عباده (بما يشاء) ويعلم من يشاء ما يشاء لا يمانع في تدبيره ولا يغالب في سلطانه، ولا يدافع في مشيئته، ولا يعاز في تنفيذ قضيته، له البسط والقبض والإبرام والنقض، يفعل ما يشاء ويحكم ما يريد، وهو ولي التوفيق والتسديد.
It did not occur to any of them [that] something of that; they did not knock on a door for tawhid, and they made rivals and idols a wondrous thing. He did not go to anyone for learning nor study a book containing anything of that; then he knew from himself all these aspects whose mention has passed with their proofs, then he explained in a manner falling short of reaching its core and limit among countless distinguished scholars, those specialized in soundness of intellects and minds, sharpness of thoughts and goodness of natural aptitudes, who spent their lives learning the religious sciences and exercising in the philosophical disciplines, investigating the realities of things, and acquiring knowledge of the rules of dialectic and conditions of demonstration. This is impossible and prevented. And by pausing at this summary, it is known that he knew what he knew from the Mighty, the Praiseworthy, who honors whom He wills among His servants (with what He wills) and teaches whom He wills what He wills. He is not opposed in His management, nor overcome in His authority, nor repelled in His will, nor prevented in executing His decree. To Him belongs expansion and contraction, binding and unbinding; He does what He wills and judges what He desires, and He is the Guardian of success and guidance.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a proof by impossibility (burhān al-imtinā‘). The author argues that no single person could have independently come to know all the detailed aspects of tawhid with their proofs, requiring immense scholarly effort, unless Allah taught him. He gives a hypothetical scenario: someone who never learned from anyone, never studied a book, yet knew all these aspects and explained them in a way that surpasses countless distinguished scholars. This is impossible. The conclusion is that such knowledge must be from Allah. He then praises Allah's absolute sovereignty and power. This is a classic kalam argument for divine origin of prophetic knowledge.

Key Terms
توحيد
العلم
البرهان
الجدل
الاستحالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is circular because it assumes divine teaching to prove divine teaching.
Correction: The argument is not circular. It starts with an accepted impossibility (independent comprehensive knowledge) and infers a cause (divine teaching). It does not presuppose divine teaching; it reasons to it.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what makes the scenario impossible?
A) The person was not intelligent enough.
B) The person did not go to any teacher nor study any book.
C) The scholars of the time were better.
D) The subject is unknowable.

Key Takeaway
Comprehensive knowledge of tawhid cannot be attained independently; it must come from Allah through divine teaching.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that no one can know tawhid comprehensively without Allah teaching them. Where in your understanding of tawhid have you relied on your own intellect instead of seeking direct instruction from the Qur’an and the Prophet? How will you change this starting today?
?
The passage says those who try to know tawhid through their own reasoning fall short of the 'core and limit' that even distinguished scholars cannot reach. Which aspect of your faith have you been content with a superficial understanding, thinking you know enough? What is one concrete step you will take to deepen your knowledge from revealed sources this week?
?
Allah teaches whom He wills what He wills. Does your pride prevent you from being teachable? In what area of your tawhid are you resistant to learning from revelation or from others? Will you humble yourself today and ask Allah to teach you?

The First Aspect: Belief in Allah's Existence
Nasafi introduces the first aspect of belief in Allah: existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in Allah's existence is the foundational pillar that guards against denial (ta'til).

Core Idea
Denying Allah's existence is the deepest form of disbelief.

Imam al-Nasafi begins the discussion of beliefs by focusing on the most important pillar: belief in Allah. He divides this belief into three aspects. In this lesson, we explore the first aspect: affirming Allah's existence, which protects against the error of ta'til (denial of God). The author reminds us that the Prophet (peace be upon him) brought proofs of Allah's existence in the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the structure: the author announces the division into three sections and then presents the first.
The third section is not included in this excerpt.
2
Identify the purpose of this aspect
Note that belief in existence is intended to be free from ta'til (denial). Understand that ta'til means rejecting God's existence.
This is a theological term; consider looking it up.
3
Reflect on the proof mentioned
The author says the Prophet came with proofs from the Quran. Ask yourself why proving existence is necessary before discussing oneness.
This lesson establishes the bedrock of all belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[الكلام في العقيدة] [أولاً: الإيمان بالله ] فنبدأ بالاعتقادات فنقول: الركن الأهم منها الإيمان بالله تعالى وهو ينقسم إلى أقسام ثلاثة أحدها: الإيمان بوجوده ليسلم عن التعطيل وقد مر أنه عليه السلام ورد بذلك وأرشد إلى الدلالة على ثبوته في كتابه الذي أتى به في مواضع على ما مر، ثم الإيمان بوحدانيته ليسلم عن الشرك، وقد ورد به فأقام الدلالة عليه وجرد القول بالتصريح بذلك فقال: تَعَالَوْا إِلَى كَلِمَةٍ سَوَاءٍ بَيْنَنَا وَبَيْنَكُمْ أَلَّا نَعْبُدَ إِلَّا اللَّهَ
[Speech on the Creed] [First: Belief in Allah] We begin with beliefs and say: The most important pillar of them is belief in Allah, the Exalted, and it is divided into three sections. One of them: belief in His existence to be free from denial (ta‘ṭīl), and it has passed that he, peace be upon him, came with that and guided to the proof of His establishment in the Book he brought in places as has passed. Then belief in His oneness to be free from association (shirk), and he came with it and established the proof upon it and expressed the statement explicitly with that, saying: 'Come to a word common between us and you: that we worship none but Allah' (Quran 3:64).
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage begins the detailed discussion of beliefs, focusing on the first pillar: belief in Allah. It states that belief in Allah is divided into three aspects, but only two are mentioned in the excerpt: belief in His existence (to avoid denial) and belief in His oneness (to avoid shirk). The third aspect is not provided here, possibly cut off by the page break. The author provides Quranic evidence for tawhid (Quran 3:64). This is a definition and proof passage.

Key Terms
الإيمان بالله
الوجود
التعطيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Belief in Allah is only about oneness, not existence.
Correction: Nasafi clearly states that belief in Allah includes belief in His existence as a separate and necessary aspect.

Checkpoint
What does belief in Allah's existence protect against according to the passage?
A) Shirk
B) Ta'til (denial)
C) Hypocrisy
D) Innovation

Key Takeaway
The first aspect of belief in Allah is affirming His existence, which saves one from the error of denying God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt shaken by doubts about Allah's existence? What specific proof from the Quran or your life has strengthened your certainty? Write a commitment to revisit that proof this week.
?
The passage warns that denying Allah's existence is the deepest disbelief. Is your conviction in His existence so firm that it shapes your daily choices? What area of your life would change if you truly believed that denial is the worst failure?
?
The Prophet ﷺ brought clear proofs for Allah's existence. When was the last time you shared a proof with someone silently struggling with doubt? Be honest: do you avoid such conversations out of discomfort? Resolve today to learn one simple proof to share.
