The Second Aspect: Belief in Allah's Oneness
Nasafi presents the second aspect of belief in Allah: oneness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in Allah's oneness protects against shirk and is supported by explicit Quranic command.

Core Idea
Tawhid is the call of all prophets.

Having established the necessity of affirming Allah's existence, Imam al-Nasafi now turns to the second aspect: belief in His oneness (tawhid). This aspect shields the believer from shirk (associating partners with Allah). The author references the Quranic verse commonly known as the 'word of equality' (kalimat sawā') which calls people to worship Allah alone.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the English translation. Note that this is the second aspect of belief in Allah.
The verse quoted is Quran 3:64.
2
Understand the purpose: avoiding shirk
Recognize that belief in oneness is to be free from shirk. Shirk is associating partners with Allah.
This is the opposite of tawhid.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
The author quotes a verse that calls for unity in worship. Reflect on why this verse is a powerful proof for tawhid.
This verse is addressed to both Muslims and People of the Book.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[الكلام في العقيدة] [أولاً: الإيمان بالله ] فنبدأ بالاعتقادات فنقول: الركن الأهم منها الإيمان بالله تعالى وهو ينقسم إلى أقسام ثلاثة أحدها: الإيمان بوجوده ليسلم عن التعطيل وقد مر أنه عليه السلام ورد بذلك وأرشد إلى الدلالة على ثبوته في كتابه الذي أتى به في مواضع على ما مر، ثم الإيمان بوحدانيته ليسلم عن الشرك، وقد ورد به فأقام الدلالة عليه وجرد القول بالتصريح بذلك فقال: تَعَالَوْا إِلَى كَلِمَةٍ سَوَاءٍ بَيْنَنَا وَبَيْنَكُمْ أَلَّا نَعْبُدَ إِلَّا اللَّهَ

One of them: belief in His existence to be free from denial (ta‘ṭīl), and it has passed that he, peace be upon him, came with that and guided to the proof of His establishment in the Book he brought in places as has passed. Then belief in His oneness to be free from association (shirk), and he came with it and established the proof upon it and expressed the statement explicitly with that, saying: 'Come to a word common between us and you: that we worship none but Allah' (Quran 3:64).

Commentary
This passage begins the detailed discussion of beliefs, focusing on the first pillar: belief in Allah. It states that belief in Allah is divided into three aspects, but only two are mentioned in the excerpt: belief in His existence (to avoid denial) and belief in His oneness (to avoid shirk). The third aspect is not provided here, possibly cut off by the page break. The author provides Quranic evidence for tawhid (Quran 3:64). This is a definition and proof passage.

Quranic Proofs for the Two Types of Istita'a
Nasafi cites two Quranic proofs to demonstrate the division of istita'a.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses two Quranic verses to establish the existence of istita'a and its division into two types: the capability of soundness of means and the capability of the act itself.

Core Idea
The Quran distinguishes between having the means and having the ability to act.

Nasafi turns to the Quran to ground the division of istita'a in divine revelation. He presents two verses that, when understood correctly, show that capability can refer either to the preconditions for an action (like health and wealth) or to the actual ability to perform the action at the moment of doing it. This lesson unpacks those proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the first proof from Surah al-Mujadila
Carefully read the verse about the expiation for zihar and Nasafi's explanation. Notice how the word 'yastati' must refer to the preconditions of fasting, not the actual ability to fast two months, which can only exist at the moment of action.
This verse demonstrates the first type: istita'a of soundness of means.
2
Read the second proof from the hypocrites' statement
Read the verse where hypocrites say 'If we had the means, we would have gone out' and Allah declares them liars. Understand why they were lying: they meant the capability of health and wealth, not the true capability to fight, which disappears before action.
This demonstrates that capability can be of two kinds.
3
Synthesize the two proofs
Consider how both verses together prove the division of istita'a into two distinct types: the pre-existing soundness of means and the actual ability to perform the act at the moment of doing it.
This division is crucial for the theological discussion of human capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الدليل على وجود الاستطاعة وانقسامها إلى قسمين قوله تعالى: ﴿ فَمَن لَّمْ يَسْتَطِعْ فَإِطْعَامُ سِتِّينَ مِسْكِينًا ﴾ والمراد منه استطاعة الأسباب والآلات إذ لا يتصور وجود قدرة أداء صوم شهرين من قبل الشروع في أدائه، ويستحيل بقاء القدرة التي كانت موجودة عند الخصوم إلى شهرين، فدل أنه أراد به استطاعة سلامة الأسباب وصحة الآلات. والدليل عليه ما عير الله تعالى به من قال من أهل النفاق : لَوِ اسْتَطَعْنَا لَخَرَجْنَا مَعَكُمْ وكذبهم الله تعالى في ذلك القول، ولو كانوا أرادوا بذلك الكلام الاستطاعة التي هي حقيقة قدرة الفعل ما كانوا بنفيها عن أنفسهم كاذبين، إذ لا شك أن استطاعة فعل الجهاد لا تبقى من وقت كونهم بالمدينة إلى أن يلقوا العدو ويباشروا القتال، وكان الخروج مطلوبًا لذلك، وحيث كذبهم دل أنهم أرادوا بذلك المرض أو فقد المال على ما بين الله تعالى بقوله : لَيْسَ عَلَى الضُّعَفَاءِ وَلَا عَلَى الْمَرْضَى ... إلى أن قال: إِنَّمَا السَّبِيلُ عَلَى الَّذِينَ يَسْتَذِنُونَكَ وَهُمْ أَغْنِيَاء .
Then the proof for the existence of istita'a (capability) and its division into two types is the saying of the Exalted: 'And whoever does not find the means, then the feeding of sixty needy persons' (Quran 58:4). What is intended by it is the istita'a of means and instruments, since it is inconceivable that the capability to perform the fast of two months exists before beginning to perform it, and it is impossible for the capability that existed according to the opponents to last for two months. So it indicates that He intended by it the istita'a of soundness of means and health of instruments. Another proof for it is what Allah, the Exalted, reproached those among the hypocrites who said: 'If we had the means, we would have gone out with you' (Quran 9:42), and Allah declared them liars in that statement. If they had intended by that speech the istita'a that is the true capability of the action, they would not have been liars in denying it of themselves, for there is no doubt that the capability to perform jihad does not remain from the time they were in Medina until they meet the enemy and engage in combat, and going out was required for that. And since He declared them liars, it indicates that they intended by that illness or lack of wealth, as Allah, the Exalted, clarified by His saying: 'There is no blame upon the weak nor upon the ill...' up to His saying: 'The way is only against those who ask permission of you while they are rich' (Quran 9:91-93).
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a scriptural argumentation. Nasafi provides two Quranic proofs to demonstrate the existence of istita'a and its division into two types. First, he cites the verse from Surah al-Mujadila (58:4) regarding the expiation for zihar: whoever cannot fast two consecutive months must feed sixty poor people. The word 'yastati' (cannot find the means) refers to the ability to fast, which is a capacity that must exist before the act. Since one cannot have the specific ability to fast two months before starting, the verse indicates the first type of capability: soundness of means and health of instruments (i.e., being physically able to fast). The second proof is from the hypocrisy of some who said, 'If we had the means, we would have gone out with you' (Quran 9:42). Allah called them liars. If they had meant the true capability to fight (the second kind), they would not be lying because that capability only arises at the moment of action. Since they were lying, they must have meant the first type—freedom from illness and possession of wealth—as clarified by the subsequent verses (9:91-93) that excuse the weak and ill. Thus, the Quran recognizes both kinds of capability: the pre-existing health/wealth condition and the actual capacity to act.

استطاعة سلامة الأسباب
قدرة الفعل

الجهاد

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quranic term 'istita'a' always refers to the actual ability to perform an action.
Correction: Nasafi shows that in some verses, 'istita'a' refers to the preconditions like health and wealth, not the actual ability to act.

Checkpoint

B) Because the capability to fight jihad cannot exist before the moment of action, so they must have meant health and wealth.
C) Because they were excused by illness and poverty.
D) Because the verse says they were liars, proving they had the true capability.

Key Takeaway
The Quran provides clear evidence that istita'a has two meanings: capability of means and capability of action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The hypocrites used their lack of means as an excuse while Allah knew they were lying. Is there any area in your life where you hide your unwillingness behind a claim of inability? Will you ask Allah to expose that to you today?
?
If your capability to act only truly arises when you step forward in faith, what have you been waiting for perfect conditions that will never arrive? What step can you take right now, trusting that the actual ability will come?

Three Views on Annihilation and Refutation
Three theories of annihilation and refutation of Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three proposed mechanisms for God's annihilation of bodies and the rational flaw in the Mu'tazilī theory.

Core Idea
No theory of annihilation by opposites escapes arbitrariness.

The passage examines how God can annihilate a body. Three views are presented: al-Ka'bi's (cessation of recreating endurance), al-Baqillani's (removal of accidents), and the Mu'tazila's (arrival of an opposite). The author rejects the latter as logically arbitrary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify three views
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Identify the three different theories of annihilation mentioned.
The views are separated by 'وأما' and 'وأما'.
2
Analyze al-Ka'bi's view and its flaw
Notice that al-Ka'bi says endurance is an accident renewed moment by moment. The author objects that an accident cannot host the creation of endurance, so this mechanism fails.
3
Understand al-Baqillani's view
Al-Baqillani proposes that annihilation occurs by cutting off colors and spatial configurations. The author notes this is only applicable to bodies that have such accidents, without further objection.
4
Focus on the Mu'tazila view and its refutation
The Mu'tazila say annihilation happens when an opposite arrives. The author declares this impossible because the pre-existing opposite has no stronger claim to non-existence than the arriving one. He dismisses the 'occurrence is stronger' argument as arbitrary.
This is the core refutation.
5
Reflect on the logical principle
Consider why the author considers the argument arbitrary: neither opposite is more worthy of non-existence, so there is no reason for one to annihilate the other.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكعبي، فإن من مذهب هؤلاء أن البقاء عرض حادث في الأجسام لا يبقى بنفسه بل يتجدد ساعة فساعة، فإذا أراد الله تعالى إفناء الجسم قطع عنه البقاء فلم يخلقه فيه فينعدم، والعرض ليس بمحل لخلق البقاء فيه ليقال إنه إذا لم يخلق فيه البقاء في الثاني انعدم، فلم يتصور الفناء بهذا الطريق على مذهب هؤلاء، وأما أن يكون يقطع الألوان والأكوان كما ذهب إليه أبو بكر الباقلاني من متأخري متكلمي أهل الحديث؛ لأن هذا لن يتصور إلا في الأجسام التي يحلها الألوان والأكوان وأما أن يكون بطريان ضده عليه بأن يطرأ عليه ضده فيعدمه وهذا هو مذهب هؤلاء المخالفين لنا من المعتزلة في المسألة وهذا محال، لأن هذا الضد القائم الثابت المتقرر في المحل ليس بأولى بالعدم من الضد الطارئ الحادث آنفًا، ولا معنى لقول بعض أغبيائهم: إن الحدوث أقوى من البقاء؛ لأن هذا ليس بأولى ممن يقول: البقاء أقوى من الحدوث.
Al-Ka'bi, for it is from the doctrine of these that endurance (al-baqā') is an accident (ʿaraḍ) occurring in bodies, not subsisting by itself but renewing hour by hour. So when God Most High intends to annihilate a body, He cuts off endurance from it, not creating it in it, and it becomes non-existent. And an accident is not a locus for the creation of endurance in it such that it be said: if He does not create endurance in it in the second [moment], it becomes non-existent. So annihilation is not conceivable by this path according to the doctrine of these. And as for its being cutting off colors and spatial configurations (al-akwān) as Abū Bakr al-Bāqillānī among the later theologians of the people of hadith held—because this is only conceivable in bodies that admit colors and configurations. And as for its being by the arrival of its opposite against it, such that its opposite arrives and annihilates it—this is the doctrine of these opponents of ours among the Muʿtazila in this matter, and it is impossible. Because this opposite, established, fixed, and settled in the locus, is not more entitled to non-existence than the arriving opposite that occurs anew. And there is no meaning to the statement of some of their fools that occurrence (al-ḥudūth) is stronger than endurance; because this is not more entitled than one who says: endurance is stronger than occurrence.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage surveys three views on how God annihilates a body and refutes the Muʿtazilī position. First, it presents al-Kaʿbī's view: endurance is an accident that does not persist but is recreated moment by moment; annihilation occurs when God ceases to create it. The author objects that an accident cannot host the creation of endurance, so this theory fails. Second, al-Bāqillānī's view: annihilation is cutting off colors and spatial configurations—only applicable to bodies that have these accidents. Third, the Muʿtazilī view: annihilation happens when an opposite arrives and destroys the enduring attribute. The author declares this impossible, because the pre-existing opposite has no stronger claim to non-existence than the newly arriving one. He dismisses the claim that 'occurrence is stronger than endurance' as arbitrary, since one could equally claim the reverse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the Mu'tazila's annihilation-by-opposite is a coherent explanation.
Correction: The author shows it is arbitrary because neither opposite has a stronger claim to non-existence.

Checkpoint

Proof that the Enduring is Stronger in Existence
Proof that the enduring is stronger in existence than the occurring.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ontological argument that the enduring being (al-bāqī) is stronger in existence than the newly occurring (al-ḥādith), based on dependence on power, necessity vs contingency, and temporal priority.

Core Idea
The enduring being's existence is self-sufficient and necessary, making it ontologically stronger than the contingent, dependent occurring.

This passage from Tabṣirat al-Adilla presents a proof that the eternal, enduring being—God—is stronger in existence than anything that comes into being. The argument draws on the nature of existence, power, and necessity. Let's unpack the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to get a sense of the argument's flow.
Pay attention to the terms 'الباقي' and 'الحادث'.
2
Identify the two key comparisons
Notice the contrast between the enduring's existence not being attached to a preventable power, and the occurring's existence being attached. Also note the distinction between necessary and contingent existence.
These are the core ontological arguments.
3
Understand the temporal argument
The author argues that the occurring has no existence before its occurrence, so its prior non-existence does not give it strength. The enduring, however, has existence before the arrival of its opposite, which gives it strength.
This is about priority in existence.
4
Examine the analogy
The analogy compares removing what is already established vs. repelling what is not yet established. This illustrates why the enduring is harder to remove.
Connect this to the previous steps.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider how this argument supports the doctrine of God's necessary existence and ontological superiority.
This ties back to Maturidi theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الدليل على أن الباقي أقوى من الحادث في الوجود أن الباقي لم يتعلق وجوده بقدرة يصح منع القادر منه ويتوهم ذلك فيه، والحدث يتعلق وجوده بقدرة يصح منع القادر منه ويتوهم ذلك في الجملة، والدليل عليه أن الباقي واجب الوجود في حال طريان ضده عليه، والحادث جائز الوجود في حال حدوثه، ولا شك أن واجب الوجود أقوى في الوجود من جائز الوجود، على أن قوته ليس بأكثر من وجوده، ولا وجود للحادث قبل حالة الحدوث، فعدمه قبل حدوثه لا يكون موجبًا قوته في وجوده، والباقي له وجود قبل وجوده في هذه الحالة التي حدث فيه الضد فوجوده قبل وجوده موجب قوته في وجوده، والذي يقرأ هذا أن العرض الحادث يرفع الثابت المتقرر، والباقي يرفع ما لم يتقرر بعد ولم يثبت بعد، ولا شك أن دفع ما لم يثبت أسهل من رفع ما تقرر، فكان رفع الثابت المتقرر لما لم يثبت بعد أولى في عقل من له عقل من رفع ما ليس بثابت في نفسه لما هو ثابت متقرر.
Then the proof that the enduring is stronger than the occurring in existence is that the existence of the enduring is not attached to a power from which the powerful one may be prevented and that may be imagined concerning it; and the occurring's existence is attached to a power from which the powerful one may be prevented and that may be imagined concerning it in general. And the proof of it is that the enduring is necessary in existence at the time of the arrival of its opposite against it, while the occurring is contingent in existence at the time of its occurrence. There is no doubt that the necessary in existence is stronger in existence than the contingent in existence—even though its strength is not greater than its existence. And there is no existence for the occurring before the state of occurrence, so its non-existence before its occurrence does not entail its strength in its existence. The enduring has existence before its existence in this state in which the opposite occurred, so its existence before its existence entails its strength in its existence. And one who reads this—that the occurring accident removes what is established and settled, while the enduring removes what has not yet been settled nor established—there is no doubt that repelling what has not been established is easier than removing what has been settled. So the removal of what is established and settled by what has not yet been established is more appropriate in the mind of one who has a mind than the removal of what is not established in itself by what is established and settled.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage presents a proof that the enduring being (al-bāqī) is stronger in existence than the newly occurring (al-ḥādith). The author first contrasts the ontological grounding: the enduring's existence does not depend on a power that could be withheld, whereas the occurring's existence does depend on a power that could be prevented. Next, he argues that at the moment an opposite arrives, the enduring is necessary of existence (it cannot cease to exist by itself), while the occurring is contingent. Since the necessary is stronger than the contingent, the enduring is stronger. He adds that the occurring has no existence before its occurrence, so its prior non-existence does not give it strength. The enduring has existence prior to the arrival of the opposite, which gives it strength. A final analogy: it is easier to prevent something not yet established than to remove what is already settled; thus an enduring thing can only be removed by something already established, not by a new thing.

Key Terms
الباقي
الحادث
واجب الوجود
جائز الوجود
القدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Strength in existence refers to physical power or duration in time.
Correction: Strength here means ontological firmness: the enduring being's existence is self-sufficient, necessary, and not dependent on any external cause.

Checkpoint
According to the proof, why is the enduring stronger than the occurring?
A) Because it is older in time.
B) Because its existence is not dependent on a power that can be prevented, and it is necessary of existence at the moment of the opposite's arrival.
C) Because it is a substance, not an accident.
D) Because it has more matter.

Key Takeaway
The enduring being's existence is ontologically superior because it does not depend on any power, is necessary by itself, and has priority in existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Could it be that this removal was actually from the enduring One, who alone can remove what is established? How does this reshape your trust in Him?
?
You are an occurring being—your existence at this very moment is attached to a power that could be withheld. If you truly believed that, would you live more humbly and urgently? What would you change today if you knew your existence could be removed as easily as it was given?

The Trilemma Refuting Annihilation by Opposite
Trilemma refuting the Mu'tazilī theory of annihilation by opposite.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical trilemma used to refute the Muʿtazilī claim that an opposite causes annihilation, and why each option is impossible.

Core Idea
The new opposite cannot cause annihilation before, during, or after its existence.

The Muʿtazilīs argued that an enduring attribute is annihilated when its opposite arrives. But when does this causation occur? The author presents a devastating trilemma: the opposite cannot cause non-existence before it exists, nor at the moment of existence (due to locus problems), nor after existence (due to causal priority). Each path leads to contradiction, dismantling the claim entirely.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Muʿtazilī claim
The Muʿtazilīs held that annihilation of an attribute is caused by the arrival of its opposite (e.g., blackness destroys whiteness). The author aims to refute this by asking a simple timing question.
2
Consider the first timing: before existence
The author asks: does the opposite cause non-existence before it exists? This is impossible because a non-existent thing cannot be a cause.
The non-existent cannot affect the existent.
3
Consider the second timing: during existence
Does it cause non-existence at the moment of its own existence? Here the author examines two subcases: whether it exists in the same locus as the enduring attribute or in a different locus. Both are impossible.
If in the same locus, both opposites would coexist. If not in a locus, accidents cannot exist without a locus.
4
Consider the third timing: after existence
The author uses the Muʿtazilīs' own principle that cause precedes effect. If the opposite causes annihilation after it exists, then its existence would be before the annihilation, but then the cause would not be simultaneous with the effect—contradicting their own causal theory.
5
Conclude the refutation
All three timings are impossible, so the annihilation cannot be caused by the arrival of an opposite. This refutes the Muʿtazilī claim and upholds that only Allah causes annihilation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذي يقطع شغب هؤلاء الجهلة أن يقال لهم: إن الطارئ متى يوجب عدم الباقي قبل وجوده أم في حال وجوده أم بعدما وجد؟ لا جائز أن يقال يوجب عدم الباقي قبل وجوده لأنه قبل وجوده معدوم، والمعدوم لا يوجب عدم الموجود، فكان انعدام الباقي قبل وجود الطارئ لعلة سوى وجود الطارئ، ولا جائز أن يوجب عدمه في حال وجوده لأنا نقول: يوجد في هذا المحل أم لا في محل آخر؟ فإن قال: يوجد في هذا، فهذا محال، لأن وجوده في هذا المحل قبل ارتفاع الأول عن المحل محال؛ لأنه يوجب البقاء للضدين في الوجود، وإذا التقيا في الوجود لم يكونا ضدين وإن وجد لا في محل فوجود العرض لا في محل محال أيضا، ووجوده لا في محل هذا الضد لا يوجب عدمه؛ لأن وجوده ضد لا في محل ضده لا يوجب عدم ضده إن وجد في محل آخر، فذاك لا يوجب عدم العرض الباقي لأن السواد الموجود في المحل لا يوجب عدم البياض الثابت في محل آخر إلى أن ينتقل إلى هذا المحل، ولا يتصور انتفاء له إلى هذا المحل لاستحالة الانتقال من محل إلى محل على الأعراض، ولأن هذا العرض الطارئ عندهم علة لانعدام الباقي، ومن أصلهم أن العلة تكون سابقة على المعلول، فيكون وجود الطارئ سابقا على انعدام الموجود ثم لا يوجب عدمه.
And what cuts off the sophistry of these ignoramuses is that one says to them: When does the newly arriving cause the non-existence of the enduring—before its existence, or at the moment of its existence, or after it has existed? It is not permissible to say that it causes the non-existence of the enduring before its existence, because before its existence it is non-existent, and the non-existent does not cause the non-existence of the existent. So the non-existence of the enduring before the existence of the newly arriving is due to a cause other than the existence of the newly arriving. And it is not permissible that it causes its non-existence at the moment of its existence, for we say: Does it exist in this locus or in another locus? If he says: It exists in this [same locus], this is impossible, because its existence in this locus before the removal of the first from the locus is impossible; for it entails the subsistence of both opposites in existence, and when they meet in existence they are not opposites. And if it exists not in a locus—then the existence of an accident not in a locus is also impossible. And its existence not in the locus of this opposite does not entail its non-existence; because the existence of an opposite not in the locus of its opposite does not necessitate the non-existence of its opposite if it exists in another locus—that does not necessitate the non-existence of the enduring accident because the black existing in a locus does not necessitate the non-existence of the white established in another locus until it transfers to this locus. And it is inconceivable for it to remove itself to this locus due to the impossibility of transfer from locus to locus for accidents. And because this newly arriving accident according to them is a cause for the annihilation of the enduring, and it is from their principle that the cause precedes the effect, so the existence of the newly arriving precedes the annihilation of the existent, and then it does not cause its non-existence.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage provides a definitive refutation of the Muʿtazilī claim that annihilation occurs by the arrival of an opposite. The author poses a three-part dilemma: when does the new opposite cause the non-existence of the enduring? Before its own existence, during its existence, or after? Each option is impossible. Before existence, the new opposite is non-existent and cannot affect the existent. During existence, the author asks whether it exists in the same locus or another. If the same locus, both opposites would coexist, which is impossible. If not in a locus, then an accident cannot exist without a locus. If it exists in a different locus, the opposite in another locus does not affect the enduring attribute. Finally, the author invokes the Muʿtazilī principle that a cause must precede its effect; if the new opposite is the cause, it must exist before the annihilation, but then its effect would be before its existence, contradiction.

Key Terms
الطارئ
الضد
المحل
العلة
المعلول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the new opposite could cause annihilation after it exists, even if not simultaneous.
Correction: The author shows that even after existence, the opposite cannot cause annihilation because the Muʿtazilī principle requires cause to precede effect; if the opposite is the cause, its existence should immediately cause annihilation, but if it delays, then it is not the cause.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it impossible for the opposite to cause non-existence before its own existence?
A) Because the non-existent cannot be a cause.
B) Because the locus would be empty.
C) Because the opposite would have to coexist with the enduring.
D) Because the cause must precede the effect.

Key Takeaway
The arrival of an opposite cannot be the cause of annihilation, as every possible timing leads to a logical impossibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever assume that a new habit (like patience) will automatically destroy an old one (like anger) the moment it appears? This lesson shows that two opposites cannot coexist in the same moment. When have you expected immediate transformation without allowing time for the old to be genuinely removed? Will you instead acknowledge that patience must be built and anger actively dismantled, not simply replaced in an instant?
?
If a non-existent cause cannot produce an effect, then what does that say about your hopes for change based on future circumstances that haven't yet arrived? Are you waiting for a 'future opposite' to fix your problems? How might you instead take responsibility for addressing the causes already present?
?
Consider a recurring sin you struggle with. Do you think that simply entering a good environment (the 'new opposite') will automatically erase it? This lesson teaches that the external good cannot directly annihilate the internal bad, because they exist in different 'loci.' What does this force you to confront about the need for internal, intentional change rather than relying on external circumstances?

Scriptural Proofs for Soundness of Means as Basis of Obligation
Imam al-Nasafi presents Qur'anic examples and logical argument to show obligation depends on soundness of means.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Nasafi uses Qur'anic examples of Hajj and Jihad to prove that valid obligation requires only soundness of means, not actual capability.

Core Idea
Obligation is based on having the means, not on already having the ability.

Imam al-Nasafi now appeals to scripture to support the Maturidi position. He presents two concrete examples from the Qur'an: Hajj and Jihad. In both cases, people are obligated even though they lack actual capability at the moment of address. This passage unpacks the reasoning and defends it against a potential objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the flow: examples, principle, objection, rebuttal, and final illustration.
The passage is dense; don't worry about every detail on first read.
2
Identify the two scriptural examples
Find the Hajj example (person in Bukhara) and the Jihad example (those at the frontiers). Notice that in both, obligation is tied to having the means, not actual performance ability.
What means are mentioned? Provisions, mount, sufficiency.
3
Understand the principle and objection
The author states that a command to an act includes command to its necessary prerequisites. Then he rejects the idea that one must first acquire capability; that would reverse the logical order.
Focus on the phrase 'followed follows the follower' – it's about logical priority.
4
Examine the consensus and Moses proof
The consensus proof: neglecting Hajj despite having means incurs sin for leaving Hajj, not the journey. The Moses example shows that blame attaches when means are present, even if actual ability is lacking.
These support the distinction between soundness of means and real capability.
5
Reflect on the key distinction
Distinguish between 'first type of capability' (soundness of means) and 'second type' (actual ability). The passage concludes that divine address relies on the first.
This is the heart of the Maturidi position on obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ورد كتاب الله تعالى بتقرير ذلك، فإنه تعالى خاطب من ببخارى - عند وجود الزاد والراحلة وتوفر الأسباب والآلات - بأداء الحج وأوجب عليه ذلك، وإن كانت قدرة أداء أفعال الحج منعدمة ببخارى ، وأوجب - عند عموم التغير وقصور من بالثغور من أهل الإسلام عن مقاومة من بإزائهم من الكفرة وعجزهم عن الذب عن البيضة وحماية الحوزة - على من بأطراف دار الإسلام من المسلمين الذين بهم وكفاية، جهاد أولئك الأعداء وزبهم عن حريم دار الإسلام، وإن كانت قدرة مجاهدة العدو بأقصى الروم والهند منعدمة . ولا شك أن الحج والجهاد يجبان أولاً، ثم لما لم يتمكن من أدائهما إلا بقطع المسافة وجب عليه ذلك. والخروج على ما هو الأصل أن الأمر بالفعل أمر به وبما لم يتوصل إلى أدائه إلا به، ولا وجه إلى القول بأنه يجب عليه الخروج وقطع المسافة ليحصل له قدرة الأداء ثم يجب الأداء حينئذ لأن إيجاب تحصيل شرائط الأداء ثابت لما هو من ضرورة الخروج عن الواجب، فأما إيجاب تحصيل أسباب الوجوب أو شرائطه فغير ثابت البتة لما في الأول لاتباع التابع المتبوع وفي الثاني اتباع المتبوع التابع ، وهو قلب المعقول – يدل عليه أن من وجد الزاد والراحلة ولم يخرج إلى الحج حتى مات يأثم إثم ترك الحج بإجماع الأمة لا إثم ترك الخروج وصاحب موسى عليه السلام عاتبه عند ترك الصبر مع قوله: إِنَّكَ لَن تَسْتَطِيعَ مَعِيَ صَبْرًا لما أن أسباب الصبر وآلاته كانت ثابتة، وإنما المنعدم حقيقة استطاعة الصبر، دل أن الخطاب يعتمد الاستطاعة الأولى لا الثانية.
And the Book of Allah Almighty has come confirming that. For He Almighty addressed the person in Bukhara – when he had provisions and mount and the means and instruments were available – with performing Hajj and made it obligatory upon him, even though the capability to perform the actions of Hajj was absent in Bukhara. And He obligated – at the time of general change and the insufficiency of those at the frontiers among the Muslims to resist those facing them from the disbelievers, and their inability to defend the community and protect the territory – upon those at the edges of the Abode of Islam from among the Muslims who had sufficiency, the jihad against those enemies and their repulsion from the sacred precinct of the Abode of Islam, even though the capability to fight the enemy in the farthest reaches of Rome and India was absent. And there is no doubt that Hajj and Jihad are obligatory first, then when one cannot perform them except by traversing distance, that (journey) becomes obligatory upon him. And the matter is in accordance with the principle that the command to do an act is a command to do it and to that without which its performance cannot be attained. And there is no way to say that he must set out and traverse distance in order to acquire the capability to perform, then perform at that time, because making the acquisition of the conditions of performance obligatory is established because it is a necessary consequence of performing the obligation. As for making the acquisition of the causes or conditions of obligation obligatory, it is not established at all, because in the first case the follower follows the followed, and in the second case the followed follows the follower, which is an inversion of reason. This is indicated by the fact that whoever finds provisions and mount and does not go out for Hajj until he dies is sinful for leaving Hajj by consensus of the ummah, not sinful for leaving the journey. And the companion of Moses (peace be upon him) reproached him when he lacked patience, despite his saying: 'Indeed, you will never be able to have patience with me' [Qur'an 18:72?] because the causes and instruments of patience were present, and what was absent was only the reality of the ability to be patient. This indicates that the address relies on the first type of capability, not the second.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage provides scriptural evidence from the Qur'an for the Maturidi position that valid obligation requires only soundness of means (salāmat al-ālāt), not actual capability (ḥaqīqat al-qudra). The author gives two examples: Hajj and Jihad. For Hajj, God addresses a person in Bukhara who has provisions and a mount – i.e., the means to travel – with the obligation of Hajj, even though the actual capability to perform the rituals of Hajj (e.g., standing at Arafat) is absent while he is still in Bukhara. This shows that the obligation is not contingent on having actual capability at the moment of address, but on having the means to acquire it. Similarly, for Jihad, God obligates those at the borders of the Islamic world who have sufficient strength to fight, even though the actual capability to engage the distant enemy is absent at that moment. The author then explains the principle: the command to perform an act is also a command to do whatever is necessary to achieve it. So if Hajj is obligatory, the journey to perform it also becomes obligatory. However, one cannot say that the journey is obligatory in order to acquire the capability to perform, because that would reverse the logical order: the obligation to acquire the cause of obligation would make the acquisition precede the obligation, which is irrational. The proof from consensus is that someone who has the means but fails to go to Hajj and dies is sinning for abandoning Hajj, not for abandoning the journey, meaning the journey is a necessary part of fulfilling the obligation, not a separate obligation to acquire capability. Finally, the example of Moses and al-Khidr (the companion) illustrates this: Moses was reproached for lacking patience despite the statement that he would not be able to have patience, because the means (causes and instruments) for patience were present in him; only the actual ability to be patient was absent. Thus the divine address relies on the first type of capability (soundness of means), not the second (actual capability).

Key Terms
حج (Hajj)
جهاد (Jihad)
استطاعة (al-istitāʿa)
سلامة الآلات (salāmat al-ālāt)
حقيقة الاستطاعة (ḥaqīqat al-istitāʿa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Maturidi position contradicts scripture.
Correction: Imam al-Nasafi shows that scripture itself (Hajj and Jihad verses) supports that obligation is based on soundness of means, not actual capability.

Checkpoint
According to the proof from Hajj, why is the person in Bukhara obligated for Hajj despite lacking actual capability to perform it?
A) Because God can obligate anything at any time.
B) Because the person has the means to acquire capability by traveling.
C) Because Hajj is obligatory regardless of capability.
D) Because the person actually has the capability for Hajj.

Key Takeaway
Soundness of means is the basis for obligation, not actual capability, as confirmed by scripture and reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have health, wealth, and time to pray, give charity, or seek knowledge—but you delay, saying you are not ready or capable of doing it perfectly. What is the one religious duty you have been postponing because you feel you lack the 'actual ability'? Write it down now. Then, looking at the means you already possess, commit to taking the first concrete step toward it this week. What is that step?
?
When you face a difficult task like standing up for truth, defending your faith, or helping someone in need, do you wait until you feel strong enough, or do you act on the means you already have? What means (knowledge, resources, support from others) do you already possess that you are ignoring? Name one specific means you will use today to act on a neglected duty.
?
The man in Bukhara could have said, 'I am not in Mecca, so Hajj is not required yet.' What is your equivalent excuse for a duty you know God has obligated on you? Write that excuse down. Now, using the logic of this passage—that obligation is based on means, not on being at the destination—write a rebuttal to your own excuse. What will you do differently starting now?

Refutation of Jabriyya: Scriptural and Rational Proofs
Nasafi presents scriptural and rational proofs against the Jabriyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses Quranic verses and rational arguments to demonstrate human agency and refute absolute determinism.

Core Idea
Scripture and reason together affirm human responsibility.

Nasafi opens his refutation by asserting that the Jabriyya doctrine is invalid on multiple grounds. He first cites Quranic verses that command, promise, and threaten, which imply human ability to act. Then he presents rational arguments showing the absurdity of attributing all actions to God alone. This lesson covers these two foundational pillars of his proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the flow of argument. Note the structure: first scriptural evidence, then rational evidence.
Pay attention to the Quranic citations and the logical dilemmas presented.
2
Analyze the scriptural evidence
Identify the Quranic verses mentioned and explain how each implies human action. Understand that God's commands, promises, and threats presuppose the ability to obey or disobey.
The author argues that attributing acts to God as Creator does not negate human acquisition.
3
Analyze the rational evidence
Work through the three rational sub-arguments: (a) It is ugly to attribute evil to God, (b) Reward and punishment require real human action, (c) Self-command is impossible, so God cannot be both commander and commanded.
Each sub-argument reinforces the conclusion that actions cannot be purely from God.
4
Synthesize the refutation
Connect the scriptural and rational proofs to see how they collectively refute the Jabriyya position. The passage establishes that human beings are genuine agents.
This sets the stage for the self-evident proof in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان بطلان قول الجبرية. ومذهب الجبرية باطل بدلالة السمع والعقل والضرورة التي تصير دافع ذلك مكابرًا. فأما السمع فمن نحو قوله تعالى: اعْمَلُوا مَا شِنْتُمْ وَأَفْعَلُوا الْخَيْرَ، وفي الجزاء: كَذَلِكَ يُرِيهِمُ اللَّهُ أَعْمَلَهُمْ حَسَرَاتٍ عَلَيْهِمْ، وقوله تعالى: وَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ، وقوله: جَزَاءً بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ، وغير ذلك مما أثبت لهم أسماء العمال ولفعلهم اسم الفعل بالأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد، وليس في الإضافة إلى الله تعالى نفي ذلك بل هي عليه [؟] الله تعالى بأن خلقها على ما وأوجدها بعد أن لم تكن، وللخلق على ما كسبوها وفعلوها على أن الله تعالى أمر ونهى ومحال الأمر بما لا فعل للمأمور أو المنهى، وقال الله تعالى: إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَأْمُرُ بِالْعَدْلِ وَالْإِحْسَانِ، ولو جاز الأمر بذلك بلا معنى الفعل في الحقيقة لجاز الأمر بشيء يكون لأمس أو للعام الأول أو بإنشاء الخلائق، وإن كان لا معنى لذلك في أمر الخلق، ثم في العقل قبيح أن يضاف إلى الله تعالى الطاعة والمعصية وارتكاب الفواحش والمناكير، وأنه المأمور المنهى المثاب المعاقب، فبطل أن يكون الفعل من هذه الوجوه له ولا قوة إلا بالله. وأيضا أن الله تعالى إنما وعد الثواب لمن أطاعه في الدنيا والعقاب لمن عصاه، فإذا كان الأمران فعله فإذا هو المجزي بما ذكر، وإذا كان الثواب والعقاب حقيقة فالائتمار والانتهاء كذلك، ولا قوة إلا بالله تعالى. وكذلك في العقل محال أن يأمر أحد نفسه أو يطيعه أو يعصيه، ومحال تسمية الله تعالى عبدًا ذليلاً مطيعا عاصيًا سفيهًا جائراً، وقد سمى الله تعالى بهذا كله أولئك الذين أمرهم ونهاهم، فإذا صارت هذه الأسماء في التحقيق له فيكون هو الرب وهو العبد وهو الخالق والمخلوق ولا غيره، وذلك مدفوع في السمع والعقل جميعًا، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وأيضا أن كل حد يعلم من نفسه أنه مختار لما يفعله، وأنه فاعل كاسب، فلو جاز صرف مثله عما هو طريق العلم به الحس أو إبطاله فحق العلم بجميع العالم مثله، وذلك قول مهجور، ومثله قول أهل الجبر، وهذا قول تغني الحكاية عن الإطناب فيه لانقراض الجبرية عن آخرهم وارتفاع مقالتهم، ولما ليس لهذا القول معنى تكلم عليه صاحبه إذ هو ينفي عن نفسه حقيقة كل قول وفعل، وإذا انتفى بطل القول، وبه يناظر ويحاج، فزال الذي يكون به الحجاج واضمحل.
Statement of the invalidity of the doctrine of the Jabriyya. The doctrine of the Jabriyya is invalid by the evidence of revelation, reason, and necessity, which renders its defender obstinate. As for revelation, it is from such as His saying, may He be exalted: 'Do what you will and do good', and in requital: 'Thus Allah shows them their deeds as regrets upon them', and His saying: 'And whoever does an atom's weight', and His saying: 'A recompense for what they used to do', and other things by which He affirmed for them names of workers and for their action the name of action by command, prohibition, promise, and threat. And there is not in attribution to Allah, may He be exalted, a negation of that; rather it is [?] Allah, may He be exalted, by creating them as they are and bringing them into existence after they were not, and for the creatures according to what they acquired and did, on the basis that Allah, may He be exalted, commanded and prohibited, and it is impossible to command something over which the commanded or prohibited has no act. And Allah, may He be exalted, said: 'Indeed, Allah commands justice and excellence.' And if commanding that without meaning of act in reality were permissible, then it would be permissible to command something that was for yesterday or for the first year or to create creatures, even if there is no meaning to that in the command to creatures. Then in reason, it is ugly that obedience and disobedience and committing abominations and evils be attributed to Allah, may He be exalted, and that He be the commanded, the prohibited, the rewarded, the punished. So the act becomes invalid that from these aspects it is from Him, and there is no power except through Allah. And also: Allah, may He be exalted, only promised reward to whoever obeys Him in this world and punishment to whoever disobeys Him. If the two states were His act, then He is the requiter for what was mentioned, and if reward and punishment are real, then compliance and abstention are likewise, and there is no power except through Allah, may He be exalted. And likewise in reason, it is impossible that one command himself or obey himself or disobey himself, and it is impossible to name Allah, may He be exalted, a lowly slave, obedient, disobedient, foolish, unjust. And Allah, may He be exalted, has named all these those whom He commanded and prohibited. If these names become in reality to Him, then He is the Lord and He is the slave, He is the Creator and the created, and no other; and that is repudiated in both revelation and reason, and there is no power except through Allah. And also: every individual knows from himself that he is free in choice for what he does, and that he is an agent and acquirer. If it were permissible to turn him away from what is the path of knowledge about it through sense or to nullify it, then the right of knowledge about the entire world would be like that. And that is an abandoned saying, and similar to it is the saying of the people of jabr. And this is a saying whose narration suffices from elaboration upon it due to the extinction of the Jabriyya completely and the disappearance of their doctrine. And since this saying has no meaning, its proponent speaks upon it, for it negates from itself the reality of every saying and act. And when it is negated, the saying becomes invalid, and by it one debates and argues, so that by which debate is conducted has ceased and vanished.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (بطلان) of the Jabriyya doctrine of absolute determinism. The author begins by declaring that the Jabriyya position is invalid based on three sources of evidence: revelation (السمع), reason (العقل), and necessity (الضرورة), the last of which renders anyone who denies it a mere obstinate disputant. He then proceeds with the scriptural evidence: God commands human action (e.g., 'Do what you will' and 'do good'), threatens punishment for deeds (e.g., showing them their deeds as regrets), and promises reward (e.g., 'Whoever does an atom's weight ...'). These verses attribute acts to humans, using terms like 'workers' and 'action,' and link them to commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats. The author argues that attributing these acts to God by virtue of His creating them does not negate human attribution; rather, God created the acts and brought them into existence, while the creatures are the acquirers and doers of them in accordance with God's command and prohibition. It is impossible for God to command something over which the commanded has no actual ability to perform. If that were permissible, one could absurdly command things that have already happened or that are impossible. Next, the rational proof (العقل) is presented: it is morally repugnant (قبيح) to attribute disobedience and evil to God, or to say that God is the commanded, punished, etc. If God's own act were the subject of command and prohibition, He would be both commander and commanded, which is impossible. Moreover, God promised reward for obedience and punishment for disobedience; if both obedience and disobedience are God's act, then God is rewarding and punishing Himself, which contradicts the reality of reward and punishment. Reason also shows that one cannot command or obey oneself; it is impossible to call God a slave, disobedient, foolish, or unjust. Yet God applies these terms to those He commands and prohibits. If these attributes were truly applied to God, He would be both Lord and slave, Creator and created, which revelation and reason both reject. Finally, the author appeals to self-evident knowledge (الضرورة): every person intuitively knows that he chooses his actions freely and is the agent and acquirer of them. Denying this foundational self-awareness would dissolve all knowledge based on sense perception, an absurd consequence. The author concludes that the Jabriyya doctrine is so refuted that its proponents have become extinct, and their argument is self-defeating because it negates the reality of all speech and action, leaving no basis for meaningful discussion.

Key Terms
الجبرية
السمع
العقل
الأمر والنهي
الفعل
الكسب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the author denies God's role as creator of actions.
Correction: The author distinguishes God's creation of the act from human acquisition (كسب), affirming both.

Checkpoint

B) It is ugly and impossible.
C) It is a matter of divine decree.
D) It is affirmed by scriptural evidence.

Key Takeaway
Scripture and reason both show that human beings are genuine agents, undermining the Jabriyya claim that all actions are solely from God.

Refutation of Jabriyya: Self-Evident Knowledge and Conclusion
Nasafi presents a self-evident proof of free will and concludes the refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses self-evident human knowledge of free choice to refute the Jabriyya and why their doctrine is self-defeating.

Core Idea
Every person knows intuitively that they choose their actions.

After scriptural and rational proofs, Nasafi now appeals to an even more fundamental evidence: the innate human awareness of free will. Every person knows from themselves that they are free in choice and the agent of their actions. Denying this foundational self-knowledge would destroy all knowledge based on sense perception. Furthermore, the Jabriyya position is so absurd that its proponents have become extinct, and their argument is self-defeating because it negates the reality of all speech and action.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the self-evident proof and the concluding remarks. Note the shift from external evidence to internal human experience.
The author emphasizes that this knowledge is necessary and immediate.
2
Understand the self-evident proof
Nasafi argues that every individual (كل حد) knows from themselves that they are free in choice (مختار) and are the agent (فاعل) and acquirer (كاسب) of their actions. This knowledge comes from sense and self-awareness.
If this self-evident truth could be overturned, all sensory knowledge would be invalid.
3
Analyze the conclusion about the Jabriyya
The author notes that the Jabriyya have become extinct because their doctrine is self-refuting. It negates the reality of every saying and act, leaving no basis for debate or argument.
The passage ends with the idea that the very means of debate has vanished.

Source Text

بيان بطلان قول الجبرية. ومذهب الجبرية باطل بدلالة السمع والعقل والضرورة التي تصير دافع ذلك مكابرًا. فأما السمع فمن نحو قوله تعالى: اعْمَلُوا مَا شِنْتُمْ وَأَفْعَلُوا الْخَيْرَ، وفي الجزاء: كَذَلِكَ يُرِيهِمُ اللَّهُ أَعْمَلَهُمْ حَسَرَاتٍ عَلَيْهِمْ، وقوله تعالى: وَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ، وقوله: جَزَاءً بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ، وغير ذلك مما أثبت لهم أسماء العمال ولفعلهم اسم الفعل بالأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد، وليس في الإضافة إلى الله تعالى نفي ذلك بل هي عليه [؟] الله تعالى بأن خلقها على ما وأوجدها بعد أن لم تكن، وللخلق على ما كسبوها وفعلوها على أن الله تعالى أمر ونهى ومحال الأمر بما لا فعل للمأمور أو المنهى، وقال الله تعالى: إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَأْمُرُ بِالْعَدْلِ وَالْإِحْسَانِ، ولو جاز الأمر بذلك بلا معنى الفعل في الحقيقة لجاز الأمر بشيء يكون لأمس أو للعام الأول أو بإنشاء الخلائق، وإن كان لا معنى لذلك في أمر الخلق، ثم في العقل قبيح أن يضاف إلى الله تعالى الطاعة والمعصية وارتكاب الفواحش والمناكير، وأنه المأمور المنهى المثاب المعاقب، فبطل أن يكون الفعل من هذه الوجوه له ولا قوة إلا بالله. وأيضا أن الله تعالى إنما وعد الثواب لمن أطاعه في الدنيا والعقاب لمن عصاه، فإذا كان الأمران فعله فإذا هو المجزي بما ذكر، وإذا كان الثواب والعقاب حقيقة فالائتمار والانتهاء كذلك، ولا قوة إلا بالله تعالى. وكذلك في العقل محال أن يأمر أحد نفسه أو يطيعه أو يعصيه، ومحال تسمية الله تعالى عبدًا ذليلاً مطيعا عاصيًا سفيهًا جائراً، وقد سمى الله تعالى بهذا كله أولئك الذين أمرهم ونهاهم، فإذا صارت هذه الأسماء في التحقيق له فيكون هو الرب وهو العبد وهو الخالق والمخلوق ولا غيره، وذلك مدفوع في السمع والعقل جميعًا، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وأيضا أن كل حد يعلم من نفسه أنه مختار لما يفعله، وأنه فاعل كاسب، فلو جاز صرف مثله عما هو طريق العلم به الحس أو إبطاله فحق العلم بجميع العالم مثله، وذلك قول مهجور، ومثله قول أهل الجبر، وهذا قول تغني الحكاية عن الإطناب فيه لانقراض الجبرية عن آخرهم وارتفاع مقالتهم، ولما ليس لهذا القول معنى تكلم عليه صاحبه إذ هو ينفي عن نفسه حقيقة كل قول وفعل، وإذا انتفى بطل القول، وبه يناظر ويحاج، فزال الذي يكون به الحجاج واضمحل.
Statement of the invalidity of the doctrine of the Jabriyya. The doctrine of the Jabriyya is invalid by the evidence of revelation, reason, and necessity, which renders its defender obstinate. As for revelation, it is from such as His saying, may He be exalted: 'Do what you will and do good', and in requital: 'Thus Allah shows them their deeds as regrets upon them', and His saying: 'And whoever does an atom's weight', and His saying: 'A recompense for what they used to do', and other things by which He affirmed for them names of workers and for their action the name of action by command, prohibition, promise, and threat. And there is not in attribution to Allah, may He be exalted, a negation of that; rather it is [?] Allah, may He be exalted, by creating them as they are and bringing them into existence after they were not, and for the creatures according to what they acquired and did, on the basis that Allah, may He be exalted, commanded and prohibited, and it is impossible to command something over which the commanded or prohibited has no act. And Allah, may He be exalted, said: 'Indeed, Allah commands justice and excellence.' And if commanding that without meaning of act in reality were permissible, then it would be permissible to command something that was for yesterday or for the first year or to create creatures, even if there is no meaning to that in the command to creatures. Then in reason, it is ugly that obedience and disobedience and committing abominations and evils be attributed to Allah, may He be exalted, and that He be the commanded, the prohibited, the rewarded, the punished. So the act becomes invalid that from these aspects it is from Him, and there is no power except through Allah. And also: Allah, may He be exalted, only promised reward to whoever obeys Him in this world and punishment to whoever disobeys Him. If the two states were His act, then He is the requiter for what was mentioned, and if reward and punishment are real, then compliance and abstention are likewise, and there is no power except through Allah, may He be exalted. And likewise in reason, it is impossible that one command himself or obey himself or disobey himself, and it is impossible to name Allah, may He be exalted, a lowly slave, obedient, disobedient, foolish, unjust. And Allah, may He be exalted, has named all these those whom He commanded and prohibited. If these names become in reality to Him, then He is the Lord and He is the slave, He is the Creator and the created, and no other; and that is repudiated in both revelation and reason, and there is no power except through Allah. And also: every individual knows from himself that he is free in choice for what he does, and that he is an agent and acquirer. If it were permissible to turn him away from what is the path of knowledge about it through sense or to nullify it, then the right of knowledge about the entire world would be like that. And that is an abandoned saying, and similar to it is the saying of the people of jabr. And this is a saying whose narration suffices from elaboration upon it due to the extinction of the Jabriyya completely and the disappearance of their doctrine. And since this saying has no meaning, its proponent speaks upon it, for it negates from itself the reality of every saying and act. And when it is negated, the saying becomes invalid, and by it one debates and argues, so that by which debate is conducted has ceased and vanished.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (بطلان) of the Jabriyya doctrine of absolute determinism. The author begins by declaring that the Jabriyya position is invalid based on three sources of evidence: revelation (السمع), reason (العقل), and necessity (الضرورة), the last of which renders anyone who denies it a mere obstinate disputant. He then proceeds with the scriptural evidence: God commands human action (e.g., 'Do what you will' and 'do good'), threatens punishment for deeds (e.g., showing them their deeds as regrets), and promises reward (e.g., 'Whoever does an atom's weight ...'). These verses attribute acts to humans, using terms like 'workers' and 'action,' and link them to commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats. The author argues that attributing these acts to God by virtue of His creating them does not negate human attribution; rather, God created the acts and brought them into existence, while the creatures are the acquirers and doers of them in accordance with God's command and prohibition. It is impossible for God to command something over which the commanded has no actual ability to perform. If that were permissible, one could absurdly command things that have already happened or that are impossible. Next, the rational proof (العقل) is presented: it is morally repugnant (قبيح) to attribute disobedience and evil to God, or to say that God is the commanded, punished, etc. If God's own act were the subject of command and prohibition, He would be both commander and commanded, which is impossible. Moreover, God promised reward for obedience and punishment for disobedience; if both obedience and disobedience are God's act, then God is rewarding and punishing Himself, which contradicts the reality of reward and punishment. Reason also shows that one cannot command or obey oneself; it is impossible to call God a slave, disobedient, foolish, or unjust. Yet God applies these terms to those He commands and prohibits. If these attributes were truly applied to God, He would be both Lord and slave, Creator and created, which revelation and reason both reject. Finally, the author appeals to self-evident knowledge (الضرورة): every person intuitively knows that he chooses his actions freely and is the agent and acquirer of them. Denying this foundational self-awareness would dissolve all knowledge based on sense perception, an absurd consequence. The author concludes that the Jabriyya doctrine is so refuted that its proponents have become extinct, and their argument is self-defeating because it negates the reality of all speech and action, leaving no basis for meaningful discussion.

Reward Belongs to the Action, Not the Object
Nasafi argues that recompense is for actions, not objects, using Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses Quranic verses to prove that divine reward is based on the action itself, not the physical object produced, and how this supports the createdness of human actions.

Core Idea
Recompense is for the act, not the artifact.

Nasafi presents a subtle but crucial theological point: when the Quran speaks of 'what you used to do' or 'what you carve,' the focus is on the act of doing or carving, not the thing produced. This distinction matters because it shows that actions are real entities that can be created and rewarded. In this passage, he unpacks two Quranic verses to draw this out.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to get the flow of Nasafi's argument.
Notice the two Quranic verses he cites.
2
Identify the key principle
Nasafi states clearly: 'الجزاء يكون بالعمل دون المعمول' — recompense is by the action, not the thing acted upon. Underline this sentence.
This is the main thesis.
3
Examine the first verse (Paradise)
He interprets 'بما كنتم تعملون' as 'by your action.' Why is this interpretation significant? It means the action itself is the basis for reward.
The word 'بما' can mean 'by that which' — he specifies it as the act, not the product.
4
Examine the second verse (idols)
He interprets 'ما تنحتون' as 'your carving.' The polytheists worshipped idols only after carving them; thus they worshipped the act of carving, not the stone.
This reinforces that the action (carving) is what matters.
5
Synthesize the argument
Both verses show that actions are the real loci of reward and worship. This implies actions are created entities, not mere accidents.
This connects to broader kalam discussions on human actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معمولهم، وقال تعالى: ادْخُلُوا الْجَنَّةَ بِمَا كُنتُمْ تَعْمَلُونَ أي بعملكم إذ الجزاء يكون بالعمل دون المعمول، وكذا دخول الجنة، وكذا في قوله تعالى: أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ أي نحتكم لأنهم لما كانوا لا يعبدون تلك الأعيان إلا بعدما نحتوا ولم يروها مستحقة للعبادة إلا به صاروا في الحقيقة عابدين نحتهم دون منحوتهم.
Their worked thing, and He said exalted: 'Enter Paradise because of what you used to do' meaning by your action, since recompense is by the action not the thing acted upon, and likewise entering Paradise, and likewise in His saying exalted: 'Do you worship what you carve?' meaning your carving, because when they did not worship those entities except after they had carved them and did not consider them deserving of worship except by it, they became in reality worshippers of their carving rather than their carved thing.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a proof that human actions are created by God, using Quranic verses. The author begins by citing the verse 'ادخُلُوا الْجَنَّةَ بِمَا كُنتُمْ تَعْمَلُونَ' (Enter Paradise because of what you used to do). He interprets 'بما كنتم تعملون' as 'by your action' (عمل), not 'the thing acted upon' (معمول), because recompense is for the action itself. He then applies this reasoning to the verse 'أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ' (Do you worship what you carve?), explaining that 'what you carve' (ما تنحتون) means 'your carving' (نحتكم), the act of carving, not the carved idol. The polytheists only worshipped the idols after carving them, so they were actually worshippers of their own act of carving. This supports the idea that actions are real, created entities that are the basis of reward and worship.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think reward is for the physical object produced (e.g., the idol).
Correction: Reward is for the action itself, as Nasafi shows from Quran.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi shows that Quranic references to 'what you do' or 'what you carve' point to the action itself as the basis for reward, proving actions are real and created.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Three Proofs Against Creation Power for Others
Enumeration of three proofs for impossibility of creation power for other than God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational proofs that establish the impossibility of creation power for anyone other than God.

Core Idea
Only God can create—three proofs show it's logically impossible for others.

The author presents a multi-faceted argument. He first states the thesis that creation power is impossible for other than God, then provides three distinct proofs (wujūh). These proofs appeal to necessary conditions, the testimony of reason, and a reductio ad absurdum. This lesson introduces all three before focusing on the first in detail.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text from the start through the mention of the three proofs, ending at 'والحق لا يولد الباطل'. Note the three proofs are enumerated as واحد, آخر, ثالث.
The enumeration is clear.
2
Identify the three proofs
List the three proofs: (1) Loss of condition, (2) Testimony of reason, (3) Leads to impossible. Understand each briefly.
The third proof is a logical consequence argument.
3
Reflect on the argumentative strategy
Notice how the author uses multiple independent proofs to strengthen his case. This is typical in kalam to leave no doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إثبات قدرة التخليق لغير الله تعالى محال]: الدليل على ذلك وجوه: أحدها فقد شرط ثبوت تلك القدرة وثبوت الشيء في حال انعدام شرطه الذي علق وجوده به محال تشهد العقول الصحيحة بفطرها بإحالته. والآخر: شهادة نفس العقل. والثالث: أن إثبات قدرة التخليق له يؤدي إلى أمر محال عرفت إحالته بإجماع الخصوم وشهادة العقول وما يؤدي إلى المحال يعرف إحالته لأن الصحيح لا ينتج الفاسد، والحق لا يولد الباطل. [ الأول : فقد شرط ثبوت قدرة التخليق للعبد ] أما الأول فبيانه أن شرط ثبوت قدرة التخليق هو ثبوت العلم للخالق بالمخلوق قبل حصول المخلوق، ودليل كون ذلك شرطا كتاب الله تعالى ومساعدة الخصوم
Establishing the power of creation for other than God is impossible. Proof of that has aspects: First: The condition for affirming that power, and affirming a thing in the state of the absence of its condition which its existence is tied to is impossible, as sound intellects testify by their innate disposition to its impossibility. Second: The testimony of reason itself. Third: That affirming the power of creation for him leads to an impossible matter whose impossibility is known by the consensus of opponents and the testimony of intellects, and what leads to the impossible is known to be impossible because the sound does not produce the corrupt, and the truth does not generate falsehood. [First: The condition for affirming the power of creation for the servant] As for the first, its explanation is that the condition for affirming the power of creation is the affirmation of the creator's knowledge of the created before the created comes into existence, and the proof that this is a condition is the Book of God Most High and the assistance of the opponents.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is a proof structure. The author states that it is impossible for anyone other than God to have the power of creation, then provides three distinct proofs (wujūh). The first proof is based on a condition: any power of creation requires a prior condition, which is the creator's knowledge of the created before it exists. Since this condition is absent in the servant, the existence of such power in the servant is impossible, as sound intellects testify. The second proof is simply the direct testimony of reason (shahādat nafs al-'aql). The third proof is a reductio: affirming creation power for a servant leads to an absurd consequence known to be impossible by consensus of opponents and reason; therefore the premise is false because truth cannot generate falsehood. The author then elaborates the first proof: the condition for creation power is knowledge of the created before its coming into existence. He cites the Qur'an and the opponents' own admission as evidence for this condition.

Key Terms
قدرة التخليق
محال
فطرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think creation power could be delegated to prophets or angels.
Correction: The author argues it is logically impossible, not just prohibited.

Checkpoint
How many proofs does the author list for the impossibility of creation power for other than God?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Three rational proofs—based on condition, reason, and reductio—establish that creation power belongs exclusively to God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that only God possesses the power to create. In what specific area of your life have you been acting as if you—or another human—have the power to create something (like your own peace, success, or moral standing)? What does this passage demand you surrender today?
?
The third proof says 'the sound does not produce the corrupt, and the truth does not generate falsehood.' Where in your daily worship or character is there a gap between what you claim to believe and what your actions produce? How will you close that gap starting now?
?
The first proof says that if a condition is missing, the thing is impossible. Are there any conditions of true faith (like sincerity, fear of Allah, trust in His creation power) that you have neglected, and how does this passage show you the impossibility of the fruits of faith without those conditions?

The First Proof in Detail: Prior Knowledge as Condition
Elaboration of the first proof: condition of prior knowledge for creation power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed first proof: creation power requires prior knowledge of the creation, and this condition is not met in anyone except God.

Core Idea
To create, you must first know—only God has that knowledge.

After enumerating three proofs, the author elaborates the first one, which is based on a necessary condition (sharṭ). He explains that the condition for creation power is the creator's knowledge (ʿilm) of the created before it exists. This condition is proven by the Qur'an and the opponents' own consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the detailed passage
Read the Arabic text from 'أما الأول فبيانه' to the end. Focus on the explanation of the condition.
Notice the phrase 'شرط ثبوت قدرة التخليق'.
2
Identify the condition and its evidence
The condition is knowledge (ʿilm) of the created before it exists. The evidence is the Book of God and assistance of opponents.
The author appeals to both revelation and rational consensus.
3
Understand the implication
Since this condition is not present in the servant (ʿabd), the power of creation cannot be affirmed for him.
This is the core of the first proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إثبات قدرة التخليق لغير الله تعالى محال]: الدليل على ذلك وجوه: أحدها فقد شرط ثبوت تلك القدرة وثبوت الشيء في حال انعدام شرطه الذي علق وجوده به محال تشهد العقول الصحيحة بفطرها بإحالته. والآخر: شهادة نفس العقل. والثالث: أن إثبات قدرة التخليق له يؤدي إلى أمر محال عرفت إحالته بإجماع الخصوم وشهادة العقول وما يؤدي إلى المحال يعرف إحالته لأن الصحيح لا ينتج الفاسد، والحق لا يولد الباطل. [ الأول : فقد شرط ثبوت قدرة التخليق للعبد ] أما الأول فبيانه أن شرط ثبوت قدرة التخليق هو ثبوت العلم للخالق بالمخلوق قبل حصول المخلوق، ودليل كون ذلك شرطا كتاب الله تعالى ومساعدة الخصوم
Establishing the power of creation for other than God is impossible. Proof of that has aspects: First: The condition for affirming that power, and affirming a thing in the state of the absence of its condition which its existence is tied to is impossible, as sound intellects testify by their innate disposition to its impossibility. Second: The testimony of reason itself. Third: That affirming the power of creation for him leads to an impossible matter whose impossibility is known by the consensus of opponents and the testimony of intellects, and what leads to the impossible is known to be impossible because the sound does not produce the corrupt, and the truth does not generate falsehood. [First: The condition for affirming the power of creation for the servant] As for the first, its explanation is that the condition for affirming the power of creation is the affirmation of the creator's knowledge of the created before the created comes into existence, and the proof that this is a condition is the Book of God Most High and the assistance of the opponents.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is a proof structure. The author states that it is impossible for anyone other than God to have the power of creation, then provides three distinct proofs (wujūh). The first proof is based on a condition: any power of creation requires a prior condition, which is the creator's knowledge of the created before it exists. Since this condition is absent in the servant, the existence of such power in the servant is impossible, as sound intellects testify. The second proof is simply the direct testimony of reason (shahādat nafs al-'aql). The third proof is a reductio: affirming creation power for a servant leads to an absurd consequence known to be impossible by consensus of opponents and reason; therefore the premise is false because truth cannot generate falsehood. The author then elaborates the first proof: the condition for creation power is knowledge of the created before its coming into existence. He cites the Qur'an and the opponents' own admission as evidence for this condition.

Key Terms
شرط
علم
قدرة التخليق
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that creation power could be independent of knowledge, e.g., spontaneous generation.
Correction: The author argues creation necessarily requires prior knowledge, citing revelation and consensus.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, what is the condition for the power of creation?
A) The creator must be eternal.
B) The creator must have prior knowledge of the created.
C) The creator must be omnipotent.
D) The creator must be just.

Key Takeaway
The first proof shows that creation power requires prior knowledge of the created, which only God possesses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what specific area of your life do you act as if God does not know your situation before you experience it? How can you surrender that area to His prior knowledge today?
?
If you truly believed that God's knowledge of you is complete and precedes your existence, how would you change the way you plan and worry about the future?
?
The proof shows that only God possesses the prior knowledge necessary to create. Are you trying to 'create' your own life without relying on His knowledge? What would it look like to let His prior knowledge guide your decisions starting today?
