The Rational Proof That Humans Lack Creative Power
Nasafi presents the rational proof for the absence of creative power in the servant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that the servant does not possess creative power, based on the observation that actions often contradict intentions.

Core Idea
Your actions not matching your intentions prove you are not their creator.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi presents the second proof that humans do not have creative power. It is a purely rational proof: look at your own actions — how often they turn out differently than you intended. This mismatch reveals that the true creator is Allah, not you. The argument also distinguishes between two ways we know this: through reason and through sensory observation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Nasafi uses a condensed, logical style.
2
Identify the core argument
The passage argues that if the servant had creative power, his actions would match his intentions. Since they often don't, the true agent is another. Find this chain of reasoning.
3
Distinguish the two proofs
Nasafi then says there are two ways to know the mismatch: through reason and through sense. The text gives an example from reason (the disbeliever). See if you can identify what the sensory proof might be.
The sensory proof would involve observable outcomes like accidents or unintended consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني: العقل يشهد بعدم قدرة التخليق للعبد
وأما شهادة نفس العقل أن العبد ليست له قدرة التخليق فهي أن أفعال العباد لا تخرج على ما يقصده العبد من الوصف لفعله بل تخرج على ما يضاد ذلك الوصف ولو كان العبد له قدرة الاختراع والإيجاد لأوجده على ما يريده من الوصف ويقصده، وحيث لم يوجد الفعل على وفق مراده، دل أن الموجد لذلك غيره فجعله فعلاً له على الوصف الذي شاء الموجد أن يوجده ويجعله فعلاً للعبد، والعبد تتعلق قدرته بذلك الموجود على الوصف الذي أوجده الموجد.
ودليل خروج فعل العبد عن الوصف الذي يقصده العبد وحصوله على وصف لا يقصده، بل يقصد ضده أمران أحدهما ما يعرف امتناع حصول ما قصده من الوصف وحصول ما يضاد الوصف العقل، والآخر يعرف ذلك فيه بالحس.
أما ما يعرف فيه ذلك بالعقل فهو أن الكافر يعتقد وجوب عبادة الصنم (۹)
The second: The intellect testifies to the absence of creative power for the servant. As for the testimony of the intellect itself that the servant does not have creative power, it is that the actions of servants do not come out according to the description the servant intends for his action, but rather come out according to a description opposite to that. If the servant had the power of invention and bringing into existence, he would bring it into existence according to the description he wills and intends. Since the action does not occur in accordance with his desire, it indicates that the bringer into existence is other than him. So He made it an action for Him according to the description that the bringer into existence willed to bring it into existence and make it an action for the servant. The servant's power is related to that existing thing according to the description that the bringer into existence brought it into existence. The proof of the departure of the servant's action from the description he intends and its occurrence according to a description he does not intend (rather he intends its opposite) is two matters: one of them is that reason knows the impossibility of obtaining the description he intended and the occurrence of the opposite description; the other is that the sense knows that. As for what is known therein by reason, it is that the disbeliever believes in the obligation of worshipping the idol (9).
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof (the second proof, following a previous one) that the servant does not possess creative power (qudrat al-takhlīq). The argument is based on observation: the actions of servants often fail to match the intended description; instead they turn out opposite to what was intended. If a person truly had the power to invent and bring into existence, he would bring about exactly what he intends. Since his action does not conform to his intention, it shows that the agent (al-mūjid) is other than himself. The true agent creates the action according to His own will and then assigns it to the servant as an acquired act (kasb). The servant's power relates only to the existing action as it actually occurs. There are two ways to prove the mismatch between intention and outcome: through reason (al-‘aql) and through sense (al-ḥiss). An example from reason is given: the disbeliever intends to worship an idol, but reason judges that such worship is wrong and that his action is actually disobedience. The text cuts off, but the point is that the disbeliever's action does not achieve the intended good.

Key Terms
قدرة التخليق
الاختراع والإيجاد
الموجد
الوصف
المعرفة بالعقل
المعرفة بالحس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Because the servant has power to choose, he must be the creator of his own acts.
Correction: Nasafi argues that the actual outcome differing from intention shows that creation belongs to God alone; the servant's power is limited to acquisition (kasb).

Checkpoint
What is the main rational proof Nasafi gives for the absence of creative power in the servant?
A) The servant cannot see his own actions
B) Actions often contradict the servant's intentions
C) The servant lacks knowledge of the future
D) The intellect cannot grasp creation

Key Takeaway
The rational proof that humans are not creators is grounded in the observable fact that our actions do not always match our intentions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Can you recall a specific moment when your intention for an action was pure, yet the outcome was far from what you wanted? Did that experience not reveal that you are not the ultimate controller of your own life? How will you let this truth reshape your reliance on your own planning today?
?
If even your most carefully intended actions are ultimately brought into existence by Another, what does that say about your sense of self-sufficiency? Are you willing to acknowledge that your very existence and every action you 'perform' is a gift from God, and not a product of your own power?
?
The proof shows that your power is only related to the action as it already exists, not to its creation. Does that make you feel less responsible, or more? In light of this, how will you view your accountability for your actions tomorrow, knowing that God is the true creator of them?

The Servant Lacks Creative Power
Al-Nasafi states the core rational proof that the servant lacks creative power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the central rational argument that the servant cannot be the true creator of his actions because his actions do not occur as he intends.

Core Idea
If we controlled our actions, they would always match our intention—but they don't.

Imam al-Nasafi opens this passage with a clear rational proof. He argues that since our actions frequently occur contrary to what we intend, we cannot be the ones who bring them into existence. This establishes that the true power of creation belongs solely to God, and the servant's power is merely related to the act as God creates it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the author's argument.
Notice the use of 'قدرة التخليق' vs 'قدرة الاختراع والإيجاد'.
2
Identify the main claim
The author states that the servant does not have creative power. Find the sentence that states this and the supporting reasoning.
3
Understand the argument from intention
The author argues that if the servant were the creator, his actions would follow his intended description. Since they do not, the true creator is other than him.
This is a simple conditional argument.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that God creates the act according to His will, and the servant's power is related to it in that state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما شهادة نفس العقل أن العبد ليست له قدرة التخليق فهي أن أفعال العباد لا تخرج على ما يقصده العبد من الوصف لفعله بل تخرج على ما يضاد ذلك الوصف ولو كان العبد له قدرة الاختراع والإيجاد لأوجده على ما يريده من الوصف ويقصده، وحيث لم يوجد الفعل على وفق مراده، دل أن الموجد لذلك غيره فجعله فعلاً له على الوصف الذي شاء الموجد أن يوجده ويجعله فعلاً للعبد، والعبد تتعلق قدرته بذلك الموجود على الوصف الذي أوجده الموجد. ودليل خروج فعل العبد عن الوصف الذي يقصده العبد وحصوله على وصف لا يقصده، بل يقصد ضده أمران أحدهما ما يعرف امتناع حصول ما قصده من الوصف وحصول ما يضاد الوصف العقل، والآخر يعرف ذلك فيه بالحس. أما ما يعرف ذلك فيه بالعقل فهو أن الكافر يعتقد وجوب عبادة الصنم ويباشر ذلك بجوارحه يريد حصول ذلك كله على صفة الحسن دون القبيح ومعلوم دون أن حصول ذلك على ما يضاد الحسن وهو القبح لا على الحسن الذي قصده. وأما ما يعرف ذلك فيه بالحس فإن الإنسان يتأذى بالمشي الدائم ويتألم بالقيام الممتد اللازم، وكذا بكل فعل ثابر المرء على اكتسابه وواظب على ارتكابه، ولا شك أن الفعل لا يقصد إليه الفاعل ليتألم به ويتأذى، ومع هذا حصل مؤذيًا متعبًا فصح ما ادعينا من خروج الفعل على ضد ما يقصده العبد من الوصف ما لم يقصده، فإذا لم يوجد على ذلك دل أن له موجد خرج الموجود على ما أراده. يحقق هذا أن خروج الكفر وعبادة الصنم على ما يقصده الكافر من الحسن وصوابًا وطاعة الله تعالى يتقرب بها إليه يضاد الحكمة وينافيها، وخروجه على ما خرج عليه من القبح مما يقتضيه التدبير الصائب والحكمة البالغة. وجوده على هذا الوصف وإن لم يقصده الكافر إما إن كان بالكافر أم بالفعل نفسه بموجب مختار تولى إيجاده عليه، فإن كان بالكافر أوجب ذا جواز حصول جميع الأفعال الحكمية ممن لا يقصد تحيلها، وذا يؤدي إلى القول بالطبائع والنجوم وهو فاسد على أن فساد ذلك متقرر في البداهة وإن لم يؤد ذلك إلى مذهب باطل. وإن كان بالفعل نفسه أوجب ذلك جواز وجود جميع الأفعال الحكمية من السماوات والأرضين بلا موجد قصد إيجادها وتحصيلها، وذا محال.
As for the testimony of reason itself that the servant does not have creative power, it is that the acts of servants do not come out according to the description the servant intends for his act, but rather come out contrary to that description. If the servant had the power of invention and creation, he would bring it into existence according to the description he wants and intends. But since the act is not brought into existence in accordance with his desire, it indicates that the one who brings it into existence is other than him, so He made it an act for him according to the description that the Creator willed to bring it into existence and make it an act for the servant; and the servant's power is related to that existing thing according to the description that the Creator brought it into existence. The proof that the servant's act comes out contrary to the description he intends and occurs with a description he does not intend—rather he intends the opposite—are two matters: one is known by reason as the impossibility of obtaining the description he intended and the occurrence of the opposite description; the other is known in it by sense. As for what is known by reason, it is that the disbeliever believes in the obligation of worshipping the idol and performs that with his limbs, wanting all that to occur with the attribute of good, not evil; and it is known without that that occurrence is contrary to good, i.e., evil, not the good he intended. As for what is known by sense, it is that a person is harmed by continuous walking and pained by prolonged standing, and likewise every act that one persists in and continues in. There is no doubt that the agent does not intend the act to cause him pain and harm, yet it occurs as harmful and tiring. So what we claimed is confirmed: that the act comes out contrary to the description the servant intends, not what he intended. So if it does not occur according to that, it indicates that it has a creator who brought the existing thing into existence according to what He willed. This is verified by the fact that the occurrence of disbelief and idol-worship according to what the disbeliever intends—good, correctness, and obedience to God Most High by which he seeks nearness—contradicts wisdom and is incompatible with it; and its occurrence as it did, with evil, is what sound planning and perfect wisdom require. Its existence with this description, even if the disbeliever did not intend it, is either from the disbeliever or from the act itself, by a free agent who undertook to bring it into existence. If it is from the disbeliever, it necessitates the permissibility of the occurrence of all volitional acts from one who does not intend their attainment, and that leads to the theory of natures and stars, which is corrupt; indeed its corruption is self-evident, even if it does not lead to a false doctrine. And if it is from the act itself, it necessitates the possibility of the existence of all volitional acts from the heavens and the earths without a creator who intended to bring them into existence and obtain them, and that is impossible.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage presents a rational proof that the servant does not have creative power (qudrat al-takhliq). The author argues that the acts of servants do not come out according to the description the servant intends, but rather contrary to it. If the servant had the power to invent and create, he would bring the act into existence according to his intended description. Since this does not happen, it shows that the true creator is other than the servant. The proof is based on two indicators: reason and sense. By reason: the disbeliever intends his worship of the idol as good and obedient, but in reality it is evil—therefore his intention is not realized. By sense: a person does not intend to harm himself by continuous walking or standing, yet pain occurs—so the act's harmful quality is not from his intention. The author then deepens the argument: if the act's evil quality is not from the servant, it must be from either the servant, the act itself, or a free agent. Attributing it to the servant leads to accepting that volitional acts can occur without intention, which leads to the corrupt theories of natures and stars. Attributing it to the act itself leads to the absurdity that all things could exist without a creator. Therefore, the only sound conclusion is that a free agent (God) brings the act into existence with its description.

Key Terms
قدرة التخليق
الاختراع والإيجاد
الوصف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The belief that the servant creates his own actions because he has power (qudra) over them.
Correction: The servant's power is not creative; it is a capacity to act that is dependent on God's creation of the action. This passage shows that if the servant were creative, his actions would always match his intention.

Checkpoint
What is the main evidence that the servant does not have creative power?
A) The servant sometimes fails to act
B) The servant's acts occur contrary to his intention
C) The servant's acts are always evil
D) The servant's power is limited

Key Takeaway
The central argument is that the discrepancy between intention and outcome proves the servant is not the true creator of his actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a recent moment when you intended to do something perfectly—perhaps a good deed or a task—but the outcome fell short or turned out differently. Who was truly in control of that outcome? How does this passage challenge your hidden belief that you are the master of your own actions?
?
If you genuinely believe that every action you perform is created by Allah and only acquired by you, how would that change the way you pray, ask for forgiveness, or rely on Him throughout your day? Are you willing to admit that you create nothing?
?
The argument shows that even your best intentions cannot guarantee the outcome. What does this reveal about your need for Allah’s mercy and guidance in every moment? Will you now turn to Him as the true creator of your deeds and ask Him to grant you good outcomes?

Two Proofs: Reason and Experience
Al-Nasafi presents two indicators: rational and empirical, showing the servant's act occurs contrary to his intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two specific proofs—rational and empirical—that demonstrate the servant's act occurs contrary to his intention, reinforcing that the true agent is other than the servant.

Core Idea
Both reason and sense experience confirm that our actions do not follow our intentions.

After establishing the main argument, Imam al-Nasafi now provides two concrete proofs to support it. The first is a rational proof: the disbeliever intends his worship as good, yet it is evil. The second is an empirical proof: a person does not intend to harm himself by continuous actions, yet harm occurs. Both prove that the act's description is not from the servant.

Guided Path
1
Read the rational proof
Read the part about the disbeliever worshipping the idol. He intends it as good and obedience, but it is evil. This demonstrates that his intention is not realized.
The author uses the example of the disbeliever to show that even with clear intention, the act's moral quality contradicts intention.
2
Read the empirical proof
Read the part about continuous walking and standing causing pain. The agent does not intend the pain, yet it occurs. This sense experience proves the same point.
3
Compare the two proofs
Notice that one is based on rational judgment (the disbeliever's intention is not fulfilled) and the other on sensory experience (pain occurs un-intended). Together they cover both realms of knowledge.
4
Understand the conclusion
Both proofs lead to the conclusion that the act is not brought about by the servant according to his intention, so there must be another agent who creates it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما شهادة نفس العقل أن العبد ليست له قدرة التخليق فهي أن أفعال العباد لا تخرج على ما يقصده العبد من الوصف لفعله بل تخرج على ما يضاد ذلك الوصف ولو كان العبد له قدرة الاختراع والإيجاد لأوجده على ما يريده من الوصف ويقصده، وحيث لم يوجد الفعل على وفق مراده، دل أن الموجد لذلك غيره فجعله فعلاً له على الوصف الذي شاء الموجد أن يوجده ويجعله فعلاً للعبد، والعبد تتعلق قدرته بذلك الموجود على الوصف الذي أوجده الموجد. ودليل خروج فعل العبد عن الوصف الذي يقصده العبد وحصوله على وصف لا يقصده، بل يقصد ضده أمران أحدهما ما يعرف امتناع حصول ما قصده من الوصف وحصول ما يضاد الوصف العقل، والآخر يعرف ذلك فيه بالحس. أما ما يعرف ذلك فيه بالعقل فهو أن الكافر يعتقد وجوب عبادة الصنم ويباشر ذلك بجوارحه يريد حصول ذلك كله على صفة الحسن دون القبيح ومعلوم دون أن حصول ذلك على ما يضاد الحسن وهو القبح لا على الحسن الذي قصده. وأما ما يعرف ذلك فيه بالحس فإن الإنسان يتأذى بالمشي الدائم ويتألم بالقيام الممتد اللازم، وكذا بكل فعل ثابر المرء على اكتسابه وواظب على ارتكابه، ولا شك أن الفعل لا يقصد إليه الفاعل ليتألم به ويتأذى، ومع هذا حصل مؤذيًا متعبًا فصح ما ادعينا من خروج الفعل على ضد ما يقصده العبد من الوصف ما لم يقصده، فإذا لم يوجد على ذلك دل أن له موجد خرج الموجود على ما أراده. يحقق هذا أن خروج الكفر وعبادة الصنم على ما يقصده الكافر من الحسن وصوابًا وطاعة الله تعالى يتقرب بها إليه يضاد الحكمة وينافيها، وخروجه على ما خرج عليه من القبح مما يقتضيه التدبير الصائب والحكمة البالغة. وجوده على هذا الوصف وإن لم يقصده الكافر إما إن كان بالكافر أم بالفعل نفسه بموجب مختار تولى إيجاده عليه، فإن كان بالكافر أوجب ذا جواز حصول جميع الأفعال الحكمية ممن لا يقصد تحيلها، وذا يؤدي إلى القول بالطبائع والنجوم وهو فاسد على أن فساد ذلك متقرر في البداهة وإن لم يؤد ذلك إلى مذهب باطل. وإن كان بالفعل نفسه أوجب ذلك جواز وجود جميع الأفعال الحكمية من السماوات والأرضين بلا موجد قصد إيجادها وتحصيلها، وذا محال.
As for the testimony of reason itself that the servant does not have creative power, it is that the acts of servants do not come out according to the description the servant intends for his act, but rather come out contrary to that description. If the servant had the power of invention and creation, he would bring it into existence according to the description he wants and intends. But since the act is not brought into existence in accordance with his desire, it indicates that the one who brings it into existence is other than him, so He made it an act for him according to the description that the Creator willed to bring it into existence and make it an act for the servant; and the servant's power is related to that existing thing according to the description that the Creator brought it into existence. The proof that the servant's act comes out contrary to the description he intends and occurs with a description he does not intend—rather he intends the opposite—are two matters: one is known by reason as the impossibility of obtaining the description he intended and the occurrence of the opposite description; the other is known in it by sense. As for what is known by reason, it is that the disbeliever believes in the obligation of worshipping the idol and performs that with his limbs, wanting all that to occur with the attribute of good, not evil; and it is known without that that occurrence is contrary to good, i.e., evil, not the good he intended. As for what is known by sense, it is that a person is harmed by continuous walking and pained by prolonged standing, and likewise every act that one persists in and continues in. There is no doubt that the agent does not intend the act to cause him pain and harm, yet it occurs as harmful and tiring. So what we claimed is confirmed: that the act comes out contrary to the description the servant intends, not what he intended. So if it does not occur according to that, it indicates that it has a creator who brought the existing thing into existence according to what He willed. This is verified by the fact that the occurrence of disbelief and idol-worship according to what the disbeliever intends—good, correctness, and obedience to God Most High by which he seeks nearness—contradicts wisdom and is incompatible with it; and its occurrence as it did, with evil, is what sound planning and perfect wisdom require. Its existence with this description, even if the disbeliever did not intend it, is either from the disbeliever or from the act itself, by a free agent who undertook to bring it into existence. If it is from the disbeliever, it necessitates the permissibility of the occurrence of all volitional acts from one who does not intend their attainment, and that leads to the theory of natures and stars, which is corrupt; indeed its corruption is self-evident, even if it does not lead to a false doctrine. And if it is from the act itself, it necessitates the possibility of the existence of all volitional acts from the heavens and the earths without a creator who intended to bring them into existence and obtain them, and that is impossible.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage presents a rational proof that the servant does not have creative power (qudrat al-takhliq). The author argues that the acts of servants do not come out according to the description the servant intends, but rather contrary to it. If the servant had the power to invent and create, he would bring the act into existence according to his intended description. Since this does not happen, it shows that the true creator is other than the servant. The proof is based on two indicators: reason and sense. By reason: the disbeliever intends his worship of the idol as good and obedient, but in reality it is evil—therefore his intention is not realized. By sense: a person does not intend to harm himself by continuous walking or standing, yet pain occurs—so the act's harmful quality is not from his intention. The author then deepens the argument: if the act's evil quality is not from the servant, it must be from either the servant, the act itself, or a free agent. Attributing it to the servant leads to accepting that volitional acts can occur without intention, which leads to the corrupt theories of natures and stars. Attributing it to the act itself leads to the absurdity that all things could exist without a creator. Therefore, the only sound conclusion is that a free agent (God) brings the act into existence with its description.

Key Terms
الحسن
القبيح
الحس
العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The belief that if a person intends an act, the outcome is always in line with that intention.
Correction: Both rational and empirical evidence show that outcomes often contradict intentions, so the true agent is not the person.

Checkpoint
What is the empirical proof that the servant's act occurs contrary to his intention?
A) The disbeliever's worship is evil despite intention
B) Continuous walking causes pain, which is not intended
C) The heavens and earth exist without a creator
D) The servant's power is limited to certain acts

Key Takeaway
The two proofs—rational and empirical—together demonstrate that the actual description of an act does not originate from the servant's intention.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of an action you intended as good but which brought about harm or was judged otherwise by others. Who truly determined its outcome, and what does that reveal about relying solely on your own intention?
?
When you persist in a good deed and feel exhausted or burdened, do you attribute that pain to your own effort or to the One who created the act? How might acknowledging His control transform your worship?
?
The disbeliever assumed his idol worship was good based on his intention. What actions in your life do you assume are good simply because you intend them, without examining their actual description against revelation? Are you willing to let go of that assumption?

Refuting Alternatives: The True Origin of the Act's Description
Al-Nasafi refutes alternative sources for the act's description, affirming it comes from God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the deeper analysis where the author refutes the possibilities that the act's description comes from the servant or from the act itself, proving it must come from God.

Core Idea
The evil of the disbeliever's act cannot be from him or from the act itself—only from God's wisdom.

Imam al-Nasafi now strengthens the argument by considering alternatives: if the act's bad quality is not from the servant's intention, it could be from the servant, the act itself, or a free agent. He systematically refutes the first two possibilities, showing they lead to absurdities, leaving only the conclusion that God creates the act with its description according to His perfect wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dilemma
The disbeliever's act of worship is evil, but he intended it as good. The evil description must come from somewhere: either from the disbeliever, from the act itself, or from a free agent.
2
Refutation of the first alternative
If the evil description came from the disbeliever, it would allow for volitional acts to occur without intention, leading to the corrupt theory of natures and stars.
The author says this is self-evidently false.
3
Refutation of the second alternative
If it came from the act itself, it would allow for acts in the heavens and earth to exist without a creator, which is impossible.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The only remaining possibility is that a free agent (God) brings the act into existence with its description, consistent with His wisdom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

B) It would lead to the theory of natures and stars

?
If God's wisdom requires even the evil of disbelief to be created by Him, can you still claim that your small transgressions are merely 'accidental' or 'outside His plan'? How will you respond to the accountability this places on you?
?
This lesson argues that attributing evil to the doer or the act itself leads to absurd consequences. Are you willing to submit your understanding of good and evil entirely to God's wisdom, even when you cannot see the reason? What step will you take today to accept His sovereignty over your actions?

Accidents: Foundation for Proving World's Temporality
Logical argument: accidents prove bodies' temporality; if not from God, proof fails.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why accidents are essential to prove that bodies (and thus the world) are temporal, and the consequence of denying that God creates accidents.

Core Idea
Without accidents as divine creations, the proof for the world's temporality collapses.

This passage presents a critical link: knowledge of bodies' temporality comes through accidents. If accidents are not created by God, then God Himself would not have established this proof, leaving bodies as the only alternative. The author warns that such a view undermines the entire argument for a Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the first part of the source: from 'ثم العلم بحدوث الأجسام' to 'وهو الأجسام'. Notice the logical chain: bodies' temporality is known through accidents.
Focus on the structure: condition (if accidents not created) leads to conclusion (proof fails).
2
Trace the logical argument
Identify the premise: knowledge of bodies' temporality depends on accidents. Then the conditional: if accidents are not created by God, then God cannot prove the world's temporality. Instead, bodies themselves would have to provide the proof.
This reverses the normal order: accidents prove bodies, not the other way.
3
Reflect on the theological stake
Consider why this matters: the proof of a Creator hinges on the temporality of the world. If that proof fails, the argument for God's existence is weakened. The author insists that only God can create accidents, so denying that is a serious error.
This connects to broader discussions in kalam about causality and divine action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم العلم بحدوث الأجسام يحصل بمعرفة حدوث الأعراض، والأعراض ليست بمخلوقة الله فلم يكن الله تعالى مثبتاً دلالة حدوث العالم ولا قادرًا على إثباته. وإنما أثبت ذلك غيره وهو الأجسام، وكذلك ما أثبت الرسول دلالة الصدق إذ ما يثبت في العصا من الجيئة والذهاب، وفي اليد من النور، وفي الماء من الانفلاق، وفي الميت من الحياة، وفي الأكمة والأبرص من البرء، وفي الخشب من الحنين، وفي الشاه المسمومة من الكلام كل ذلك أعراض لا صنع الله تعالى فيها، والقول به كفر.
Then knowledge of the temporality of bodies is obtained by knowing the temporality of accidents. But if accidents are not created by God, then God has not established the proof of the world's temporality, nor is He able to prove it. Rather, something else established that, namely bodies. Similarly, the Messenger did not establish the proof of truthfulness, for what appears in the staff of coming and going, in the hand of light, in the water of splitting, in the dead of life, in the blind and leper of healing, in the wood of yearning, in the poisoned sheep of speech — all of that are accidents in which God has no act, and holding that view is disbelief.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage explains a critical consequence of denying that accidents are created by God. The proof for the temporality of bodies (and thus the existence of a Creator) depends on the temporality of accidents. If accidents are not created by God, then this proof fails, and God would not have established it. Moreover, the miracles of the prophets (like Moses' staff, Jesus healing the blind, etc.) are accidents; if they are not created by God, they cannot serve as proofs of prophethood. The author asserts that such a view is kufr (disbelief).

Key Terms
الأعراض
حدوث الأجسام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof for God's existence does not rely on accidents being created by God.
Correction: According to this passage, the standard proof for the world's temporality (and thus a Creator) depends entirely on accidents being temporal and created by God. Without that, the proof collapses.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if accidents are not created by God?
A) The world's temporality becomes easier to prove.
B) God cannot prove the world's temporality.
C) Bodies provide the proof instead.
D) Miracles become stronger proofs.

Key Takeaway
Accidents are the linchpin for proving the world's temporality; denying they are from God destroys the proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the entire proof for the world's temporality depends on accidents being created by God, and you personally ever attribute sudden events to 'luck' or 'coincidence', does that not undermine your own confidence in this argument? Will you actively remind yourself today that even the smallest changes are from Allah?
?
This passage shows that without divine creation of accidents, God Himself would be powerless to prove the world's temporality. Does your faith rest on arguments that you understand deeply, or have you passively accepted them? Will you commit to studying this proof until you can defend it with clarity?
?
If a skeptic asked you why accidents cannot be self-generated or eternally recurring, what from this passage would you say? Are you ready to give an answer, or do you realize you may be relying on a foundation you have not fully examined?

Miracles as Accidents: Defending Prophethood
Argument that miracles are accidents; denying divine origin of miracles is disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why miracles, being accidents, must be created by God to serve as proofs of prophethood, and why the opposite view is considered disbelief.

Core Idea
Miracles are accidents; if not from God, they lose their evidentiary power and the view becomes kufr.

The author extends the same logic to prophethood. The miracles performed by prophets—like Moses' staff turning into a snake, Jesus healing the blind—are accidents. If these are not created by God, they cannot be signs of truthfulness. To hold that they are not from God is a grave error, amounting to disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the second part: from 'وكذلك ما أثبت الرسول' to the end. Identify the list of miracles mentioned.
Notice that each miracle is described as an accident (e.g., coming and going in the staff, light in the hand, etc.).
2
Understand the parallel argument
The author draws a parallel: just as accidents are necessary for proving the world's temporality, they are also necessary for proving prophethood. If miracles are not from God, they cannot be proof, and claiming otherwise is disbelief.
The phrase 'والقول به كفر' is emphatic.
3
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider why this matters: prophethood is proven through miracles. If miracles are not divine, then prophethood cannot be verified. The author safeguards the divine origin of miracles as a core belief.
This reinforces the Ash'ari/Maturidi view that God creates all actions, including miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم العلم بحدوث الأجسام يحصل بمعرفة حدوث الأعراض، والأعراض ليست بمخلوقة الله فلم يكن الله تعالى مثبتاً دلالة حدوث العالم ولا قادرًا على إثباته. وإنما أثبت ذلك غيره وهو الأجسام، وكذلك ما أثبت الرسول دلالة الصدق إذ ما يثبت في العصا من الجيئة والذهاب، وفي اليد من النور، وفي الماء من الانفلاق، وفي الميت من الحياة، وفي الأكمة والأبرص من البرء، وفي الخشب من الحنين، وفي الشاه المسمومة من الكلام كل ذلك أعراض لا صنع الله تعالى فيها، والقول به كفر.
Then knowledge of the temporality of bodies is obtained by knowing the temporality of accidents. But if accidents are not created by God, then God has not established the proof of the world's temporality, nor is He able to prove it. Rather, something else established that, namely bodies. Similarly, the Messenger did not establish the proof of truthfulness, for what appears in the staff of coming and going, in the hand of light, in the water of splitting, in the dead of life, in the blind and leper of healing, in the wood of yearning, in the poisoned sheep of speech — all of that are accidents in which God has no act, and holding that view is disbelief.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage explains a critical consequence of denying that accidents are created by God. The proof for the temporality of bodies (and thus the existence of a Creator) depends on the temporality of accidents. If accidents are not created by God, then this proof fails, and God would not have established it. Moreover, the miracles of the prophets (like Moses' staff, Jesus healing the blind, etc.) are accidents; if they are not created by God, they cannot serve as proofs of prophethood. The author asserts that such a view is kufr (disbelief).

Key Terms
الأعراض
دلالة الصدق
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are not accidents; they are acts of prophets themselves.
Correction: In kalam, miracles are considered accidents (temporal events) that God creates through prophets as signs. They are not acts of the prophets themselves.

Checkpoint
What does the author say about those who claim that miracles are not created by God?
A) They are mistaken but not disbelievers.
B) They are guilty of disbelief (kufr).
C) They have a valid theological position.
D) They are considered heretics but not disbelievers.

Key Takeaway
Miracles are accidents that must be created by God; denying this is disbelief because it undermines the proof of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever attributed a miracle (like a healing or an extraordinary event) to luck, nature, or coincidence rather than to God’s direct act? How does the statement 'كل ذلك أعراض' challenge you to see every event, no matter how rare, as created by God?
?
If you truly believed that every accident—including every miracle in history—is created by God and not by any other cause, how would that reshape your daily gratitude, fear, and reliance on Allah? Are there areas of your life where you still act as if things happen without His creation?
?
The author says that denying God’s role in miracles is kufr. Examine your own heart: is there any miracle mentioned in the Quran or authentic hadith (like the splitting of the sea or the Prophet’s healing of the blind) that you have subconsciously dismissed as exaggeration or metaphor? Confront that doubt now and align your belief with the source.

The Effect of Human Power Through Acquisition
Imam al-Nasafi refutes the objection that if God alone creates, human power is vain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi response to the objection that human power would be idle, showing that power attaches to the act through acquisition (kasb) without requiring invention.

Core Idea
Human power is not idle—it makes the act the servant's through acquisition.

Imam al-Nasafi now addresses a key objection: if God alone creates, what does human power do? The objection claims it would be idle. The answer is nuanced: the servant does have an act that is his acquired power, and power attaches without invention. This passage clarifies the role of human choice and the effect of power through a detailed categorization of divine invention.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and initial answer
Read the first few lines: the objection that human power becomes idle, and the initial response affirming that a proof has established the servant's act and that power attaches without invention.
Notice that the author does not reject the objection outright but builds on previous proofs.
2
Understand the role of the two proofs
The author mentions 'the combination of the two proofs' (God's sole creation and human accountability). Reflect on how these together show that power attaches without invention.
3
Analyze the three categories of invention
The passage distinguishes: (1) what God invents in non-choosing things, (2) what He invents in choosers that are not subject to their power, and (3) what He invents in choosers by their choice and within their power. Identify how each case affects whether the act is attributed to the servant.
This is the core of the argument.
4
Grasp the effect of acquisition
Focus on the third category: although God invents the act, the servant's power makes it his act. This is the meaning of kasb. Understand that the author calls this explanation 'elaboration' but insists the proofs suffice.
Compare with the Ash'ari view mentioned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: لو استحال ذلك لبطل تعلق قدرة العبد بشيء وتعطلت قدرته. قلنا: وقد أقمنا الدليل على أن العبد له فعل هو مقدوره فجيب الانقياد للدليل وإثبات الفعل للعبد وإن لم يخترعه، وثبت بمجموع الدليلين جواز تعلق القدرة لا بجهة الاختراع. ثم نقول: ما يخترعه الله تعالى فيما لا اختيار له لا يكون فعلاً له فيكون مخلوق الله تعالى ومفعوله لا فعله ولا فعل غيره عندنا، وعند الأشعرية والنجارية يكون فعل الله تعالى لأنه مفعوله والفعل والمفعول واحد، وما يخترعه فيمن له الاختيار، إن كان ذلك الشيء مما لا يتعلق به قدرة المحل فهو أيضا ليس بفعل للعبد بل العبد محله لا غير، وما يخترعه فيه باختيار العبد ذلك وله عليه قدرة فأثر تعلق قدرته به كونه فعلاً، فيكون الله تعالى مخترعا فعل العبد باختياره لولا اختيار العبد وقصده اكتسابه لما خلقه الله تعالى فعلا له فأثر قدرته كون ذلك المخترع فعلاً له، هذا عن جهة التبرع مع أنا لا حاجة بنا إلى بيان ذلك على ما بينا من أن وجوب اتباع الدليلين يقتضي ما قلنا، والله الموفق.
If they say: If that were impossible, then the attachment of the servant's power to anything would be invalidated and his power would be idle. We say: We have established the proof that the servant has an act that is his acquired power, so it is necessary to submit to the proof and affirm the act for the servant even if he does not invent it, and it is established by the combination of the two proofs the possibility of the attachment of power without the aspect of invention. Then we say: What Allah invents in that which has no choice is not an act for it, so it is Allah's creation and effect, not His act nor another's act according to us, while according to the Ash'aris and Najjariyya it is Allah's act because it is His effect, and the act and the effect are one. And what He invents in one who has choice: if that thing is something that the power of the locus does not attach to, then it is also not an act of the servant; rather the servant is its locus, nothing else. And what He invents in it by the servant's choice and he has power over it, then the effect of the attachment of his power to it is its being an act, so Allah is the inventor of the servant's act by his choice; were it not for the servant's choice and intention and acquisition, Allah would not have created it as an act for him. So the effect of his power is that invented thing being an act for him. This is from the perspective of elaboration, though we have no need to explain this given what we have clarified that the obligation to follow the two proofs necessitates what we said. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. The objection states that if it were impossible for human power to produce an effect (as Maturidis hold regarding invention), then human power would be attached to nothing and be idle. The response has several parts. First, the author reaffirms that a proof has already been established showing that the servant does have an act that is his acquired power (maqdūr), so one must submit to that proof. The combination of two proofs (probably the proof of God's sole creation and the proof of human accountability) shows that power can attach to an act without the aspect of invention (ikhtirā'). Second, the author distinguishes categories: what God invents in non-choosing things (e.g., minerals) is not an act for that thing; it is God's creation. The Ash'aris and Najjariyya call it God's act because they identify act and effect. For beings with choice (like humans), if the thing invented is not subject to the power of the locus (the human), then it is not the human's act; the human is merely a locus. But if the human chooses it and has power over it, then the attachment of his power makes it his act: God invents the act in the human, but only because of the human's choice and acquisition (kasb) – otherwise God would not create it as his act. Thus, the servant's power's effect is that the invented thing becomes his act. The author notes this is an elaboration (tabarru') and that the main point is that the two proofs necessitate this conclusion. The passage guards against misunderstanding that human power is meaningless; it has a real effect (making the act the servant's) without requiring invention.

Key Terms
قدرة
فعل
مقدور
اختراع
اكتساب
محل
كسب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That if God creates all actions, human power has no real effect and is idle.
Correction: The passage shows that human power does have a real effect: it makes the act the servant's through acquisition (kasb), even though God invents it.

Checkpoint
The answer to the objection establishes that the servant's power attaches to his act by what aspect?
A) invention (ikhtirā')
B) acquisition (kasb)
C) direct creation
D) coercion (jabr)

Key Takeaway
Human power has a real effect: through acquisition, it makes an act invented by God become the servant's own act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage teaches that your action becomes truly yours through your choice and intention, even though God invents it. Are you aware, when you act, that your power is not creating the act but making it yours? How does that change your sense of ownership of your deeds? Will you start acknowledging your responsibility more deeply today?
?
The objectors thought human power would be idle if God alone creates. But you have power that attaches to your choices. When you sin, do you still claim it as your act, or do you excuse yourself by saying God created it? What does this passage demand of you? Are you willing to stop evading responsibility and own your sins before God?
?
The servant's choice and intention 'cause' God to create the act as his. Your intentions matter so much that they determine whether an action is yours. Are you conscious, moment by moment, that your intentions are shaping the moral ownership of your actions before God? How can you live more intentionally starting right now?

The Two Proofs: God as Creator, Servant as Acquirer
Conclusion of two proofs and rebuttal of objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the combined two proofs establish that God is the powerful inventor and the servant is the acting acquirer with choice, and why objections that challenge this are invalid.

Core Idea
The two proofs together necessitate both divine power and human acquisition.

The author now states the conclusion drawn from the two preceding proofs. He affirms that God is the powerful inventor and the servant is the agent and acquirer with choice. He also addresses a potential objection, showing that since the proofs are certain, any question that would invalidate them is itself invalid.

Guided Path
1
Read the conclusion passage
Read the Arabic text once to grasp the author's main point. Then compare with the translation.
Notice the concise style; every word carries weight.
2
Identify the two conclusions
The passage affirms two things: God as powerful inventor, and the servant as agent/acquirer. Write them down.
These are the 'two aspects' mentioned later.
3
Understand the rebuttal
The author argues that any objection invalidating one aspect is itself invalid because the proofs are certain. Reflect on why certainty protects against objections.
4
Relate to the bigger picture
Consider how this conclusion sets the stage for the detailed response in the next passage.
The objection might be about God's will and human freedom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مجموع الدليلين موجبًا كونه تعالى قادرًا مخترعًا، وكون العبد فاعلاً مكتسبًا مختارا. وما قلتم من السؤال يوجب بطلان أحد هذين الوجهين، وما ثبت بالدليل المتيقن غير محتمل للبطلان، فإذا كان السؤال في نفسه باطلاً. ثم نقول: إن كان الله تعالى أراد الحركة الضرورية من العبد فيخلقه ولا يكون للعبد قدرة الامتناع والله تعالى قادر والعبد مضطر، وإن أراد تخليق الحركة الاختيارية فالعبد لا يتصور منه الامتناع لأنه تعالى إنما يخلق تلك الحركة إذا أرادها العبد واختار وقصد اكتسابها فيخلق الله تعالى لا محالة لإجرائه العادة في تخليقه عند وجود قصد العهد لا لكونه ملجأ إلى ذلك، على أن الله تعالى إذا كان يخلقه مقارنا لقدرة العبد كيف يتصور منه الامتناع عن الفعل وهو موجود والامتناع عن الموجود محال، والله الموفق.
The sum of the two proofs necessitates that He, exalted, is powerful and inventive, and that the servant is an agent, an acquirer, and choiceful. And what you have said of the question necessitates the invalidity of one of these two aspects, and what is established by certain proof is not susceptible to invalidity, so the question is in itself invalid. Then we say: If God, exalted, willed the necessary movement from the servant, He creates it and the servant has no power of prevention, and God is powerful and the servant is compelled; and if He willed the creation of the voluntary movement, then prevention from the servant is inconceivable because He only creates that movement when the servant wills it, chooses it, and intends to acquire it, so God creates it necessarily because His habit continues in creating it when the servant's intention exists, not because He is compelled to that. Moreover, if God creates it concomitant with the servant's power, how can prevention from the act be conceived while it is existent? For prevention of the existent is impossible. And God grants success.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage concludes a previous proof and responds to an objection. The author first states that the combined effect of the two proofs (argued earlier) is that God is the powerful inventor and the servant is the acting acquirer with choice. Any objection that would invalidate one of these two aspects is itself invalid because the proofs are certain. Then the author addresses a possible objection concerning God's will and the servant's ability to prevent. If God wills a necessary movement (e.g., of a limb), He creates it and the servant cannot refrain—God is powerful, the servant compelled. If God wills to create a voluntary movement, the servant cannot refrain either because this movement is only created when the servant wills and intends it; God creates it habitually, not out of compulsion. Since God creates it concurrent with the servant's power, refraining from an existing act is impossible. This supports the harmony between divine power and human acquisition.

Key Terms
دليل
قادر
مخترع
مكتسب
مختار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that divine power negates human agency.
Correction: The author shows that the two proofs together affirm both, and objections that deny one are invalid.

Checkpoint
What do the two proofs together necessitate according to the author?
A) Only God's power
B) Only human free will
C) Both God's power and human acquisition
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The two certain proofs establish both divine creation and human acquisition, and any objection to either is invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if God is the Creator of your every action, while also taking full responsibility for your choices? Which area of your life do you most often blame circumstances or others instead of owning your own acquisition?
?
When you reflect on the balance between divine power and your own free will, does it lead you to rely more on God or to feel burdened by responsibility? How can you strengthen both tawakkul and personal accountability in your daily decisions?
?
The passage declares any objection that invalidates a certain proof to be itself invalid. Are there any certain truths from revelation that you have doubted because they seemed hard to reconcile with your own reasoning? What would it take for you to submit completely to that certainty?

God's Will and Human Prevention: Necessary vs Voluntary Movements
Detailed reply distinguishing necessary and voluntary movements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why, under God's will, the servant cannot prevent necessary movements and cannot prevent voluntary movements due to the habit of creation.

Core Idea
Whether necessary or voluntary, God's will ensures the act occurs; prevention is impossible.

After establishing the conclusion, the author delves into a detailed response to the objection concerning God's will and human prevention. He distinguishes between necessary movements and voluntary movements, explaining why in both cases the servant cannot refrain from the act.

Guided Path
1
Read the detailed response
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting the two cases presented. Use the translation to clarify.
The passage has a conditional structure: 'if ... then ...'
2
Analyze the first case: necessary movement
For necessary movement, God creates it and the servant has no power of prevention. The servant is compelled. Understand this.
3
Analyze the second case: voluntary movement
For voluntary movement, the servant cannot prevent because God creates it only when the servant intends. This is due to God's habit, not compulsion.
Note the phrase 'لا لكونه ملجأ' (not because He is compelled).
4
Consider the final argument
The author adds that since God creates the act concurrent with the servant's power, preventing an existent act is impossible. Reflect on the logic.

The Non-Existent as a Thing: Mu'tazila Error
Author refutes Mu'tazila claim that non-existent is a thing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila claim that the non-existent is a thing leads to absurdities and undermines divine and human agency.

Core Idea
Calling the non-existent a 'thing' destroys the basis for divine power and moral accountability.

The Mu'tazila asserted that the non-existent (al-ma'dum) is a thing with real attributes before existence. This might seem like a minor semantic point, but the author shows it unravels the entire fabric of Islamic theology: it denies God's power, affirms the pre-eternity of the world, and nullifies human acts and divine commands. Let's examine their claim and its devastating consequences.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila claim
Read the Arabic passage where the author states the Mu'tazila doctrine. Notice the terms: المعدوم شيء, عين, عرض, جوهر.
These terms indicate they consider the non-existent to have full ontological status.
2
Trace the author's argument
Follow the logical chain: if the non-existent is a thing with pre-eternal attributes, then power cannot relate to existence (since existence is not a separate meaning), leaving no relation of power at all.
This leads to تعطيل الصانع (nullification of the Maker).
3
Identify the consequences
List the four consequences mentioned: nullifying God, pre-eternity of world, abolishing human acts, negating commands and promises.
These show the high stakes of the debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد بينا أنه معقول لقيام الدلائل العقلية عليه إلا أنه ليس بموهوم، ولو رفضت المعتزلة التعصب ونظرت بالعقل وانقادت للدليل وجانبت الهوى وأنصفت من نفسها لعرفت أنهم القائلون بما لا يعقل المستمسكون بما هو المحال الممتنع، وذلك أن من مذهب جمهورهم أن المعدوم شيء، وأكثرهم يزعمون أنه عين وعرض وجوهر قبل الحدوث وكذا سواد وحركة وذات على ما قررنا قبل هذا من بيان أقاويلهم. ثم قدرة الفاعل لا تتعلق إلا بالوجود ولا تعلق لها بالشيئية، ولا تكون حركة ولا سوادا ولا جوهرًا ولا ذاتاً ولا عينا لأن هذه الأوصاف كانت ثابتة في الأزل، ثم الوجود ليس بمعنى وراء الذات ولا تعلق للقدرة بالذات فلا يتصور تعلقها بالوجود إذ هو ليس معنى وراء الذات فإذا لا تعلق القدرة ما، لا للقدرة القديمة ولا للقدرة المحدثة بمقدور البتة، وفيه تعطيل الصانع والقول بقدم العالم، وإبطال ثبوت الفعل للعباد، وتعطيل الأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد، ونحن نقول: إن الله تعالى خلق العالم وجعل ما ليس بسواد ولا بياض ولا جوهر ولا عرض ولا موجود سوادًا وبياضا وجوهرًا وعرضًا وموجودًا ، ثم ما كان من ذلك أفعال العباد فوجوده وشيئيته متعلقة بقدرة الله تعالى وكونه حركة وسكونا وطاعة ومعصية متعلقة بقدرة العبد، وعندهم لا تتعلق شيئية بقدرة أحد ووجوده ليس بمعنى

والمكتسب هو المال ولذلك لا يوصف تعالى بالاكتساب وقد يكون من فعل العبد ما هو مكتسب إذا كان خيرًا أو شرًا اجتلبه بغيره من الأفعال، فأما أول أفعاله فلا يقال فيه إنه مكتسب وإنما يسمى اكتسابًا وقد يكون في أفعاله ما لا يكون اكتسابًا إذا لم يكتسب به نفعًا أو ضرا كحركات الطفل والنائم والساهي.. وكل هذا يبين من جهة اللغة أن المكتسب لابد من أن يكون فاعلاً ومحدثًا. ويقول عبد الجبار الرازي: وكل هذا يبين تجاهل المجبرة في قولهم: إن العبد يكتسب ولا يفعل، وإن هذا ينقض سائر ما يتعلقون به في باب العبادة عند فصلهم بين الكسب والفعل وكأنهم تجنبوا القول بأن الإنسان يفعل.

وراء الشيئية، فينبغي أن لا تتعلق قدرة العبد به فلم يمكنهم تعليق قدرة العبد إلا بقدر ما قلنا، فإذا قلنا بمثل ما قالوا ولم يبق بيننا خلاف إلا في العبارة فإنهم سموا ذلك خلقًا واختراعا، ونحن سميناه كسبًا إلا أن ما وراء ذلك عندنا متعلق بقدرة الله تعالى وعندهم لا يقدره أحد فاستوينا في جنبة العبد ولم يبق لهم علينا إشكال، وفيما وراء ذلك التحقوا بالدهرية والمعطلة، ونحن ثبنا على القول بثبوت الصانع بل هم أتوا بما هو غير المعقول وأبطلوا القول بتعلق القدرة بالمقدور، فإنهم أحالوا تعلقها إلا بالوجود والوجود راجع إلى الذات إذ هو ليس بمعنى وراء الذات ولا تعلق لها بالذات والشيئية فإن تعلقها بما لا تعلق لها به وهو محال وهذيان وبطل بهذا الفصل جميع قواعد المعتزلة وأضمحلت شبهاتهم، ونحن نحمد الله في غاية الوضوح.
We have explained that it is intelligible because rational proofs establish it, but it is not an imagination. If the Mu'tazila abandoned partisanship and looked with reason, submitted to the proof, avoided caprice, and were fair to themselves, they would know that they are those who say what is not intelligible, who cling to what is impossible and absurd. That is because the doctrine of the majority of them is that the non-existent is a thing, and most of them claim that it is an entity, an accident, a substance before coming into existence, and likewise blackness, motion, and essence, according to what we have set forth earlier in explaining their statements. Then the power of the agent relates only to existence and does not relate to thinghood; and it does not become motion, blackness, substance, essence, or entity because these attributes were established in pre-eternity. Then existence is not a meaning beyond essence, so power does not relate to essence; thus its relation to existence cannot be conceived because it is not a meaning beyond essence. So there is no relation of power at all—neither for eternal power nor for temporal power to any potential (maqdur) whatsoever. In this is the nullification of the Maker, the statement of the pre-eternity of the world, the abolition of the establishment of the act of servants, and the nullification of command, prohibition, promise, and threat. And we say: God Almighty created the world and made what is not blackness, whiteness, substance, accident, or existent into blackness, whiteness, substance, accident, and existent. Then whatever of that is the acts of servants, its existence and its thinghood are related to the power of God Almighty, and its being motion, rest, obedience, or disobedience is related to the power of the servant. According to them, thinghood is not related to anyone's power, and its existence is not a meaning beyond thinghood. The acquired (al-muktasab) is property, and therefore the Exalted is not described as acquiring. There may be from the act of the servant what is acquired if it is good or evil that is sought through other acts. As for the first of his acts, it is not called 'acquired'; it is only called 'acquisition' (iktisab). There may be in his acts what is not acquisition if no benefit or harm is acquired through it, like the movements of a child, the sleeping person, and the inattentive person. All this makes clear from the linguistic perspective that the acquirer must be a doer and an originator. And 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Razi says: "All this shows the ignorance of the Jabriya in their statement that the servant acquires but does not act, and that this contradicts everything else they cling to in the chapter of worship when they distinguish between kasb and fi'l; it is as if they avoided saying that man acts." Beyond thinghood, it is necessary that the servant's power does not relate to it; they could not relate the servant's power except to the extent we said. So when we say what they said, no difference remains between us except in expression: they call it creation (khalq) and invention (ikhtira'), while we call it acquisition (kasb). But what is beyond that is, according to us, related to the power of God Almighty, while according to them, no one has power over it. So we are equal regarding the servant, and no objection remains for them against us. In what is beyond that, they align with the Dahriyya and the Mu'attila. We, on the other hand, adhere to the affirmation of the Maker, but they have brought what is irrational and invalidated the statement that power relates to the potential (maqdur). For they considered it impossible for power to relate except to existence, but existence returns to essence since it is not a meaning beyond essence; and power does not relate to essence and thinghood. So its relation to what it does not relate to is impossible, nonsense. With this chapter, all the principles of the Mu'tazila have collapsed and their doubts have vanished. We praise God for utmost clarity.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument refuting the Mu'tazila on the nature of the non-existent and divine/human power, followed by the author's own doctrine of acquisition. The passage begins by noting that the intelligibility of a thing is established by rational proofs, but the Mu'tazila have abandoned reason for partisanship. Their error is traced to the claim that the non-existent (ma'dum) is a thing, and even an entity, accident, substance, etc., before existence. The author then argues that power (qudra) of any agent relates only to existence, not to attributes like thinghood or essence that are pre-eternal. Since existence is not a separate meaning from essence, power cannot relate to existence either, leading to absurdities: denying God's power, claiming the world is pre-eternal, and nullifying human acts and moral commands. The Maturidi position is then stated: God creates the world and its properties, and the acts of servants have their existence and thinghood from God's power, but their specific qualities (motion, obedience, etc.) from the servant's power. The Mu'tazila deny thinghood from any power, contradicting themselves. The author then introduces a definition of 'al-muktasab' (the acquired), explaining that only the servant's subsequent acts are acquired, not the first act. A quote from the Mu'tazila scholar 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Razi criticizes the Maturidi distinction between kasb and fi'l. The author responds by arguing that the Mu'tazila's own view forces them to deny any power relation, but the Maturidi view accounts for all cases. The response concludes that the Mu'tazila have no real objection, and their position aligns with the Dahriyya and Mu'attila (deniers of God or attributes). The final conclusion is that the entire Mu'tazila system collapses, and God is praised for clarity.

Key Terms

القدرة
الشيئية
الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The non-existent (ma'dum) has reality as a 'thing' with attributes before coming into existence.
Correction: The non-existent is nothing; it has no attributes. Calling it a 'thing' leads to denying divine power and human accountability.

Checkpoint
What do the Mu'tazila claim about the non-existent (al-ma'dum) according to the author?
A) It is nothing and has no attributes.
B) It is a thing and even an entity, substance, etc., before existence.
C) It is only an accident after existence.
D) It is an imagination that cannot be conceived.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila claim that the non-existent is a thing leads to the absurd conclusion that no power—divine or human—can have any effect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you plan your day, do you treat your future actions as already decided and real, forgetting that only Allah's power brings them into being? This lesson exposes how the Mu'tazila fallacy subtly denies divine agency. Where in your life do you assume things are 'real' before they exist, and how can you repent from that?
?
The passage says that if the non-existent is a thing, then power relates to nothing. This means no one can truly act. Do you ever feel like your efforts are meaningless or that God's power is irrelevant to your daily choices? How does this lesson correct that?
?
The Mu'tazila error nullifies command and promise. Are there times when you treat Allah's commands as optional or His promises as uncertain, as if they have no real power? How can you reaffirm that Allah's words are effective and His power is absolute?

The Maturidi Theory of Acquisition (Kasb)
Author states Maturidi doctrine of acquisition and contrasts with Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi doctrine of acquisition (kasb) and how it distinguishes between divine creation of existence and human responsibility for moral qualities.

Core Idea
God creates the existence of acts; humans acquire their moral character through choice.

Having refuted the Mu'tazila position, the author now presents the Maturidi alternative: God creates the world and its properties, including the existence and thinghood of human acts. But the specific qualities—whether an act is motion, obedience, or sin—are related to the servant's power through acquisition (kasb). This distinction preserves divine omnipotence while affirming human accountability.

Guided Path
1
Read the Maturidi positive statement
Find the sentences beginning 'ونحن نقول' in the Arabic passage. Read them carefully.
Note the two parts: (1) God creates the existence and thinghood; (2) the servant's power relates to the specific quality.
2
Understand the definition of al-muktasab
The author defines 'the acquired' (al-muktasab) and gives examples. Note the linguistic argument.
Acquisition is only for subsequent acts, not the first act.
3
Compare with the Mu'tazila view
The author argues that the only difference between Maturidis and Mu'tazila is in terminology (khalq vs. kasb), but beyond that the Mu'tazila align with atheists.
This is a polemical simplification but highlights the key difference.

وقد بينا أنه معقول لقيام الدلائل العقلية عليه إلا أنه ليس بموهوم، ولو رفضت المعتزلة التعصب ونظرت بالعقل وانقادت للدليل وجانبت الهوى وأنصفت من نفسها لعرفت أنهم القائلون بما لا يعقل المستمسكون بما هو المحال الممتنع، وذلك أن من مذهب جمهورهم أن المعدوم شيء، وأكثرهم يزعمون أنه عين وعرض وجوهر قبل الحدوث وكذا سواد وحركة وذات على ما قررنا قبل هذا من بيان أقاويلهم. ثم قدرة الفاعل لا تتعلق إلا بالوجود ولا تعلق لها بالشيئية، ولا تكون حركة ولا سوادا ولا جوهرًا ولا ذاتاً ولا عينا لأن هذه الأوصاف كانت ثابتة في الأزل، ثم الوجود ليس بمعنى وراء الذات ولا تعلق للقدرة بالذات فلا يتصور تعلقها بالوجود إذ هو ليس معنى وراء الذات فإذا لا تعلق القدرة ما، لا للقدرة القديمة ولا للقدرة المحدثة بمقدور البتة، وفيه تعطيل الصانع والقول بقدم العالم، وإبطال ثبوت الفعل للعباد، وتعطيل الأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد، ونحن نقول: إن الله تعالى خلق العالم وجعل ما ليس بسواد ولا بياض ولا جوهر ولا عرض ولا موجود سوادًا وبياضا وجوهرًا وعرضًا وموجودًا ، ثم ما كان من ذلك أفعال العباد فوجوده وشيئيته متعلقة بقدرة الله تعالى وكونه حركة وسكونا وطاعة ومعصية متعلقة بقدرة العبد، وعندهم لا تتعلق شيئية بقدرة أحد ووجوده ليس بمعنى

والمكتسب هو المال ولذلك لا يوصف تعالى بالاكتساب وقد يكون من فعل العبد ما هو مكتسب إذا كان خيرًا أو شرًا اجتلبه بغيره من الأفعال، فأما أول أفعاله فلا يقال فيه إنه مكتسب وإنما يسمى اكتسابًا وقد يكون في أفعاله ما لا يكون اكتسابًا إذا لم يكتسب به نفعًا أو ضرا كحركات الطفل والنائم والساهي.. وكل هذا يبين من جهة اللغة أن المكتسب لابد من أن يكون فاعلاً ومحدثًا. ويقول عبد الجبار الرازي: وكل هذا يبين تجاهل المجبرة في قولهم: إن العبد يكتسب ولا يفعل، وإن هذا ينقض سائر ما يتعلقون به في باب العبادة عند فصلهم بين الكسب والفعل وكأنهم تجنبوا القول بأن الإنسان يفعل.

وراء الشيئية، فينبغي أن لا تتعلق قدرة العبد به فلم يمكنهم تعليق قدرة العبد إلا بقدر ما قلنا، فإذا قلنا بمثل ما قالوا ولم يبق بيننا خلاف إلا في العبارة فإنهم سموا ذلك خلقًا واختراعا، ونحن سميناه كسبًا إلا أن ما وراء ذلك عندنا متعلق بقدرة الله تعالى وعندهم لا يقدره أحد فاستوينا في جنبة العبد ولم يبق لهم علينا إشكال، وفيما وراء ذلك التحقوا بالدهرية والمعطلة، ونحن ثبنا على القول بثبوت الصانع بل هم أتوا بما هو غير المعقول وأبطلوا القول بتعلق القدرة بالمقدور، فإنهم أحالوا تعلقها إلا بالوجود والوجود راجع إلى الذات إذ هو ليس بمعنى وراء الذات ولا تعلق لها بالذات والشيئية فإن تعلقها بما لا تعلق لها به وهو محال وهذيان وبطل بهذا الفصل جميع قواعد المعتزلة وأضمحلت شبهاتهم، ونحن نحمد الله في غاية الوضوح.
We have explained that it is intelligible because rational proofs establish it, but it is not an imagination. If the Mu'tazila abandoned partisanship and looked with reason, submitted to the proof, avoided caprice, and were fair to themselves, they would know that they are those who say what is not intelligible, who cling to what is impossible and absurd. That is because the doctrine of the majority of them is that the non-existent is a thing, and most of them claim that it is an entity, an accident, a substance before coming into existence, and likewise blackness, motion, and essence, according to what we have set forth earlier in explaining their statements. Then the power of the agent relates only to existence and does not relate to thinghood; and it does not become motion, blackness, substance, essence, or entity because these attributes were established in pre-eternity. Then existence is not a meaning beyond essence, so power does not relate to essence; thus its relation to existence cannot be conceived because it is not a meaning beyond essence. So there is no relation of power at all—neither for eternal power nor for temporal power to any potential (maqdur) whatsoever. In this is the nullification of the Maker, the statement of the pre-eternity of the world, the abolition of the establishment of the act of servants, and the nullification of command, prohibition, promise, and threat. And we say: God Almighty created the world and made what is not blackness, whiteness, substance, accident, or existent into blackness, whiteness, substance, accident, and existent. Then whatever of that is the acts of servants, its existence and its thinghood are related to the power of God Almighty, and its being motion, rest, obedience, or disobedience is related to the power of the servant. According to them, thinghood is not related to anyone's power, and its existence is not a meaning beyond thinghood. The acquired (al-muktasab) is property, and therefore the Exalted is not described as acquiring. There may be from the act of the servant what is acquired if it is good or evil that is sought through other acts. As for the first of his acts, it is not called 'acquired'; it is only called 'acquisition' (iktisab). There may be in his acts what is not acquisition if no benefit or harm is acquired through it, like the movements of a child, the sleeping person, and the inattentive person. All this makes clear from the linguistic perspective that the acquirer must be a doer and an originator. And 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Razi says: "All this shows the ignorance of the Jabriya in their statement that the servant acquires but does not act, and that this contradicts everything else they cling to in the chapter of worship when they distinguish between kasb and fi'l; it is as if they avoided saying that man acts." So when we say what they said, no difference remains between us except in expression: they call it creation (khalq) and invention (ikhtira'), while we call it acquisition (kasb). But what is beyond that is, according to us, related to the power of God Almighty, while according to them, no one has power over it. So we are equal regarding the servant, and no objection remains for them against us. In what is beyond that, they align with the Dahriyya and the Mu'attila. We, on the other hand, adhere to the affirmation of the Maker, but they have brought what is irrational and invalidated the statement that power relates to the potential (maqdur). For they considered it impossible for power to relate except to existence, but existence returns to essence since it is not a meaning beyond essence; and power does not relate to essence and thinghood. So its relation to what it does not relate to is impossible, nonsense. With this chapter, all the principles of the Mu'tazila have collapsed and their doubts have vanished. Commentary

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Acquisition (kasb) means the servant creates his own acts independently of God.
Correction: Acquisition is not creation; the existence of the act is from God, the quality is from the servant's choice and power.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidi view, what is related to the power of the servant in human acts?
A) The existence and thinghood of the act.
B) The act being motion, rest, obedience, or disobedience.
C) Both the existence and the quality.
D) Nothing; all is from God.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi theory of acquisition distinguishes between God's creation of the act's existence and the servant's responsibility for its moral quality, preserving both divine omnipotence and human accountability.

?

?

?
If you truly believed that every good deed's existence is from God and only your choosing makes it good, how would your gratitude and reliance on Him change today?

Final Refutation: Collapse of Mu'tazila Principles
Author delivers final refutation and declares Mu'tazila system collapsed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author concludes that the Mu'tazila position is irrational and collapses their entire theological system.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila, by denying God's power over thinghood, align with atheists and contradict reason.

After presenting his own doctrine, the author delivers a final, devastating critique. He argues that the Mu'tazila's own logic forces them to deny any relation of power to the potential, which is absurd. By severing power from its objects, they effectively become like the Dahriyya (materialists) and Mu'attila (those who deny God's attributes). The author concludes that all Mu'tazila principles have collapsed and praises God for clarity.

Guided Path
1
Read the closing argument
Find the final sentences from 'فإنهم أحالوا تعلقها إلا بالوجود' to 'وأضمحلت شبهاتهم'. Read them in Arabic and translation.
Note the logical steps: power can only relate to existence, existence = essence, so power relates to nothing.
2
Understand the accusation of alignment with Dahriyya
The author claims the Mu'tazila, in what lies beyond the servant's power, have no one with power—thus they deny God's creative power.
This is why they 'align with the Dahriyya and Mu'attila'.
3
Grasp the final conclusion
The author declares that all Mu'tazila principles have collapsed (بطل بهذا الفصل جميع قواعد المعتزلة).
This is a rhetorical flourish emphasizing victory.
