وقد بينا أنه معقول لقيام الدلائل العقلية عليه إلا أنه ليس بموهوم، ولو رفضت المعتزلة التعصب ونظرت بالعقل وانقادت للدليل وجانبت الهوى وأنصفت من نفسها لعرفت أنهم القائلون بما لا يعقل المستمسكون بما هو المحال الممتنع، وذلك أن من مذهب جمهورهم أن المعدوم شيء، وأكثرهم يزعمون أنه عين وعرض وجوهر قبل الحدوث وكذا سواد وحركة وذات على ما قررنا قبل هذا من بيان أقاويلهم. ثم قدرة الفاعل لا تتعلق إلا بالوجود ولا تعلق لها بالشيئية، ولا تكون حركة ولا سوادا ولا جوهرًا ولا ذاتاً ولا عينا لأن هذه الأوصاف كانت ثابتة في الأزل، ثم الوجود ليس بمعنى وراء الذات ولا تعلق للقدرة بالذات فلا يتصور تعلقها بالوجود إذ هو ليس معنى وراء الذات فإذا لا تعلق القدرة ما، لا للقدرة القديمة ولا للقدرة المحدثة بمقدور البتة، وفيه تعطيل الصانع والقول بقدم العالم، وإبطال ثبوت الفعل للعباد، وتعطيل الأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد، ونحن نقول: إن الله تعالى خلق العالم وجعل ما ليس بسواد ولا بياض ولا جوهر ولا عرض ولا موجود سوادًا وبياضا وجوهرًا وعرضًا وموجودًا ، ثم ما كان من ذلك أفعال العباد فوجوده وشيئيته متعلقة بقدرة الله تعالى وكونه حركة وسكونا وطاعة ومعصية متعلقة بقدرة العبد، وعندهم لا تتعلق شيئية بقدرة أحد ووجوده ليس بمعنى

والمكتسب هو المال ولذلك لا يوصف تعالى بالاكتساب وقد يكون من فعل العبد ما هو مكتسب إذا كان خيرًا أو شرًا اجتلبه بغيره من الأفعال، فأما أول أفعاله فلا يقال فيه إنه مكتسب وإنما يسمى اكتسابًا وقد يكون في أفعاله ما لا يكون اكتسابًا إذا لم يكتسب به نفعًا أو ضرا كحركات الطفل والنائم والساهي.. وكل هذا يبين من جهة اللغة أن المكتسب لابد من أن يكون فاعلاً ومحدثًا. ويقول عبد الجبار الرازي: وكل هذا يبين تجاهل المجبرة في قولهم: إن العبد يكتسب ولا يفعل، وإن هذا ينقض سائر ما يتعلقون به في باب العبادة عند فصلهم بين الكسب والفعل وكأنهم تجنبوا القول بأن الإنسان يفعل.

وراء الشيئية، فينبغي أن لا تتعلق قدرة العبد به فلم يمكنهم تعليق قدرة العبد إلا بقدر ما قلنا، فإذا قلنا بمثل ما قالوا ولم يبق بيننا خلاف إلا في العبارة فإنهم سموا ذلك خلقًا واختراعا، ونحن سميناه كسبًا إلا أن ما وراء ذلك عندنا متعلق بقدرة الله تعالى وعندهم لا يقدره أحد فاستوينا في جنبة العبد ولم يبق لهم علينا إشكال، وفيما وراء ذلك التحقوا بالدهرية والمعطلة، ونحن ثبنا على القول بثبوت الصانع بل هم أتوا بما هو غير المعقول وأبطلوا القول بتعلق القدرة بالمقدور، فإنهم أحالوا تعلقها إلا بالوجود والوجود راجع إلى الذات إذ هو ليس بمعنى وراء الذات ولا تعلق لها بالذات والشيئية فإن تعلقها بما لا تعلق لها به وهو محال وهذيان وبطل بهذا الفصل جميع قواعد المعتزلة وأضمحلت شبهاتهم، ونحن نحمد الله في غاية الوضوح.
We have explained that it is intelligible because rational proofs establish it, but it is not an imagination. If the Mu'tazila abandoned partisanship and looked with reason, submitted to the proof, avoided caprice, and were fair to themselves, they would know that they are those who say what is not intelligible, who cling to what is impossible and absurd. That is because the doctrine of the majority of them is that the non-existent is a thing, and most of them claim that it is an entity, an accident, a substance before coming into existence, and likewise blackness, motion, and essence, according to what we have set forth earlier in explaining their statements. Then the power of the agent relates only to existence and does not relate to thinghood; and it does not become motion, blackness, substance, essence, or entity because these attributes were established in pre-eternity. Then existence is not a meaning beyond essence, so power does not relate to essence; thus its relation to existence cannot be conceived because it is not a meaning beyond essence. So there is no relation of power at all—neither for eternal power nor for temporal power to any potential (maqdur) whatsoever. In this is the nullification of the Maker, the statement of the pre-eternity of the world, the abolition of the establishment of the act of servants, and the nullification of command, prohibition, promise, and threat. And we say: God Almighty created the world and made what is not blackness, whiteness, substance, accident, or existent into blackness, whiteness, substance, accident, and existent. Then whatever of that is the acts of servants, its existence and its thinghood are related to the power of God Almighty, and its being motion, rest, obedience, or disobedience is related to the power of the servant. According to them, thinghood is not related to anyone's power, and its existence is not a meaning beyond thinghood. The acquired (al-muktasab) is property, and therefore the Exalted is not described as acquiring. There may be from the act of the servant what is acquired if it is good or evil that is sought through other acts. As for the first of his acts, it is not called 'acquired'; it is only called 'acquisition' (iktisab). There may be in his acts what is not acquisition if no benefit or harm is acquired through it, like the movements of a child, the sleeping person, and the inattentive person. All this makes clear from the linguistic perspective that the acquirer must be a doer and an originator. And 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Razi says: "All this shows the ignorance of the Jabriya in their statement that the servant acquires but does not act, and that this contradicts everything else they cling to in the chapter of worship when they distinguish between kasb and fi'l; it is as if they avoided saying that man acts." Beyond thinghood, it is necessary that the servant's power does not relate to it; they could not relate the servant's power except to the extent we said. So when we say what they said, no difference remains between us except in expression: they call it creation (khalq) and invention (ikhtira'), while we call it acquisition (kasb). But what is beyond that is, according to us, related to the power of God Almighty, while according to them, no one has power over it. So we are equal regarding the servant, and no objection remains for them against us. In what is beyond that, they align with the Dahriyya and the Mu'attila. We, on the other hand, adhere to the affirmation of the Maker, but they have brought what is irrational and invalidated the statement that power relates to the potential (maqdur). For they considered it impossible for power to relate except to existence, but existence returns to essence since it is not a meaning beyond essence; and power does not relate to essence and thinghood. So its relation to what it does not relate to is impossible, nonsense. With this chapter, all the principles of the Mu'tazila have collapsed and their doubts have vanished. We praise God for utmost clarity.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a multi-part argument refuting the Mu'tazila on the nature of the non-existent and divine/human power, followed by the author's own doctrine of acquisition. The passage begins by noting that the intelligibility of a thing is established by rational proofs, but the Mu'tazila have abandoned reason for partisanship. Their error is traced to the claim that the non-existent (ma'dum) is a thing, and even an entity, accident, substance, etc., before existence. The author then argues that power (qudra) of any agent relates only to existence, not to attributes like thinghood or essence that are pre-eternal. Since existence is not a separate meaning from essence, power cannot relate to existence either, leading to absurdities: denying God's power, claiming the world is pre-eternal, and nullifying human acts and moral commands. The Maturidi position is then stated: God creates the world and its properties, and the acts of servants have their existence and thinghood from God's power, but their specific qualities (motion, obedience, etc.) from the servant's power. The Mu'tazila deny thinghood from any power, contradicting themselves. The author then introduces a definition of 'al-muktasab' (the acquired), explaining that only the servant's subsequent acts are acquired, not the first act. A quote from the Mu'tazila scholar 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Razi criticizes the Maturidi distinction between kasb and fi'l. The author responds by arguing that the Mu'tazila's own view forces them to deny any power relation, but the Maturidi view accounts for all cases. The response concludes that the Mu'tazila have no real objection, and their position aligns with the Dahriyya and Mu'attila (deniers of God or attributes). The final conclusion is that the entire Mu'tazila system collapses, and God is praised for clarity.

Key Terms
الدهرية
المعطلة
القدرة
المقدور
المحال

Checkpoint
What does the author claim happens to the Mu'tazila principles in this passage?
A) They are strengthened by rational proof.
B) They have collapsed and their doubts have vanished.
C) They remain but need revision.
D) They are partially accepted.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila position reduces to absurdity because power cannot relate to anything, collapsing their entire theological framework.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself mentally limiting God’s power by assuming He cannot work through certain means or bring about something you deem impossible in your own life? What would it take for you to truly abandon that subtle restriction and trust His absolute power over all things—even those that seem utterly nonexistent to you now?
?
The Mu'tazila’s downfall was over-reliance on their own reason, leading them to deny what is rationally necessary about God. Is there a particular belief or assumption you hold about God that you have never questioned because it ‘makes sense’ to you, yet may actually contradict the clear teachings of revelation and sound reason? Will you have the courage to examine it today?
?
The author ends with praise to God for clarity. When you encounter a truth that resolves confusion in your faith, do you spontaneously praise Him, or do you move on without gratitude? Commit to pausing and thanking Allah the next time He grants you clarity in your understanding of Him.

Answer to the objection about God creating movement
Nasafi refutes the Batiniyya objection with a counter-argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes the Batiniyya objection by exposing a logical inconsistency in their own position.

Core Idea
The answer turns the objection back on the objector.

Nasafi presents a brilliant tu quoque argument. The Batiniyya claim that if God creates movement, human action is meaningless. Nasafi replies by showing that their own ontology—where existence is identical to essence—leads to an even greater problem: if God does not create anything, then nothing exists to be acted upon. The objection collapses under its own weight.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then its literal translation. Pay attention to the structure: objection, response, and the key premise.
The premise 'existence is identical to essence' is crucial.
2
Identify the objection and counter-objection
The Batiniyya say: if God creates movement, what did I do? Nasafi counters: if you did not do the thing, and existence is the thing, then what did you do? Also, what did God do if He did not create anything?
Notice the symmetry: each side's question mirrors the other.
3
Understand the key premise
The premise 'existence is identical to essence' means that a thing is not separate from its existence. So if God does not create the essence, nothing exists. This exposes the inconsistency in the Batiniyya position.
This premise is borrowed from philosophical theology; Nasafi uses it ad hominem.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبهذا يجابون عن قولهم: إن الله تعالى إذا فعل الحركة فماذا فعلت أنا؟ فيقال لهم: وإذا لم تفعل أنت الشيء ولا العين والوجود هو عين الشيء إذ ليس بمعنى وراءه فماذا فعلت إذا لم يفعل الله الجوهر ولا العرض ولا الشيء ولا العين ولا السواد ولا البياض ولا الرائحة ولا الطعم فماذا فعل؟ ووجودها إذا لم يكن معنى وراءها أو هو عينها وذاتها ولم يفعل عينها ولا ذاتها فماذا فعل؟ فما أجابوا من شيء فهو لهم جواب.
And with this they are answered regarding their statement: 'If Allah Most High creates the movement, then what did I do?' It is said to them: 'And if you did not do the thing nor the essence—and existence is the essence of the thing, since it is not a meaning behind it—then what did you do, if Allah did not create the substance nor the accident nor the thing nor the essence, nor blackness nor whiteness nor smell nor taste; what did He do? And their existence, if it is not a meaning behind them or it is their essence and their selves, and He did not create their essence nor their self, then what did He do? Whatever they answer is an answer for them.'
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and a counter-objection. The Batiniyya argue: if God creates a movement, then what action is left for the human? Nasafi's answer exposes a logical consequence of their own position. He says: if we grant that 'existence is identical to the essence' (الوجود عين الشيء), i.e., there is no extra attribute of existence, then when God does not create a thing, the human has no object to act upon. The question is turned back: 'Then what did you do?' and 'What did God do?' If nothing, then the objection is moot. The answer is a tu quoque: whatever they say in response applies equally to them.

Key Terms
الحركة
فعل العبد
العين
الوجود عين الشيء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The answer denies human agency altogether.
Correction: The answer does not deny human agency; it exposes inconsistency in the Batiniyya position.

Checkpoint
In the answer, what is said to be the relationship between existence and essence?
A) Existence is separate from essence.
B) Existence is identical to essence.
C) Essence is unnecessary.
D) Existence and essence are both created by God.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi refutes the Batiniyya by showing that their own premises lead to a contradiction, thus the objection is invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used the Batiniyya's logic—'if God created this situation, then I have no role'—to excuse yourself from responsibility? This lesson shows that such thinking is self-defeating. What is one area where you need to stop making that excuse and take deliberate action?
?
When you feel powerless, do you blame God for not creating a solution for you? This lesson exposes that blame as logically flawed. What is one step you can take today to act within God's creation instead of waiting for Him to act alone?
?
The passage argues that if existence equals essence, then both God and you are involved in every action. Does that challenge you to embrace personal responsibility, or comfort you that God is always present? How will you change your daily choices in light of this truth?

Refutation of Abu al-Hudhayl's Compulsion in Paradise
The author refutes Abu al-Hudhayl's view using a dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attributing all actions of the inhabitants of Paradise to Allah without human choice leads to a blasphemous conclusion and how the author forces Abu al-Hudhayl into a dilemma.

Core Idea
Extreme determinism in Paradise would make Allah the eater and drinker—an absurd blasphemy.

Abu al-Hudhayl argued that the people of Paradise are compelled in their actions and that all their actions are directly from Allah. The author of Tabsirat al-Adilla exposes the logical consequence of this view: if all actions, including eating, drinking, and walking, are solely acts of Allah, then the subject performing them would be Allah Himself. This is clearly unacceptable. The passage presents a dilemma that forces Abu al-Hudhayl either to accept blasphemy or abandon his argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify Abu al-Hudhayl's position
Read the first part of the passage to understand what Abu al-Hudhayl claims about the actions of Paradise inhabitants.
He says they are compelled (majboorun) in their actions.
2
List the specific actions mentioned
Note the actions listed: eating, drinking, sexual intercourse, walking, sitting, grasping, spreading.
These are ordinary human actions.
3
Understand the consequence
If all these actions are directly the act of Allah, then the one who eats, drinks, etc., is Allah Himself—a blasphemous conclusion.
The author emphasizes this by saying 'Allah is exalted above what they say.'
4
Recognize the dilemma
Abu al-Hudhayl is forced between two options: accept the blasphemy and become a disbeliever, or reject it and invalidate his own argument.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
5
Note the label 'Jahmī of the Hereafter'
Understand why this label is used: it associates his view with the deterministic theology of Jahm ibn Safwan.
It shows the extremity of his position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم من مذهب رئيسكم أبي الهذيل أن أهل الجنة مجبورون على أفعالهم وما يوجد منهم من الأكل والشرب والجماع والمشي والقعود والقبض والبسط كله فعل الله تعالى بلا اختيار للعبد حتى قيل: إن أبا الهذيل جهمي الآخرة فيكون على قود كلامه هذا الآكل الشارب المجامع الماشي القاعد القابض الباسط هو الله تعالى الله عما يقولون علوا كبيرًا - فكان هو بين أمرين إما أن يلتزم ذلك كله فيكفر، وإما أن يمتنع فيبطل حجاجه.
Then from the doctrine of your leader Abu al-Hudhayl is that the people of Paradise are compelled in their actions, and whatever appears from them of eating, drinking, sexual intercourse, walking, sitting, grasping, and spreading is entirely the act of Allah the Exalted without any choice for the servant, until it was said: 'Abu al-Hudhayl is a Jahmī of the Hereafter.' So according to the implication of his statement, the eater, the drinker, the one having intercourse, the walker, the sitter, the grasper, the spreader would be Allah the Exalted—exalted is Allah above what they say, with great exaltation. So he was between two matters: either he accepts all of that and thus disbelieves, or he refrains and thus invalidates his argument.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage refutes Abu al-Hudhayl's position that the actions of the inhabitants of Paradise are entirely compelled and are directly the acts of Allah. The author points out the absurd consequence: if all actions such as eating, drinking, walking, etc. in Paradise are solely acts of Allah with no human choice, then the subject performing those actions (the eater, the drinker, etc.) would be Allah Himself. This is clearly blasphemous, as it attributes human bodily actions to Allah. The author states that Abu al-Hudhayl is thus forced into a dilemma: either he accepts this blasphemous implication and becomes a disbeliever, or he rejects it and thereby invalidates his own argument. The passage uses the label 'Jahmī of the Hereafter' to associate his view with the deterministic theology of Jahm ibn Safwān.

Key Terms
أبو الهذيل
الجنة
مجبورون
جهمي
فعل الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if Allah creates all actions, human agency is completely negated even in Paradise, and this is acceptable.
Correction: The author shows that extreme determinism leads to attributing imperfect human actions to Allah, which is blasphemous; thus, some human agency must be preserved.

Checkpoint
What is the dilemma faced by Abu al-Hudhayl according to the author?
A) He must accept that Paradise is temporary or eternal.
B) He must accept that the people of Paradise are not rewarded or punished.
C) He must either accept that Allah eats and drinks (blasphemy) or reject his own view.
D) He must admit that his view contradicts the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The argument shows that extreme determinism, if applied consistently, leads to attributing human bodily actions to Allah, which is blasphemy; thus it must be rejected.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking, 'Allah made me do it'? How does this lesson's warning against attributing human actions to Allah confront that excuse?
?
If you truly believe that your good deeds in Paradise will be your own choices, how does that motivate you to cultivate sincere obedience now, knowing that Allah does not compel you?
?
Abu al-Hudhayl's error was taking a truth (Allah's power) to an extreme. In what area of your faith might you be exaggerating a sound principle to the point where it distorts your view of Allah? Will you repent and return to balance today?

Refutation of Mu'tazila: Human Acts Cannot Be Superior to God's Acts
The author refutes the Mu'tazilite claim by showing it leads to the absurdity that human acts are better than God's acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the Mu'tazilite claim that humans create their own acts by showing it leads to the absurd conclusion that human good deeds are superior to God's acts.

Core Idea
If humans create their own acts, human virtue would surpass God's acts.

The Mu'tazila held that humans have the power to create their own acts, making them independent of God's direct creation. This passage presents a powerful logical refutation (إلزام) from a Maturidi perspective: if true, then everything good would be in human power and everything evil in God's power, making human acts superior. The author lays out this absurdity and notes that the Mu'tazila themselves avoid this conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazilite position
The Mu'tazila claimed that humans create their own actions, including good and evil deeds, with a power God gives them. They argued this preserves human responsibility and justice.
The refutation does not deny human responsibility but attacks the idea of independent creation.
2
Read the passage and identify the contrast
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the two lists: what the author says would be in God's power vs. in human power if the Mu'tazilite claim were true.
The list for God includes evil and calamities; the list for humans includes acts of worship and virtue.
3
Analyze the logical implication
If humans create good deeds, then human acts would be superior in virtue to God's acts, since God would only create evil. This is an absurd and blasphemous conclusion.
The author uses this to show the Mu'tazilite position is false.
4
Reflect on the Mu'tazila response
The passage ends by noting that the Mu'tazila themselves recognize this implication and try to avoid it by focusing on negative aspects. The author prays for protection from such falsehood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفاعلين بتفاضل الأفعال فينبغي أن يكون كل عبد مطيع أفضل من الله تعالى وأحسن فعلاً وأرفع درجة لعلو رتبة فعله على فعل الله تعالى، وانحطاط رتبة فعله عز وجل عن أفعال العباد، ويكون في مقدور العبد من المحاسن ما ليس يماثل ذلك أو يقاربه في مقدور الله تعالى، والقول به قول لا خفاء بما فيه، فكان مقدور الله تعالى هو إبليس والقردة والأقذار والأنتان والزمانة والعمى والشلل والأمراض و الموت والمصائب ومقدور العبد الصوم والصلاة والحج والإقراض والتصديق واعتقاد التوحيد والإفضال إلى المحتاجين والإحسان إليهم والوفاء بالعهود وأداء الأمانات والجود والسماحة، وغير ذلك من الفضائل الداخلة تحت قدرة العباد، تقدر كل واحد من الفاعلين بمقدور ، وذهب بما خلق وفاز العبد بالقسم الأحسن والحظ الأجزل، وقصرت قدرة القديم عن ذلك، ولعلم المعتزلة بهذا الإلزام يعرضون عن جانب المحاسن صفحًا ويتشبثون بالمقابح ليتمكنوا عسى من ترويج باطلهم على ضعفاء عصمنا الله تعالى عن ذلك بكرمه وفضله وهو ذو الفضل العظيم.
The doers [would have] differences in actions, so it should be that every obedient servant is better than God Almighty, and better in act, and higher in rank, due to the elevation of his act's rank over God's act, and the decline of His rank, Exalted is He, from the acts of servants. And there would be in the servant's power of good deeds that which is not similar to that or near it in God's power. And this statement is a statement whose content is not hidden. Then God's power would be [associated with] Iblis, monkeys, filth, stench, chronic illness, blindness, paralysis, diseases, death, and calamities, while the servant's power would be fasting, prayer, Hajj, lending, verifying, believing in Tawhid, favoring the needy, treating them well, fulfilling covenants, fulfilling trusts, generosity, and magnanimity, and other virtues within the power of servants. Each of the doers is empowered with his power, and He (God) has done what He created, and the servant attains the best portion and greatest luck, and the power of the Eternal falls short of that. And the Mu'tazila, knowing this implication, turn away from the side of goodness completely and cling to bad deeds so that they might possibly promote their falsehood among the weak. May God protect us from that through His generosity and bounty, and He is the Possessor of great bounty.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (إلزام) against the Mu'tazilite doctrine that humans create their own acts. The author argues that if humans truly create their acts independently, then they would be the creators of good deeds, while God would be the creator of evil deeds, leading to the absurd conclusion that human acts are superior to God's acts. The author lists what would then be in God's power (evil things like Iblis, monkeys, filth, etc.) versus what would be in human power (good deeds like prayer, fasting, charity, etc.), and concludes that this is an unacceptable implication. The Mu'tazila are aware of this and try to avoid it by focusing on negative aspects. The passage ends with a prayer for protection.

Key Terms
مقدور
قدرة
فعل
إلزام
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ash'ari and Maturidi deny any human capacity or responsibility for actions.
Correction: This refutation targets the idea of independent creation (خلق) of acts, not human acquisition (كسب). Humans are responsible for their choices, but acts are created by God.

Checkpoint
What absurd consequence does the author derive from the Mu'tazilite claim that humans create their own acts?
A) Humans would become gods
B) Human acts of virtue would be better than God's acts
C) God would be ignorant of human actions
D) Humans would have no need for God's mercy

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite claim that humans create their own acts leads to the absurd conclusion that human good deeds are better than God's acts, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that your good deeds were created entirely by you and not by Allah, how would that change your sense of gratitude and reliance on Him? After reading this passage, do you realize that even your ability to pray is a gift from Him? How will you actively remind yourself of this when you perform salah today?
?
The author lists fasting, prayer, charity, etc. as acts that would be in human power if humans created their own acts. But in reality, these are all from Allah. Have you ever felt proud of your worship, forgetting that it is Allah who enabled you? How will you combat that pride before you pray your next prayer?
?
The Mu'tazila avoid this implication by focusing on negative aspects. Are there areas in your life where you focus more on what you perceive as shortcomings of Allah's decree (e.g., difficulties), ignoring the countless blessings you receive? What concrete step will you take today to shift your focus to gratitude?

The Murdered Person Dies by His Own Term
Definition of the Maturidi view on the term of the murdered person.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position that the murdered person dies by his own predetermined term, and how death and killing are distinguished.

Core Idea
Death is God's act; killing is the killer's act but not the cause of death.

This lesson introduces the Maturidi view on the term of the murdered person. The author clarifies that death is created by God alone, and the killer's act is merely a concomitant event. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping the broader doctrine of predestination.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the definition of killing and death
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the translation. Note the key terms: الموت (death) and القتل (killing).
Pay attention to the phrase 'لا صنع للعبد فيه' indicating no agency of the servant.
2
Identify the Maturidi position
The first sentence states the core belief: the murdered person dies by his term. The rest explains how death is God's act.
3
Distinguish between death and killing
Notice that death is a created meaning in the victim, while killing is an act of the killer that subsists in him, not transmitted to the victim.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this distinction matters: it preserves divine sovereignty over life and death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في الآجال: المقتول عندنا ميت بأجله، وما يخلق الله فيه من المعنى المنافي للحياة قتلاً، كما يسمى مفعول الله تعالى وليس بفعل للقاتل وهو الموت، والقتل فعل القاتل قائم به ليس بحال في المقتول، والفعل الذي يوجد في القاتل ويوجد الله عقيبه انزهاق الروح أو الموت في المحل بطريق إجراء العادة يسمى ما يتفرق عقيبه جسم صلب كسرا، والتفرق مفعول الله تعالى لا صنع للعبد فيه، وزعم الكعبي أن المقتول غير ميت لأن الموت من فعل الله والقتل من فعل القاتل، وقال غيره من المعتزلة في المقتول معنيان: أحدهما من الله وهو الموت، والآخر من العبد وهو القتل، وما ذكرنا من دلائل إبطال القول بالتولد يوجب بطلان هذا كله، ثم يتصل بهذا أن المقتول ميت بأجله وهذا هو أجله لا أجل له سواه، وكذا قال أبو الهذيل من جملة المعتزلة حتى قال: لو لم يقتل لمات بأجله في وقت قتله قال : والمدة التي لم يعش إليها لم تكن أجلاً ولا من عمره، وعندنا ليس الأمر كذلك بل يقتل لا محالة، وكذا قال الجبائي أن لا أجل له إلا هذا وقال الباقون المقتول مقطوع عليه أجله كذا ذكروا، ولنا قوله: ﴿ فَإِذَا جَاءَ أَجَلُهُمْ لَا يَسْتَأْخِرُونَ سَاعَةٌ وَلَا يَسْتَقْدِمُونَ ﴾ والحديث المعروف أن عند تصوير العبد في بطن أمه يأمر الله ملكا فيكتب على جبهته رزقه وأجله وسعادته وشقاوته، وتعلقهم بقوله تعالى: وَمَا يُعَمَّرُ مِن تُعَمَّرٍ وَلَا يُنقَصُ مِنْ عُمُرِه إِلَّا فِي كِتَبٍ وتقدير الآية عندنا والله أعلم - وما يعمر من معمر، ولا ينقص من عمر معمر آخر سواه أي يعطي لهذا الثاني من العمر ما يكون ناقصا بمقابلة عمر الأول والهاء راجع إلى من يماثله في الاسم لا إلى عين المذكور كما يقال : هذا درهم ونصفه أي نصف درهم آخر مماثل للأول في الاسم كذا ذكر كبار أهل اللغة
Discussion on the appointed terms (āl-ājāl): The murdered person, according to us, dies by his term, and what God creates in him of the meaning contrary to life is killing, just as it is called an act of God Almighty and not an act of the killer—that is death. Killing is an act of the killer, subsisting in him, not located in the murdered person. The act that exists in the killer, and God creates after it the departure of the soul or death in the subject by way of customary procedure, is called breaking of a solid body after which it becomes fragmented; the fragmentation is an act of God Almighty, no agency of the servant in it. Al-Ka‘bī claimed that the murdered person is not dead, because death is from God's act and killing is from the killer's act. Others among the Mu‘tazila said concerning the murdered person: there are two meanings—one from God, which is death, and the other from the servant, which is killing. What we have mentioned of proofs for invalidating the theory of generation (tawallud) necessitates the invalidity of all this. Then connected to this is that the murdered person dies by his term, and this is his term; no term other than it. Likewise Abū al-Hudhayl, one of the Mu‘tazila, said—even saying: if he were not killed, he would die by his term at the time of his killing. He said: the period he did not live to was not a term nor part of his life. According to us, it is not like that; rather he is killed inevitably. Likewise al-Jubbā'ī said that he has no term except this one. The rest said: the murdered person, his term is cut off—thus they mentioned. For us is His statement: “So when their term comes, they will not delay an hour nor advance” (7:34), and the well-known hadith that when the servant is formed in his mother's womb, God commands an angel to write on his forehead his provision, his term, his happiness, and his misery. Their attachment to His statement: “And no aged person is given length of age, nor is any diminished from his life, except in a book” (35:11). Our estimation of the verse, and God knows best, is: And no aged person is given length of age, nor is decreased from the age of another aged person besides him—meaning He gives to this second one of life what is decreased in comparison to the age of the first. The pronoun (his) refers to one similar to him in name, not to the mentioned individual himself, just as it is said: This is a dirham and its half—i.e., another half dirham similar to the first in name. Thus the leading linguists mentioned.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal discussion on the appointed term (ajal) for death, specifically addressing whether the murdered person dies by his own predetermined term. The author presents the Maturidi position and refutes the views of various Mu‘tazila. The author begins by stating the Maturidi position: the murdered person dies by his own term (ajal). God creates in him the meaning contrary to life, which is called death (mawt). Death is God's act, not the killer's act. Killing (qatl) is the act of the killer, subsisting in him, not in the victim. The act of killing in the killer is followed by God's creation of the departure of the soul or death in the subject via customary procedure (ijrā' al-‘ādah), analogous to breaking a solid body into pieces—the fragmentation is God's act, not the servant's. The author then presents the Mu‘tazila objections: Al-Ka‘bī claimed that the murdered person is not dead because death is from God and killing from the killer. Other Mu‘tazila said the murdered person has two meanings: death from God and killing from the servant. The author asserts that the earlier proofs invalidating tawallud (generation) already refute these claims. He reiterates the core: the murdered person dies by his term, and this is his only term. He then reports the views of leading Mu‘tazila: Abū al-Hudhayl said that if the person were not killed, he would die at the same time—the period not reached was not part of his term or life. Al-Jubbā'ī said the murdered person has no other term. The author rejects these, affirming that the person is killed inevitably. Evidence from the Quran (7:34) and the well-known hadith about the angel writing the term on the fetus's forehead supports the predetermination of the term. Then the author addresses the Mu‘tazila's proof-text, Surah Fatir 35:11, which seems to imply increase and decrease in lifespan. He provides an interpretation: the verse refers to two different individuals—one aged and another whose life is decreased in comparison—not that the same person's life is shortened. The pronoun 'his' in 'min ‘umurihi' refers to a similar person, not the same individual, analogous to saying 'this dirham and its half' meaning another half-dirham. This interpretation is from leading linguists.

Key Terms
الأجل
القتل
الموت
المقتول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the killer causes death directly.
Correction: The passage clarifies that death is created by God; the killer's act is not the cause.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the relationship between killing and death?
A) The killer's act directly causes death.
B) Death is created by God after the killer's act via customary procedure.
C) Death is a result of the killer's intention.
D) The killer's act and death are the same thing.

Key Takeaway
The murdered person dies by his predetermined term, and death is exclusively God's act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel safe because of your precautions—locks, doctors, or avoiding dangerous situations—do you truly believe that your term is fixed by God alone, or do you secretly trust in those means as the real protectors?
?
If death is solely God's act, why do you fear the harm others can do to you? Is your fear a sign that you attribute power to creation rather than to the Creator?
?
The killer's act is only a context—what 'killer' contexts in your life (people, circumstances, or your own actions) do you mistakenly believe are the real causes of your outcomes, instead of seeing God's decree behind them?

Refuting the Mu'tazila on the Term of the Murdered Person
Presentation and refutation of Mu'tazila views on the term of the murdered person.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila objections to the Maturidi view and why the author considers them invalid based on the rejection of tawallud.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila divide death and killing into two separate acts; Maturidis insist on one unified predestination.

This lesson presents the objections of al-Ka‘bī and other Mu‘tazila who claim that the murdered person does not die by his own term. The author refutes them by citing the principle that invalidates the theory of generation (tawallud). You will see how different schools of thought grapple with the relationship between divine decree and human action.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Mu'tazila views
First read the Arabic and translation. Identify the claims of al-Ka‘bī, the generic Mu'tazila, and the specific views of Abū al-Hudhayl and al-Jubbā'ī.
Notice the progression: Ka'bi says the murdered person is not dead, others say there are two meanings, then Abu Hudhayl says he would die at the same time if not killed.
2
Understand the refutation via tawallud
The author states that the invalidation of tawallud (generation of acts) refutes all these views. Reflect on why: if acts cannot generate other acts, then killing cannot produce death.
3
Compare the positions
List the different positions: Ka'bi, other Mu'tazila, Abu Hudhayl, Jubbai. Note how the Maturidi view rejects them all.
4
Apply the principle
Consider how the principle of no generation of acts upholds the doctrine that death is directly from God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

What is the author's main argument against the Mu'tazila views?
A) The Quran clearly states that the term is unchangeable.
B) The theory of tawallud (generation) has been invalidated, so killing cannot cause death.

D) The Mu'tazila are wrong because they deny predestination.

The Mu'tazila attempts to separate death and killing are refuted by the principle that no act generates another; death is entirely from God.

?

Is that belief reflected in your emotional response, or do you feel anger at the killer as if they completely thwarted Allah's plan?
?
If you were to die today, would you be content that your term has arrived exactly as Allah wrote? Or would you feel that something or someone 'cut it short'? How does this lesson challenge your sense of control over your own life?

Quranic and Hadith Evidence for the Fixed Term
Scriptural evidence for the fixed term and interpretation of the contested verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural proofs for the fixed term of death and the author's interpretive response to the verse that seems to imply variable lifespans.

Core Idea
Quran and hadith affirm that each person’s term is fixed and unchangeable.

This lesson examines the evidence the author brings for the fixed term: a Quranic verse stating that no one can delay or advance his term, and the well-known hadith about the angel writing the term. It also addresses the Mu'tazila's proof-text from Surah Fatir by providing a linguistic interpretation that resolves the apparent contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the two primary proofs
Read the Quranic verse (7:34) and the hadith about the angel writing the term.
2
Understand the Mu'tazila objection
The Mu'tazila used Surah Fatir 35:11 to argue that lifespans can increase or decrease. Read the verse and note their interpretation.
3
Analyze the author's interpretation
Read the author's explanation that the verse refers to two different persons, not the same individual. Understand the linguistic analogy of 'a dirham and its half'.
Pay attention to the pronoun resolution: 'his' refers to a similar person.
4
Reflect on the consistency
See how this interpretation maintains the doctrine that each person's term is fixed and does not change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في الآجال: المقتول عندنا ميت بأجله، وما يخلق الله فيه من المعنى المنافي للحياة قتلاً، كما يسمى مفعول الله تعالى وليس بفعل للقاتل وهو الموت، والقتل فعل القاتل قائم به ليس بحال في المقتول، والفعل الذي يوجد في القاتل ويوجد الله عقيبه انزهاق الروح أو الموت في المحل بطريق إجراء العادة يسمى ما يتفرق عقيبه جسم صلب كسرا، والتفرق مفعول الله تعالى لا صنع للعبد فيه، وزعم الكعبي أن المقتول غير ميت لأن الموت من فعل الله والقتل من فعل القاتل، وقال غيره من المعتزلة في المقتول معنيان: أحدهما من الله وهو الموت، والآخر من العبد وهو القتل، وما ذكرنا من دلائل إبطال القول بالتولد يوجب بطلان هذا كله، ثم يتصل بهذا أن المقتول ميت بأجله وهذا هو أجله لا أجل له سواه، وكذا قال أبو الهذيل من جملة المعتزلة حتى قال: لو لم يقتل لمات بأجله في وقت قتله قال : والمدة التي لم يعش إليها لم تكن أجلاً ولا من عمره، وعندنا ليس الأمر كذلك بل يقتل لا محالة، وكذا قال الجبائي أن لا أجل له إلا هذا وقال الباقون المقتول مقطوع عليه أجله كذا ذكروا، ولنا قوله: ﴿ فَإِذَا جَاءَ أَجَلُهُمْ لَا يَسْتَأْخِرُونَ سَاعَةٌ وَلَا يَسْتَقْدِمُونَ ﴾ والحديث المعروف أن عند تصوير العبد في بطن أمه يأمر الله ملكا فيكتب على جبهته رزقه وأجله وسعادته وشقاوته، وتعلقهم بقوله تعالى: وَمَا يُعَمَّرُ مِن تُعَمَّرٍ وَلَا يُنقَصُ مِنْ عُمُرِه إِلَّا فِي كِتَبٍ وتقدير الآية عندنا والله أعلم - وما يعمر من معمر، ولا ينقص من عمر معمر آخر سواه أي يعطي لهذا الثاني من العمر ما يكون ناقصا بمقابلة عمر الأول والهاء راجع إلى من يماثله في الاسم لا إلى عين المذكور كما يقال : هذا درهم ونصفه أي نصف درهم آخر مماثل للأول في الاسم كذا ذكر كبار أهل اللغة
Discussion on the appointed terms (āl-ājāl): The murdered person, according to us, dies by his term, and what God creates in him of the meaning contrary to life is killing, just as it is called an act of God Almighty and not an act of the killer—that is death. Killing is an act of the killer, subsisting in him, not located in the murdered person. The act that exists in the killer, and God creates after it the departure of the soul or death in the subject by way of customary procedure, is called breaking of a solid body after which it becomes fragmented; the fragmentation is an act of God Almighty, no agency of the servant in it. Al-Ka‘bī claimed that the murdered person is not dead, because death is from God's act and killing is from the killer's act. Others among the Mu‘tazila said concerning the murdered person: there are two meanings—one from God, which is death, and the other from the servant, which is killing. What we have mentioned of proofs for invalidating the theory of generation (tawallud) necessitates the invalidity of all this. Then connected to this is that the murdered person dies by his term, and this is his term; no term other than it. Likewise Abū al-Hudhayl, one of the Mu‘tazila, said—even saying: if he were not killed, he would die by his term at the time of his killing. He said: the period he did not live to was not a term nor part of his life. According to us, it is not like that; rather he is killed inevitably. Likewise al-Jubbā'ī said that he has no term except this one. The rest said: the murdered person, his term is cut off—thus they mentioned. For us is His statement: “So when their term comes, they will not delay an hour nor advance” (7:34), and the well-known hadith that when the servant is formed in his mother's womb, God commands an angel to write on his forehead his provision, his term, his happiness, and his misery. Their attachment to His statement: “And no aged person is given length of age, nor is any diminished from his life, except in a book” (35:11). Our estimation of the verse, and God knows best, is: And no aged person is given length of age, nor is decreased from the age of another aged person besides him—meaning He gives to this second one of life what is decreased in comparison to the age of the first. The pronoun (his) refers to one similar to him in name, not to the mentioned individual himself, just as it is said: This is a dirham and its half—i.e., another half dirham similar to the first in name. Thus the leading linguists mentioned.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal discussion on the appointed term (ajal) for death, specifically addressing whether the murdered person dies by his own predetermined term. The author presents the Maturidi position and refutes the views of various Mu‘tazila. The author begins by stating the Maturidi position: the murdered person dies by his own term (ajal). God creates in him the meaning contrary to life, which is called death (mawt). Death is God's act, not the killer's act. Killing (qatl) is the act of the killer, subsisting in him, not in the victim. The act of killing in the killer is followed by God's creation of the departure of the soul or death in the subject via customary procedure (ijrā' al-‘ādah), analogous to breaking a solid body into pieces—the fragmentation is God's act, not the servant's. The author then presents the Mu‘tazila objections: Al-Ka‘bī claimed that the murdered person is not dead because death is from God and killing from the killer. Other Mu‘tazila said the murdered person has two meanings: death from God and killing from the servant. The author asserts that the earlier proofs invalidating tawallud (generation) already refute these claims. He reiterates the core: the murdered person dies by his term, and this is his only term. He then reports the views of leading Mu‘tazila: Abū al-Hudhayl said that if the person were not killed, he would die at the same time—the period not reached was not part of his term or life. Al-Jubbā'ī said the murdered person has no other term. The author rejects these, affirming that the person is killed inevitably. Evidence from the Quran (7:34) and the well-known hadith about the angel writing the term on the fetus's forehead supports the predetermination of the term. Then the author addresses the Mu‘tazila's proof-text, Surah Fatir 35:11, which seems to imply increase and decrease in lifespan. He provides an interpretation: the verse refers to two different individuals—one aged and another whose life is decreased in comparison—not that the same person's life is shortened. The pronoun 'his' in 'min ‘umurihi' refers to a similar person, not the same individual, analogous to saying 'this dirham and its half' meaning another half-dirham. This interpretation is from leading linguists.

Key Terms
الأجل
الكتاب
العمر
التقدير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse in Surah Fatir (35:11) proves that a person's lifespan can be increased or decreased.
Correction: The author interprets it as referring to two different persons, not the same individual, so the term remains fixed.

Checkpoint
How does the author interpret the pronoun 'his' in the phrase 'min 'umurihi' in Surah Fatir 35:11?
A) It refers to the same person, allowing for increase and decrease.
B) It refers to a different but similar person, meaning no change for the individual.
C) It refers to the collective lifespan of humanity.
D) It is ambiguous and cannot be determined.

Key Takeaway
The fixed term of death is affirmed by clear Quranic and hadith texts, and the verse that seems to indicate variation is interpreted to refer to different individuals.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the angel writes your term on your forehead while you are still in the womb, does that make you feel helpless or liberated? How does that affect the way you spend your time today?
?
If your lifespan cannot be increased or decreased by any action or prayer, what does that mean for the sincerity of your supplications for a long life? Are you willing to submit to God's timing even when it means a short life?
?
The Mu'tazila wanted to preserve room for human effort to change one's destiny. After learning the Maturidi interpretation, do you find yourself trusting God's decree more, or do you still feel the need to control your own future? What would it take for you to fully surrender to the fixed term?

Quranic Proof Against Compulsory Belief
Nasafi uses Quran 32:13 to refute compulsory faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Quran 32:13 is used to refute the doctrine of compulsory faith and why Maturidi theology insists on voluntary belief.

Core Idea
God's will to fill Hell proves He does not compel guidance.

This lesson examines a crucial Quranic argument against the doctrine of jabr (compulsion). Imam al-Nasafi presents the verse from Surah al-Sajdah and unpacks its logical implications. The verse shows that God deliberately does not compel guidance in order to fulfill His promise to fill Hell with those who deserve it. This becomes a cornerstone for the Maturidi position on free will and responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its immediate meaning
Begin by reading the Arabic verse and its translation. Notice that God says He could give every soul guidance but refrains because His word is to fill Hell.
The verse is Quran 32:13.
2
Analyze the author's logical deduction
The author argues: if God compelled guidance, then everyone would be guided, but then Hell would not be filled since the guided are not punished. This contradicts God's declared word.
This is a reductio ad absurdum against jabr.
3
Distinguish between compelled and voluntary faith
Understanding that compelled faith (iman jabran) does not earn reward or remove punishment. God's intended faith is voluntary (ikhtiyari) which makes one deserving of Paradise.
This distinction is central to the argument.
4
Examine the refutation of the jabri interpretation
The author anticipates the objection that the verse might be about compelled faith. He shows that if it were, God would have already given it, yet disbelievers still exist, so the verse must refer to voluntary faith.
The author also notes that natural knowledge of God exists in all, but that is not saving faith.
5
Reflect on the hadith and conclusion
The hadith 'ma sha Allah kan' reinforces that God's will is effective. The passage concludes that the verse denies compulsion, affirming human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الذي يبطل جميع تأويلاتهم أن الله تعالى قال : { وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَآتَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَاهَا وَلَكِنْ حَقَّ الْقَوْلُ مِنِّي لَأَمْلَأَنَّ جَهَنَّمَ مِنَ الْجِنَّةِ وَالنَّاسِ أَجْمَعِينَ } أخبر أنه تعالى لم يأت كل نفس هداها لما أن حق القول منه لأملأن جهنم ولو أتى كل نفس هداها لم يتصور أن يملأ جهنم بهم لأن المهتدي لا يملأ به جهنم، وإعطاء الهدى بطريق الجبر على الطرق التي زعموا لا يخرجهم من استحقاقهم جهنم، وأن يملأ منهم جهنم، فدل أن هذا باطل. يحققه أن لو شاء إيمانهم بطريق الجبر على ما زعموا وحصل إيمانهم لما كان ذلك الإيمان الحاصل جبرًا هو الإيمان الذي شاء الله منهم؛ لأنه على زعمهم شاء منهم الإيمان الاختياري الذي يصيرون به مستحقين للجنة والثواب خارجين عن أن يكونوا أهلا للعقاب، وما يحصل من الإيمان بمشيئة الجبر لا يكون هذا الإيمان فإن العبد لا يصير به أهلاً للجنة والثواب ولا يخرج عن استحقاق العقاب على طريق التخليد، فإذا لم يبق قادرًا على تحصيل ما أراد في ملكه وغلبت مشيئته مشيئة إبليس وإرادة كل كافر، ولأنه لا معنى لتعلق الإيمان الحاصل جبرًا بالمشيئة والإخبار أنه لو شاء لفعل لأنه قد فعل ذلك وحصل من كل كافر إذ كل كافر وكل مخلوق يشهد بخلقه أن له صانعا حكيمًا عليمًا موصوفا بصفات الكمال متبرئًا عن سمات النقص لا يؤيد بالمعجزة الكاذب، ولا يقيم دلالة الصدق على دعوى المفتري، فكان على هذا كل مخلوق مؤمنًا بخلقته، وقد شاء الله تعالى ذلك وفعل لا معنى لقوله : { وَلَوْ شَاءَ رَبُّكَ لَآمَنَ مَن فِي الْأَرْضِ } وقوله : { وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَآتَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَاهَا } وقد فعل ذلك فدل أن المراد من الآية ليس هو الإيمان الحاصل جبرا بل إيمانهم الاختياري، وقد صح في المروي عن النبي عليه السلام أنه كان يقول : "ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن" وكذا هذه اللفظة متداولة على ألسنة
Then that which invalidates all their interpretations is that God Almighty said: {And if We had willed, We would have given every soul its guidance, but the word from Me has come true: I will surely fill Hell with jinn and people all together.} He informed that He did not give every soul its guidance because the word from Him was to fill Hell, and if He had given every soul its guidance, it would not be conceivable that He would fill Hell with them, because the guided one is not used to fill Hell. And giving guidance by way of compulsion according to the ways they claim does not remove them from deserving Hell, and that He fills Hell with them, so this indicates that this is false. He confirms it: that if He had willed their faith by way of compulsion as they claim, and their faith occurred, that faith obtained by compulsion would not be the faith that God wanted from them; because according to their claim, He wanted from them voluntary faith by which they become deserving of Paradise and reward, and are excluded from being deserving of punishment. And what is obtained from faith by the will of compulsion is not this faith, for the servant does not become thereby deserving of Paradise and reward, nor does he exit from deserving punishment in the way of eternal punishment. Thus, He is not able to achieve what He wanted in His kingdom, and His will is overcome by the will of Iblis and the desire of every disbeliever. And because there is no meaning to attaching faith obtained by compulsion to His will and the report that if He willed, He would do it, because He has already done that and it occurred from every disbeliever, since every disbeliever and every creature witnesses by his creation that he has a wise, knowing Creator described with attributes of perfection, free from marks of deficiency, who does not support the liar with miracles, and does not establish evidence of truth for the claim of the slanderer. Thus, on this basis, every creature is a believer by his creation, and God Almighty willed that and did it. So there is no meaning to His statement: {And if your Lord had willed, all on earth would have believed} and His statement: {And if We had willed, We would have given every soul its guidance}, and He did that. So it indicates that the intended meaning of the verse is not the faith obtained by compulsion, but their voluntary faith. And it is established in what is narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he used to say: "Whatever Allah wills happens, and whatever He does not will does not happen." And this phrase is common on the tongues...
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is a Quranic proof (istidlal) against the theory of compulsory faith (jabr). The author presents the verse from Surah As-Sajdah (32:13) which states that if God had willed, He could have given every soul guidance, but His word was to fill Hell. The author explains that if God had compelled guidance (hidayah) to all, then Hell would not be filled because the guided are not cast into Hell. Moreover, giving guidance by compulsion does not remove people from deserving Hell. Therefore, the verse proves that God's will is not for compelled faith but for voluntary faith (iman ikhtiyari) that merits reward. The author further argues that if God had willed compelled faith, it would have occurred, but the faith that occurs by compulsion is not the faith that makes one deserving of Paradise. Thus, God would be unable to achieve His will, and His will would be overcome by Iblis. The author also points out that every creature naturally has knowledge of God's existence, but that does not constitute saving faith. The hadith 'ma sha Allah kan' is cited to reinforce that God's will is effective. Therefore, the verses are not about compelled faith but about voluntary faith, which God did not compel.

Key Terms
الجبر
الإيمان الاختياري
الإيمان الحاصل جبرًا
مشيئة الله
الهدى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Quran 32:13 proves God could compel faith but chooses not to, implying He has the power to force belief.
Correction: The author shows that if God compelled faith, Hell would not be filled—contradicting His decree. Therefore, the verse actually proves that God does not compel faith, and that faith must be voluntary.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does God not compel guidance for all people?
A) Because He is unable to do so.
B) Because His word requires Hell to be filled with the deserving.
C) Because He only wills good for believers.
D) Because Iblis prevents it.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verse itself serves as evidence that God does not compel belief, because His decree to fill Hell would be impossible if He did.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'If We had willed, We would have given every soul its guidance', do you realize that your own faith is not forced? How does knowing that your belief is an act of your own choice affect your responsibility to seek guidance today?
?
If compelled faith does not save, then what does? Examine your own heart: Is your faith merely a product of your environment (a form of compulsion) or a genuine choice that makes you deserving of Paradise? What will you do to ensure your faith is voluntary?
?
The passage says every creature has natural knowledge of God, yet not all believe. Could it be that you have taken your existence and the signs around you for granted? In what specific area of your life are you ignoring the guidance that is already given, and what will you do to respond to it?

The Impossibility of Describing Allah with Contradictory Acts
First logical argument against the Mu'tazilite view of guidance and misguidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical inconsistency in the Mu'tazilite position on divine guidance and misguidance.

Core Idea
If Allah does not create guidance, then describing Him as guiding and misguiding becomes impossible.

The Mu'tazilites claimed that Allah does not create guidance or misguidance in the heart. The author of this passage shows that their view leads to a contradiction: if a disbeliever does not submit, Allah would have to make his chest narrow, but that would be describing Allah with an impossible act. Let's examine this argument closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening argument
Read the first part of the passage where the author describes the Mu'tazilite position and its implication. Notice the logical chain: if the disbeliever is not guided, then Allah must have made his chest narrow, but that is impossible.
2
Identify the two descriptions of Allah
The passage says Allah expands the chest of the guided and constricts the chest of the misguided. Recognize that both acts are attributed to Allah in the Quran, but the Mu'tazilite view denies one of them.
3
Understand the charge of impossibility
The author argues that denying that Allah creates misguidance leads to describing Allah with what is impossible. Why? Because if He does not create the constriction, then the constriction must come from elsewhere, contradicting divine omnipotence.
This is a key logical point in the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطريق لكل كافر فإذا لم يسلم يجده ضالاً ضالاً ويسميه فينبغي أن يجعل صدره ضيقًا حرجًا، فإذا كل كافر يشرح الله صدره لأنه هداه وضيق صدره لأنه أضله وفيه وصف الله تعالى لفعل ماهو محال، وكذا تقسيم الله تعالى الخلق قسمين: أحدهما شرح صدره، والآخر ضيق صدره باطل وهذا كله كفر، وتأويل الجبائي أنه هداية طريق الجنة في الآخرة باطل، لأنه تعالى قال وَلَكِنَّ اللَّهَ يَهْدِي مَن يَشَاءُ والله لا يهدي طريق الجنة من شاء بل من مات على إيمانه، ثم عندهم لا يجوز أن لا يدخل الجنة من مات على إيمان ولم يرتكب الكبائر أو تاب عنها بعدما ارتكب ولو لم يدخل لصار ظالمًا ولا يجوز له أن يدخل الجنة من كفر وارتكب كبيرة، ومات قبل التوبة عنها فأي مشيئة في ذلك الله تعالى يدل عليه أنه تعالى قال: وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَا نَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَنهَا ولا يجوز صرفه إلى هداية طريق الجنة وقال تعالى: فَلَوْ شَاءَ لَهَدَنَكُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ ولا يهدي جميع الخلق إلى الجنة بل لو فعل ذلك لكان عندهم سفيها وقال تعالى: يُضِلُّ مَن يَشَاءُ وَيَهْدِي مَن يَشَاءُ وهذا لا يتصور في هداية طريق الجنة
The path for every disbeliever: if he does not submit, He finds him misguided, misguided, and names him. So it is necessary that He makes his chest narrow and constrained. For every disbeliever, Allah expands his chest because He guided him, and constricts his chest because He led him astray. In this is describing Allah with what is impossible. Likewise, Allah's division of creation into two parts: one whose chest He expanded, and the other whose chest He constricted, is false. All of this is disbelief. The interpretation of al-Jubba'i that it is guidance to the path of Paradise in the Hereafter is false, because He said: 'But Allah guides whom He wills.' Allah does not guide to the path of Paradise whom He wills, but rather whoever dies in his faith. Then according to them, it is not permissible that he not enter Paradise if he died in faith and did not commit major sins or repented from them after committing them. If he did not enter, He would become an oppressor, and it is not permissible for him to enter Paradise if he disbelieved and committed a major sin and died before repenting from it. So what will is there in that? Allah indicates that He said: 'And if We willed, We would have given every soul its guidance.' It is not permissible to divert this to guidance to the path of Paradise. And He said: 'If He willed, He would have guided you all together.' And He does not guide all creatures to Paradise; rather if He did that, He would be foolish according to them. And He said: 'He leads astray whom He wills and guides whom He wills.' This is not conceivable in guidance to the path of Paradise.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazilite interpretation that Allah does not create guidance or misguidance in the hearts. The author first argues that if a disbeliever does not submit, Allah finds him misguided and names him, which would require making his chest constricted, but that is impossible because it would entail describing Allah with contradictory acts. Then he refutes al-Jubba'i's interpretation that guidance means showing the path to Paradise. He uses Quranic verses showing that guidance and misguidance are by Allah's will, and that if guidance meant showing the path, it would apply to all, but the verses indicate particularity.

Key Terms
هداية
إضلال
شرح الصدر
ضيق الصدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah does not create guidance or misguidance; He only shows the path.
Correction: The Quran describes Allah as expanding and constricting chests, which are acts of guidance and misguidance.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say that the Mu'tazilite view leads to describing Allah with what is impossible?
A) Because it denies Allah's power over guidance
B) Because it requires Allah to both guide and misguide simultaneously
C) Because it says Allah constricts the chest without creating the constriction
D) Because it limits guidance to the afterlife

Key Takeaway
Denying that Allah creates guidance and misguidance leads to describing Allah with impossible contradictions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your faith is a gift from Allah, or do you secretly think you earned it by your own efforts? What would it mean for your relationship with Him if you admitted you cannot guide yourself even one step?
?
When you see a person who is misguided, do you feel a sense of pride that you are not like them, forgetting that it is Allah who guided you? How would your view of them change if you believed that Allah creates their misguidance as a just act?
?
If Allah were to withdraw His guidance from your heart right now, could you bring it back by your own power? What does that realization demand of you today in terms of humility and reliance on Him?

Quranic Refutation of al-Jubba'i's Interpretation
Refutation of al-Jubba'i's interpretation using Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Quranic verses demonstrate that guidance and misguidance are acts of Allah, not merely showing the path to Paradise.

Core Idea
Quranic verses about guidance are particular, not general—showing the path would apply to all.

Al-Jubba'i, a leading Mu'tazilite, argued that 'guidance' in the Quran refers only to showing the path to Paradise in the Hereafter. The author refutes this by citing several verses that indicate guidance is specific and by Allah's will, not universal. Let's explore these verses and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the first verse and its refutation
The passage quotes 'But Allah guides whom He wills.' Note that the author argues this cannot mean showing the path because Allah does not show the path to everyone; only those who die in faith are guided to Paradise.
2
Consider the second verse
The verse 'And if We willed, We would have given every soul its guidance' is used to show that guidance is by divine will, not a mere invitation.
3
Examine the third and fourth verses
The verses 'If He willed, He would have guided you all together' and 'He leads astray whom He wills and guides whom He wills' further emphasize that guidance and misguidance are particular.
These verses contradict the Mu'tazilite view that guidance is general.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطريق لكل كافر فإذا لم يسلم يجده ضالاً ضالاً ويسميه فينبغي أن يجعل صدره ضيقًا حرجًا، فإذا كل كافر يشرح الله صدره لأنه هداه وضيق صدره لأنه أضله وفيه وصف الله تعالى لفعل ماهو محال، وكذا تقسيم الله تعالى الخلق قسمين: أحدهما شرح صدره، والآخر ضيق صدره باطل وهذا كله كفر، وتأويل الجبائي أنه هداية طريق الجنة في الآخرة باطل، لأنه تعالى قال وَلَكِنَّ اللَّهَ يَهْدِي مَن يَشَاءُ والله لا يهدي طريق الجنة من شاء بل من مات على إيمانه، ثم عندهم لا يجوز أن لا يدخل الجنة من مات على إيمان ولم يرتكب الكبائر أو تاب عنها بعدما ارتكب ولو لم يدخل لصار ظالمًا ولا يجوز له أن يدخل الجنة من كفر وارتكب كبيرة، ومات قبل التوبة عنها فأي مشيئة في ذلك الله تعالى يدل عليه أنه تعالى قال: وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَا نَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَنهَا ولا يجوز صرفه إلى هداية طريق الجنة وقال تعالى: فَلَوْ شَاءَ لَهَدَنَكُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ ولا يهدي جميع الخلق إلى الجنة بل لو فعل ذلك لكان عندهم سفيها وقال تعالى: يُضِلُّ مَن يَشَاءُ وَيَهْدِي مَن يَشَاءُ وهذا لا يتصور في هداية طريق الجنة
The path for every disbeliever: if he does not submit, He finds him misguided, misguided, and names him. So it is necessary that He makes his chest narrow and constrained. For every disbeliever, Allah expands his chest because He guided him, and constricts his chest because He led him astray. In this is describing Allah with what is impossible. Likewise, Allah's division of creation into two parts: one whose chest He expanded, and the other whose chest He constricted, is false. All of this is disbelief. The interpretation of al-Jubba'i that it is guidance to the path of Paradise in the Hereafter is false, because He said: 'But Allah guides whom He wills.' Allah does not guide to the path of Paradise whom He wills, but rather whoever dies in his faith. Then according to them, it is not permissible that he not enter Paradise if he died in faith and did not commit major sins or repented from them after committing them. If he did not enter, He would become an oppressor, and it is not permissible for him to enter Paradise if he disbelieved and committed a major sin and died before repenting from it. So what will is there in that? Allah indicates that He said: 'And if We willed, We would have given every soul its guidance.' It is not permissible to divert this to guidance to the path of Paradise. And He said: 'If He willed, He would have guided you all together.' And He does not guide all creatures to Paradise; rather if He did that, He would be foolish according to them. And He said: 'He leads astray whom He wills and guides whom He wills.' This is not conceivable in guidance to the path of Paradise.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazilite interpretation that Allah does not create guidance or misguidance in the hearts. The author first argues that if a disbeliever does not submit, Allah finds him misguided and names him, which would require making his chest constricted, but that is impossible because it would entail describing Allah with contradictory acts. Then he refutes al-Jubba'i's interpretation that guidance means showing the path to Paradise. He uses Quranic verses showing that guidance and misguidance are by Allah's will, and that if guidance meant showing the path, it would apply to all, but the verses indicate particularity.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Guidance in the Quran only means showing the path to Paradise, not creating belief.
Correction: The Quranic verses cited show that guidance is by will and is particular, not universal; it cannot be reduced to mere indication.

B) 'Allah is the Light of the heavens and the earth'

D) 'And We sent not any messenger except with the language of his people'

Key Takeaway
Quranic verses demonstrate that guidance and misguidance are acts of Allah by His will, not merely showing the path to Paradise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If guidance is solely by Allah's will, do you fear that you might be among those He leads astray? What steps are you taking to seek His guidance and avoid pride in your own religiosity?
?
When you share Islam with others, do you rely on your arguments or do you recognize that only Allah can guide? How does this lesson change your approach to dawah?

Quranic Proof for God's Power to Guide All
The author cites Quranic verses as proof for God's power to guide all.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'an argues for God's universal power to guide all people, and why this refutes opposing views.

Core Idea
If God claimed power He didn't have, the Qur'an would be deceptive — but it isn't.

This lesson introduces the Qur'anic evidence for the Ash'ari/Maturidi position that God has the power to guide all people if He wills. The author cites three clear verses and argues that denying this power would make the verses meaningless and even dishonest. We'll see how this argument addresses both the Mu'tazila and those who misinterpret the verses as referring to coercion.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the author's own words and the verses set the stage.
Notice the three Quranic verses cited: 32:13, 6:149, 10:99.
2
Identify the three verses
Locate each verse (indicated by verse numbers in parentheses) and note the common theme: God's will to guide everyone.
3
Understand the logical argument
The author makes a counterfactual argument: if God did not have the power to actually guide people, then these verses would be false boasts. Grasp why that would be problematic for God's truthfulness.
This is the core refutation of those who deny that God can guide all.
4
Note the refutation of 'jabr'
The author rejects the interpretation that the verses refer to coercive will (jabr) and says it was already refuted earlier.
This shows the author distinguishing his view from predestinarian extremes.
5
Connect to the broader proof set
The passage begins by listing four proofs: Quran, existence, consensus, reason. See how this Quranic proof fits into the overall argument for God's power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[دليل أهل الحق]: والدليل لأهل الحق في المسألة كتاب الله تعالى والوجود، وإجماع أهل الأديان والدليل العقلي. من الكتاب] أما الكتاب فقول الله تعالى: وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَآتَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَاهَا (٢) وقوله تعالى: فَلَوْ شَاءَ لَهَدَاكُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ (٣) وقوله تعالى ( وَلَوْ شَاءَ رَبُّكَ لَآمَنَ مَن فِي الْأَرْضِ كُلُّهُمْ جَمِيعًا (٤)، ولو لم يكن في مقدوره ما لو فعل بهم لأمنوا لم يكن لهذه الآيات فائدة سوی ادعاء قدرة ومشيئة ليستا له كفعل الكذوب المتصلف الذي يتحلى بما ليس فيه ما لا يحسن، وحملهم الآيات على مشيئة الجبر والقسر باطل على ما مر (٥).
The proof of the people of truth in this matter is the Book of Allah the Exalted, existence, the consensus of the religions, and rational proof. From the Book: Allah the Exalted says: 'And if We had willed, We would have given every soul its guidance' (32:13), and His saying: 'If He had willed, He would have guided you all' (6:149), and His saying: 'And if your Lord had willed, everyone on earth would have believed, all of them entirely' (10:99). And if it were not within His power that which if He had done to them they would have believed, then these verses would have no benefit except claiming a power and will that are not His, like the act of a lying pretender who adorns himself with what he does not have and does not do well. And their interpretation of the verses as meaning coercive will (mashi'at al-jabr) is false, as has preceded.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the proofs of the people of truth (Ahl al-Haqq): the Quran, existence, consensus of religions, and rational proof. It then focuses on the Quranic proof, citing three verses that declare God's will to guide all people if He so chose. The author argues that if God did not actually have this power, the verses would be meaningless—merely empty claims. This refutes the Mu'tazila who deny that God could guide everyone and still leave some misguided. The author also rejects the interpretation that these verses refer to a will of force (jabr), calling it false based on earlier arguments.

Misconception: Some think the verses only indicate a theoretical will, not that God actually has the power to guide all.
Correction: The author argues that denying actual power makes the verses deceptive; they must be taken as proof of real power.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'anic verses affirming God's will to guide all prove He has the power to do so, otherwise the verses would be deceptive.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God truly has the power to guide every soul, including those who reject Him, how does that change the way you view people who are far from faith? Are you willing to pray for their guidance with genuine hope, or do you secretly believe they are beyond reach?
?
The author compares claiming power without ability to a 'lying pretender'. In your own life, where do you claim spiritual power or commitment that you do not actually possess? Will you honestly examine one area today and either align your claim with action or drop the pretense?
?
If God's will to guide is not coercive, then your response to His guidance is your choice. When you read the Qur'an or hear truth, do you actively submit, or do you resist while attributing your resistance to 'God's will'? What will you do differently this week to take responsibility for your own guidance?
