The Rational Proof from Existence Against al-Aslah
A rational proof from the existence of evil against al-aslah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the existence of disbelief and sin in the world refutes the Mu'tazila doctrine that God must always do what is most beneficial for His servants.

Core Idea
The existence of harm for some servants proves that al-aslah is not obligatory upon God.

This lesson presents a rational argument that directly counters the Mu'tazila claim that God must always do what is most beneficial (al-aslah) for His servants. By examining the actual existence of disbelief and sin—which cause harm, not benefit—the argument shows that God's actions cannot be bound by such a requirement. The passage also uses specific examples to illustrate that what may appear harmful is actually part of God's greater wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Note the author's line of reasoning from the existence of disbelief and sin.
The passage is dense; read slowly to follow the logical flow.
2
Identify the main argument from existence
Find the core premise: disbelief and sin exist, they are created by God, they harm the servant, therefore they cannot be beneficial—let alone most beneficial.
This directly challenges the Mu'tazila obligation of al-aslah.
3
Examine the two examples
The author gives two concrete cases: a disbeliever kept alive with intellect knowing he will disbelieve, and a Muslim kept alive who later apostatizes. In both, dying earlier would have been more beneficial, yet God chooses otherwise.
These examples illustrate that God's wisdom may involve allowing harm.
4
Understand the conclusion on wisdom
The passage concludes that such actions are wise, and calling them foolish is disbelief. The Mu'tazila are ignorant of the true nature of wisdom.
Note the Quranic citation (3:178) supporting the idea that respite increases sin.
5
Reflect on the Mu'tazila error
Consider why the Mu'tazila fell into error: they limited divine wisdom to what benefits the servant, missing the broader purposes of God's actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل أهل الحق من الوجود] وأما الوجود فإن الكفر والمعاصي قد وجدت، وإنا أثبتنا بالدلائل السمعية (٦) والعقلية (۷) التي لا مدفع لها ولا اعتراض عليها ولا ريب فيها لمن أنصف من نفسه ولم يكابر عقله أن أفعال العباد مخلوقة الله ، وفيها الكفر والمعاصي، وهم يتضررون بها ولا ينتفعون فلم يكن إيجادها مصلحة لهم فضلاً عن الأصلح، وهذه المسألة في الحقيقة فرع لتلك المسألة، ثم ما هو أظهر من هذا وأدل أن الله تعالى فعل بالكافر ما لا صلاح له فيه بل له فيه مضرة ومفسدة، فإن الله تعالى أبقاه إلى وقت بلوغه وركب فيه العقل مع علمه أنه لا يؤمن بل يكفر ويعادي الله تعالى، ولا شك أن الله تعالى إذا علم أنه يكفر عند بلوغه واعتدال عقله لو أماته في حال صغره وعدم تمييزه أو لم يركب فيه العقل عند بلوغه حتى لو بلغ مجنونا غير مخاطب لكان ذلك أصلح له، وحيث لم يمته بل (1) أبقاه وركب فيه العقل والتمييز حتى دخل في حد التكليف والامتحان مع علمه أنه يكفر دل أنه لم (٢) يفعل به ما له فيه صلاح، وكذا من عاش مدة على الإسلام ثم ارتد بعد ذلك - نعوذ بالله - ولو كان الله تعالى قبض روحه وتوفاه قبل ارتداده بساعة حتى ختم له بالإسلام ولم يستحق التعذيب في النار خالدًا مخلدًا كان أصلح له، وحيث لم يفعل بل أبقاه مع علمه أنه يرتد عن الإسلام وكان ذلك مضرة له لا صلاحًا فقد فعل ذلك وهو تعالى حكيم، دل أن ذلك كان حكمة، ووقعت المعتزلة فيما وقعت لجهلهم بحقيقة الحكمة، ثم بعد تقرير فعل الله تعالى ذلك دعوى من زعم أن ذلك سفه وليس بحكمة وصف منه الله تعالى بذلك وهو كفر، بل ظهر بفعله أنه حكمة وإن جهلت المعتزلة بجهة الحكمة إذ الجهل عليهم جائز (۳) وخروج فعل الله تعالى عن الحكمة ممتنع. يحققه أن الله تعالى أضاف بقاءهم على الكفر إلى إبقائه وإمهاله بقوله تعالى إِنَّمَا نُمْلِي لَهُمْ لِيَزْدَادُوا إِثْمًا (٤). ثم من جهل المعتزلة أنهم يزعمون أن إبقاء الطفل إلى أن يبلغ ويتركب العقل فيه عند البلوغ مع علمه أنه يكفر أصلح له، وكذا إبقاء
The proof of the people of truth from existence: As for existence, disbelief and sins have occurred. We have proven by scriptural and rational proofs that are undeniable and beyond doubt for anyone who is fair to himself and does not argue with his intellect, that the actions of servants are created by Allah, and among them are disbelief and sins. And they are harmed by them and do not benefit. So their creation was not a benefit for them, let alone the most beneficial. This issue is in reality a branch of that one. Then what is more apparent and more indicative than this is that Allah the Exalted did to the disbeliever what has no benefit for him, but rather has harm and corruption. For Allah the Exalted kept him alive until the time of his maturity and placed intellect in him with the knowledge that he will not believe, but will disbelieve and be hostile to Allah the Exalted. There is no doubt that Allah the Exalted, when He knows that he will disbelieve upon reaching maturity and balance of intellect, if He had caused him to die in his childhood and lack of discernment, or had not placed intellect in him upon maturity so that he would remain insane and not addressed by the law, that would have been more beneficial for him. And since He did not cause him to die but kept him alive and placed intellect and discernment in him so that he entered the realm of obligation and trial with the knowledge that he would disbelieve, it indicates that He did not do for him what has benefit for him. Similarly, one who lived for a period in Islam and then apostatized—we seek refuge in Allah—if Allah the Exalted had taken his soul and caused him to die an hour before his apostasy so that he would end with Islam and not deserve torment in the fire eternally, that would have been more beneficial for him. And since He did not do that but kept him alive with the knowledge that he would apostatize from Islam, and that was harmful for him, not beneficial, He did that while He is the Wise. This indicates that this was wisdom, and the Mu'tazila fell into what they fell into due to their ignorance of the reality of wisdom. Then, after establishing that Allah the Exalted does that, the claim of one who says that this is foolishness and not wisdom, and describes Allah the Exalted with that, is disbelief. Rather, it is shown by His action that it is wisdom even if the Mu'tazila are ignorant of the aspect of wisdom, for ignorance is possible for them, and the departure of Allah's action from wisdom is impossible. Confirming it: Allah the Exalted attributed their persistence in disbelief to His giving respite and delay in His saying: 'We only give them respite so that they may increase in sin' (3:178). Then from the ignorance of the Mu'tazila is that they claim that keeping the child alive until he reaches maturity and placing intellect in him upon maturity with the knowledge that he will disbelieve is more beneficial for him, and similarly keeping the Muslim alive until he apostatizes is more beneficial?
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage presents a rational proof from existence against the Mu'tazila doctrine of al-aslah. The author begins by noting that disbelief and sin exist in the world, and since we have proven that all actions are created by God, and these actions harm the servants without benefiting them, they cannot be for their benefit—let alone the most beneficial. This is the key refutation. The author then provides a detailed example: God keeps the disbeliever alive and gives him intellect, knowing he will disbelieve and be punished. If God had let him die as a child, that would have been more beneficial for him. Since God does not do that, it shows that God is not bound to do what is most beneficial. A similar argument applies to a Muslim who apostatizes. The author emphasizes that such actions are wise, and calling them foolish is disbelief. The Mu'tazila are ignorant of the true nature of wisdom. Finally, the author cites Quran 3:178 to confirm that God's reprieve allows increase in sin, and criticizes the Mu'tazila for claiming that keeping the child alive is more beneficial, when in fact it leads to harm.

Key Terms
الوجود
المصلحة
الأصلح
الحكمة
المعتزلة
الكفر
المعاصي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God must always do what is most beneficial for each servant in this world or the next.
Correction: The existence of harm (disbelief, sin, punishment) shows that God's wisdom may involve allowing harm for greater purposes; al-aslah is not an obligation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does God's action of keeping the disbeliever alive and giving him intellect despite knowing he will disbelieve demonstrate?
A) That God is unjust
B) That God does not always do what is most beneficial for the servant
C) That God is compelled to create disbelief
D) That the disbeliever has free will to choose

Key Takeaway
The existence of harm in creation proves that God is not obligated to do what is most beneficial for His servants; His actions are always wise even if we do not understand the wisdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time when God allowed something harmful or difficult to happen to you, even though a more beneficial outcome seemed possible. How does this lesson challenge your natural desire to always receive what you think is best? Are you willing to trust that God's wisdom in that situation is greater than your own understanding? What practical step can you take today to surrender that area of your life to His wisdom?
?
The Mu'tazila claimed to know what is most beneficial for every person. In your heart, have you ever silently judged God's decisions for someone else—perhaps a loved one who persisted in sin or a non-believer you know? Where does that judgment come from, and how does this passage call you to repent and submit to God's hidden wisdom? Write down one specific person you have judged and resolve to leave their affair to God.
?
The passage mentions that calling God's actions 'foolish' is disbelief. Consider your own speech and thoughts: have you ever, even in frustration, implied that God should have done something differently? What does this reveal about your view of God's attributes? This week, commit to replacing that mindset with a declaration of God's perfect wisdom, especially in matters you do not understand.
